The Story of 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd and Rational Proof for Human Volition
Anecdote about 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd followed by a rational argument that human change demonstrates divine decree is not fatalistic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a historical anecdote and a rational argument together demonstrate that human change from one state to another is ultimately caused by divine decree, not by independent human will.

Core Idea
Human change from evil to good proves divine decree, not human free will alone.

This lesson begins with a famous story from the History of Baghdad involving 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd. A question about the Preserved Tablet leads to a deeper discussion about the relationship between divine decree and human action. The passage then presents a rational proof that our observed changes in human behavior must be attributed to God's preponderating will, not to human autonomy.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote carefully
Understand the interaction between the man and 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd. Notice the tension about the recitation of the Quran and the meaning of the verse.
The anecdote sets up the theological issue of fixed vs. conditional decree.
2
Identify the rational argument
The author argues that changes in human states (e.g., from disbelief to faith) are possible events that require a preponderator. Consider why an event without a preponderator would negate the Creator.
The argument uses the principle of causality in kalam.
3
Trace the preponderator logic
If the preponderator is from the servant, the question recurs; if from God, the conclusion is reached. See how this supports the idea that divine decree underlies all change.
This avoids infinite regress and affirms divine causation.
4
Connect to the hadith and analogy
Understand the metaphorical interpretation of 'the book precedes him' and the heart as a tablet with divine inscriptions.
The hadith is reinterpreted to mean God casts motivations into the heart.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكى الخطيب في تاريخ بغداد : أن رجلاً قال لعمرو بن عبيد : أخبرني عن ( ثبت ، هل كانت في اللوح المحفوظ ؟ فقال عمرو : ليس هكذا كانت . بل كانت : ( تبت يدا من عمل ، بمثل عمل أبي لهب ، فقال له الرجل : فهكذا ينبغي أن تقرأ ، إذا قمنا إلى الصلاة . فغضب عمرو . وقال له : اعلم أن الله ليس بشيطان ، إن علم الله لا يضر ولا ينفع . والجواب : أما أن خبر الواحد يقبل في هذه المسألة أم لا ؟ فقد تقدم القول فيه . ثم نقول : هذا خبر واحد ، تأكد مدلوله بالعقل . وذلك لأنا نرى أن الإنسان قد. يكون مواظباً على الكفر والفسق ، وأعمال أهل النار ، ثم إنه ينقلب مؤمناً بـراً ، وقد نرى الأمر على العكس منه . فانقلابه من الحالة المتقدمة إلى الحالة الأخرى المضادة لها . لا شك أنه من الجائزات الممكنات فإن وقع ذلك الممكن ، لا لمرجح ، لزم نفي الصانع ، وإن كان المرجح فذلك المرجح إن كان من العبد عاد السؤال فيه ، وإن كان من الله ، فقد حصل المطلوب . فثبت : أن هذا البرهان العقلي القاهر يدل على أن المواظب على أعمال أهل النار ، إنما ينقلب مؤمناً لأن القضاء الإلهي ، وجب قلبه من إحدى الحالتين إلى الأخرى. وهذا هو المراد من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « فيسبق عليه الكتاب ، فيعمل بعمل أهل الجنة ، والمراد من الكتاب : إلقاء داعية ذلك الفعل في قلبه . لأن قلب العبد يجري مجرى اللوح . وإلقاء تلك الدواعي المختلفة فيه ، يجري مجرى إلقاء الرقوم المختلفة ، والنقوش المتباينة في قلب العبد .
Al-Khatib narrated in the History of Baghdad that a man said to 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd: Inform me about 'tabat', was it in the Preserved Tablet? 'Amr said: It was not like that. Rather it was: 'May the hands of one who acts like the act of Abu Lahab perish.' So the man said to him: Then we should recite it like that when we stand for prayer. 'Amr became angry and said to him: Know that Allah is not a devil; the knowledge of Allah neither harms nor benefits. The answer: As for whether a solitary report is accepted in this matter or not, the discussion of that has preceded. Then we say: This is a solitary report, its meaning is confirmed by reason. That is because we see that a person may be constant upon disbelief and corruption and the works of the people of hellfire, then he turns into a pious believer, and we see the opposite of that. So his change from the previous state to the other opposite state is undoubtedly among permissible possibilities. If that possible event occurs without a preponderator, then the denial of the Maker necessarily follows; and if there is a preponderator, then if that preponderator is from the servant, the question returns upon it; and if it is from God, then what is sought is achieved. So it is established that this overwhelming rational proof indicates that the one constant upon the works of the people of hellfire only turns into a believer because the divine decree necessitates his turning from one state to the other. And this is the intended meaning of his statement, peace be upon him: 'Then the book precedes him, so he works with the work of the people of paradise.' And the intended meaning of 'the book' is the casting of the motivation for that action into his heart. For the heart of the servant functions like a tablet. And the casting of those various motivations into it is like the casting of various writings and different inscriptions into the heart of the servant.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage begins with an anecdote from the History of Baghdad: a man asks 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd about the verse 'تبت يدا أبي لهب' (May the hands of Abu Lahab perish) and whether it was written in the Preserved Tablet. 'Amr rephrases it to mean that the verse concerns one who acts like Abu Lahab, implying that it is not a fixed decree but conditional on action. The man sarcastically suggests this should be the recitation during prayer, angering 'Amr, who retorts that God is not a devil and His knowledge neither harms nor benefits. The author then provides the answer: the discussion of whether a solitary report is accepted in this matter has already been covered. Here, the hadith under discussion is a solitary report, but its meaning is confirmed by reason. The rational proof is that we observe people changing from persistent disbelief and evil to faith and righteousness, and vice versa. Such a change from one state to its opposite is undoubtedly a possible occurrence. If this possible event occurs without a preponderator (مرجح), that would negate the existence of the Creator (because a brute brute fact would imply no cause). If it occurs due to a preponderator, then if that preponderator comes from the servant, the same question would recur (why the servant chose that); if it comes from God, then the desired conclusion is reached (i.e., that God is the ultimate cause of the change). Thus, the rational proof establishes that a person's change from evil to good is due to divine decree necessitating that change. The hadith 'the book precedes him' is interpreted to mean that God casts the motivation (داعية) for the action into the heart, just as writings are placed on a tablet. The heart is like a tablet, and the various motivations are like different inscriptions.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد
البرهان العقلي
المرجح
الدواعي
اللوح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The anecdote shows that human will can overcome divine decree or that predestination is false.
Correction: The author uses the anecdote to introduce a rational proof that actually affirms divine decree as the ultimate cause of all change, not human free will alone.

Checkpoint
According to the rational proof, what follows if a possible change (like conversion) occurs without any preponderator?
A) It proves human free will.
B) It would entail the denial of the Creator.
C) It confirms the hadith is false.
D) It requires accepting the literal meaning of 'the book'.

Key Takeaway
The rational proof shows that human change from disbelief to faith is ultimately caused by God's decree, not by human will alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever experienced a sudden or gradual change from a state of disobedience to faith? According to this lesson, what was the ultimate cause of that change? How does that realization affect your gratitude to Allah, and what do you owe Him in return?
?
The rational proof shows that if you attribute your good deeds to your own will alone, you fall into infinite regress. Do you truly believe, in the depth of your heart, that every good thought and action comes from Allah? If so, why do you still feel pride in your achievements? What would it take for you to abandon that pride and attribute all success to Him?
?
When someone mocks or distorts theological truths, like the man in the story mocked 'Amr, how do you typically react? Are you more concerned with defending your own intellectual superiority or with humbly conveying the truth? What would change if you prioritized the latter, even when provoked?

intermediate

The Rational Proof for Divine Decree
Rational proof for divine decree using observation and causality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that a person's change from disbelief to faith is caused by God's decree, not by the servant's own choice.

Core Idea
Every change requires a cause; only God can be the ultimate cause of our spiritual transformation.

The author begins with a simple observation: people change from sin to righteousness and back. This change cannot happen without a preponderant cause. Why can't that cause be the servant himself? And why does this lead us to affirm divine decree? In this lesson, we follow the rational argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Observe the change in people's states
Read the opening where the author notes that people can be persistent in disbelief and then become righteous. Reflect on your own observations: have you seen such changes?
This sets up the empirical starting point.
2
Recognize the need for a preponderant
The author argues that every change from one state to another requires a preponderant (murajjih). Without it, we could allow anything to happen without cause, which is absurd.
Think about why randomness is not a sufficient explanation.
3
Eliminate the servant as the cause
If the preponderant came from the servant, the question would recur (who caused the servant to choose that?). This leads to an infinite regress.
The author says 'the problem returns'.
4
Affirm God as the cause
Therefore, the preponderant must be from God. This establishes that divine decree turns the person from one state to another, as the hadith says.
Connect to the hadith quote.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالعقل . وذلك لأنا نرى أن الإنسان قد يكون مواظباً على الكفر والفسق ، وعلى أعمال أهل النار ، ثم ينقلب مؤمناً بـرا تقياً . وقد نرى الأمر على العكس من ذلك . فانقلابه من الحالة المتقدمة ، إلى الحالة المتأخرة ، لا بد وأن يكون المرجح . إذ لو جاز حصول الرجحان ، لا لمرجح ، فلنجوز ذلك في كل الممكنات . ثم ذلك المرجح إن كان من العبد ، عاد الطلب . وإن كان من الله ، فقد حصل المطلوب فثبت : أن هذا البرهان العقلي يدل على أن المواظب على أعمال أهل النار، إنما ينقلب مواظباً على أعمال أهل الجنة. لأن القضاء الإلهي ، اقتضى ذلك ، وقلبه من أحد الجانبين إلى الجانب الآخر . وهذا هو المراد من قوله : «فيسبق عليه الكتاب ، فيعمل بعمل أهل الجنة ) . قوله : « هذا الحديث لا يدل إلا على أن أفعال العباد ، لا تقع إلا على وفق علم الله ، قلنا : هب أنه كذلك . إلا أنا بينا أن خلاف المعلوم ممتنع الوقوع . أما قوله : ( حكم الله في أفعال العباد، مشروط ، لا جازم ، قلنا : لا نزاع أن الله تعالى يعلم أن « زيداً ، لو أطاع فإنه يثاب . ولكن هل حصل مع هذه القضية الشرطية ، علم بأنه يطيع أم لا ؟ فإن لم يحصل العلم ، لا بالوقوع ، ولا بعدم الوقوع، كان تعالى غير عالم بالجزئيات . وهو كفر . وإن علم الوقوع ، أو اللاوقوع ، وجب أن لا يكون خلافه ، ممتنع الوقوع . وحينئذ يعود الإلزام المذكور . والله أعلم
By reason. And that is because we see that a person may be persistent upon disbelief and sin, and upon the deeds of the people of the Fire, then he turns into a believing, righteous, pious person. And we see the opposite of that. So his turning from the former state to the latter state must have a preponderant (al-murajjih). For if it were permissible for preponderance (al-rujhān) to occur without a preponderant, then we would allow that in all possibles (al-mumkināt). Then if that preponderant is from the servant, the problem returns; but if it is from God, then the desired is achieved. So it is established that this rational proof indicates that one who persists in the deeds of the people of the Fire turns to persisting in the deeds of the people of Paradise, because the divine decree (al-qaḍā' al-ilāhī) necessitated that and turned him from one side to the other. And this is the meaning of his saying: 'So the Book preceded over him, and he does the deeds of the people of Paradise.' His statement: 'This hadith only indicates that the actions of servants occur only in accordance with God's knowledge,' we say: Granted that it is so. But we have shown that contradiction of what is known (khilāf al-ma'lūm) is impossible of occurrence. As for his statement: 'God's judgment concerning the actions of servants is conditional, not absolute,' we say: There is no dispute that God Almighty knows that 'Zayd, if he obeys, then he will be rewarded. But is there, along with this conditional proposition, knowledge that he will obey or not? If there is no knowledge, neither of occurrence nor of non-occurrence, then He would not be knower of particulars, and that is disbelief. And if He knows occurrence or non-occurrence, then it follows that its contrary is impossible of occurrence. And then the aforementioned binding argument returns. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents a rational proof for divine decree and then responds to an objection. The author begins by stating a rational observation: we see people change from persistent disbelief to faith, and vice versa. This change requires a preponderant cause (murajjih). If change could happen without a cause, then anything could happen without cause, which is absurd. The cause cannot be the servant because that would lead to a regress (the problem returns); therefore, the cause must be God. This rational proof establishes that God's decree turns a person from one state to another, as the hadith says 'the Book precedes.' Then an opponent objects: the hadith only shows actions accord with God's knowledge, not that they are necessitated. The author answers: Even if that were so, we have already shown that the opposite of what God knows is impossible. The opponent then says that God's judgment is conditional (e.g., if a person obeys, he will be rewarded), not absolute. The author responds: If God only knows conditionally, then He does not know whether the condition will occur, which would mean He does not know particulars—that is disbelief. If He does know, then the opposite is impossible, so the original point stands.

Key Terms
المرجح
القضاء الإلهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that a person's change of heart is self-caused or purely random.
Correction: No change occurs without a cause; the ultimate cause is God's decree.

Checkpoint
According to the rational proof, why can't the preponderant be from the servant?
A) Because the servant cannot cause his own actions.
B) Because it would lead to an infinite regress.
C) Because God has decreed it directly.
D) Because the hadith says so.

Key Takeaway
The rational argument shows that God's decree is the necessary cause of every spiritual transformation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever attributed your own faith or repentance solely to your own effort, forgetting that without God's turning of your heart you would remain in your previous state? What does that reveal about your reliance on His decree?
?
When you see someone who was once persistent in sin suddenly become righteous, do you credit their free will or recognize God's hand in the transformation? How does your answer affect your gratitude to Him?
?
If you truly believe that every spiritual change is caused by God's decree, how does that reshape your prayer life? Do you ask Him sincerely to turn your heart, or do you rely on your own resolve?

Refuting the Objection of Conditional Knowledge
Response to objections about conditional knowledge and God's knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's knowledge must be decisive and not merely conditional, and how this supports the proof for divine decree.

Core Idea
God's knowledge is absolute; conditional knowledge without actual outcome would imply ignorance.

The opponent raises two objections: the hadith only shows actions accord with God's knowledge, and God's judgment is conditional. The author responds by first granting the first objection but showing that the opposite of what God knows is impossible. Then he tackles the second objection by asking whether God knows the outcome of the condition. If He does, then the opposite is impossible; if He does not, then He is not all-knowing. This powerful response closes the door on the objection.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first objection
The opponent says the hadith only shows actions occur according to God's knowledge, not that they are necessitated. The author grants this but points out that we have already shown that contradicting what God knows is impossible.
The author refers back to the earlier rational proof.
2
Examine the second objection about conditional knowledge
The opponent claims God's judgment is conditional (e.g., if Zayd obeys, he will be rewarded). The author asks: does God know whether Zayd will obey or not?
This is the key question.
3
Consider the two possibilities
If God does not know whether the event occurs, then He is not all-knowing—this is disbelief. If He does know, then the opposite is impossible, so the original argument stands.
Either way, the objection fails.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's conditional knowledge (e.g., 'if Zayd obeys, he will be rewarded') implies that God does not know the actual outcome.
Correction: God either knows the actual outcome (so it's fixed) or He doesn't (impossible). Conditional knowledge without actual knowledge would be ignorance.

Checkpoint
What does the author argue would happen if God only had conditional knowledge without knowing the actual occurrence?
A) God would still be all-knowing.
B) God would not be all-knowing, which is disbelief.
C) The conditional would be sufficient.
D) The original argument would be invalid.

Key Takeaway
The opponent's claim of conditional knowledge fails because it either denies God's omniscience or reaffirms the impossibility of changing what God knows.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that God knows every detail of your life before it happens, why do you still hesitate to surrender fully to His decree? What area of your life do you still treat as if God’s judgment is conditional—waiting for the outcome before you trust Him?
?
The passage argues that if God does not know whether you will obey or not, He would not be knower of particulars. Have you ever acted as if your sins are hidden from God’s knowledge? How does this passage force you to reconsider that assumption?
?
When you face a choice between obedience and sin, do you rely on the thought that God might not have decreed that specific moment? How does the impossibility of contradicting God's known decree change the weight of your decision right now?

The Hadith of the Funeral: Decree and Human Action
The author cites the hadith about the funeral and explains that combined capacity and motivation cause action, addressing the objection about reliance on decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of the funeral supports the Ash'ari position that action results from the combination of capacity (qudwa) and motivation (dā'ī), and why reliance on divine decree is invalid.

Core Idea
Fate is not a free pass; God creates motivations that lead to actions.

The fourth proof is a famous hadith where the Prophet directly addresses the fatalist objection. A companion asks if they can stop working because destinies are written. The Prophet's answer and the author's commentary reveal a key principle: divine decree works through causes, and the 'facilitation' (taysīr) is God's creation of motivation. This lesson unpacks that principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and the question it provokes
Start by reading the hadith narrative: the Prophet declares that every soul's place in Paradise or Hell is written. Notice the immediate objection: 'Shall we rely on our book and abandon work?' This sets up the core tension.
2
Examine the Prophet's answer
The Prophet replies: 'Work, for everyone is made easy.' He then recites verses from Surah al-Layl. Reflect on how this answer neither denies predestination nor endorses fatalism.
The word 'taysīr' (facilitation) appears here – it means God creates the motivation for the appropriate action.
3
Understand the author's explanation
The author argues that the hadith explicitly supports his view: the combination of capacity (sound limbs) and motivation necessitates the action. Without motivation, action does not occur. This explains why we cannot rely on the prior book – the effect (reward or punishment) depends on the action, which depends on the motivation.
Capacity is neutral; motivation determines direction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : ما رواه الشيخان في الصحيحين بإسناديهما ، عن أبي عبد الرحمن السلمي ، عن علي بن أبي طالب . قال : خرجنا على جنازة . فبينا نحن بالبقيع . إذ خرج علينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وبيده مخصرة فجاء ، فجلس ، ثم نكت بها في الأرض ساعة ، ثم قال : ( ما من نفس منفوسة ، إلا وقد كتب مكانها من الجنة أو النار . وإلا قد كتبت شقية أو سعيدة ، فقال رجل : أفلا نتكل على كتابنا يا رسول الله ، وندع العمل ؟ قال : ولا . ولكن اعملوا ، فكل ميسر . أما أهل الشقاء فييرون لعمل أهل الشقاء ، وأما أهل السعادة فيسرون لعمل أهل السعادة ، قال : ( ثم تلا هذه الآية : ( فأما من أعطى واتقي ، وصدق بالحسنى ، فسنيسره لليسرى . وأما من بخل واستغنى ، وكذب بالحسنى ، فسنيره للعسرى (١) ) والاستدلال بهذا الحديث ، كما تقدم تقريره في الحديث الثالث واعلم : أن هذا الحديث تصريح بما اخترناه من أن مجموع القدوة والداعي ، يوجب الفعل وذلك لأن صلاحية الآلة وسلامة الأعضاء ، حاصل بالنسبة إلى الطاعة والمعصية ، وإلى اليسرى والعسرى . إلا أنه إن حصلت داعية الطاعة ، فذاك هو التيسير لليسرى . وإن حصلت داعية المعصية . فذاك هو التيسير للعسرى . وأما قول السائل : أفلا نتكل على الكتاب السابق ؟ فلا جواب عنه إلا ما ذكره سيد البشر عليه السلام. وذلك لأن حصول اليسري تارة ، والعسرى أخرى ، إنما كان بواسطة هذه الدواعي والبواعث. فأهل الشقاوة هم الذين تيسرت لهم دواعي الفساد، وأهل السعادة هم الذين تيسرت لهم دواعي الطاعات . فإن الداعية توجب الفعل ، وحصول الفعل يوجب الأثر في الدار الآخرة . وكيف يقال : إنا نترك الفعل ، ونجد أثر ذلك الفعل ؟
The fourth proof: What al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated in the two Sahihs with their chains from Abu 'Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib. He said: We went out for a funeral. While we were at al-Baqi', the Messenger of God (peace and blessings be upon him) came out to us with a stick in his hand. He came, sat down, and poked the ground with it for a while, then said: 'There is no soul that has been breathed into existence except that its place in Paradise or Hell has been written, and except that it has been written as wretched or blessed.' A man said: 'Shall we then rely on our book and abandon work, O Messenger of God?' He said: 'No. But work, for everyone is made easy. As for the people of wretchedness, they are made easy for the deeds of the people of wretchedness; and as for the people of happiness, they are made easy for the deeds of the people of happiness.' Then he recited this verse: 'As for he who gives and fears God, and believes in the best [reward], We will ease him toward ease. But as for he who is stingy and considers himself self-sufficient, and denies the best [reward], We will ease him toward hardship.' [Al-Layl 92:5-10] And the derivation of evidence from this hadith is as was previously explained in the third hadith. And know that this hadith explicitly states what we have chosen: that the combination of capacity (al-qudwa) and motivation (al-dā'ī) necessitates the action. That is because the suitability of the instrument and soundness of the limbs are present with respect to both obedience and disobedience, and with respect to ease and hardship. However, if the motivation for obedience arises, that is the facilitation (al-taysīr) toward ease; and if the motivation for disobedience arises, that is the facilitation toward hardship. As for the questioner's statement: 'Shall we rely on the prior book?' There is no answer to it except what the master of humanity (peace be upon him) mentioned. That is because the attainment of ease at one time and hardship at another is only through these motivations and incentives. So the people of wretchedness are those for whom the motivations for corruption are made easy, and the people of happiness are those for whom the motivations for obedience are made easy. For the motivation necessitates the action, and the occurrence of the action necessitates the effect in the Hereafter. How can it be said: 'We abandon the action and find the effect of that action?'
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof, which is a hadith from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib about the funeral at al-Baqi'. The hadith states that every person's fate (Paradise or Hell) is written, and they are made easy for corresponding deeds. When a man asked whether they should rely on this decree and stop working, the Prophet replied no, but rather to work because each is made easy. The author then explains the hadith: it explicitly supports his position that the combination of capacity (qudwa, meaning the soundness of the limbs and instruments) and motivation (dā'ī) necessitates the action. Both obedience and disobedience are possible with the same capacity; what determines the action is the motivation that God creates. This is the 'facilitation' (taysīr). Then he addresses the objection: why not rely on the prior decree? The answer is given by the Prophet: the attainment of ease or hardship is only through these motivations. The motivation necessitates the action, and the action determines the outcome in the Hereafter. One cannot expect the effect without the cause.

Key Terms
التيسير
الداعية
مجموع القدوة والداعي
الكتاب السابق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Belief in divine decree means we can stop working because our fate is already written.
Correction: The Prophet explicitly rejected this; decree is realized through motivations that cause actions, so work is necessary.

Checkpoint
According to the author's explanation of the hadith, what does 'facilitation toward ease' (al-taysīr li-l-yusrā) mean?
A) God directly forces the person to do good deeds.
B) God creates the motivation for obedience in the person.
C) The person is given more physical strength.
D) The person is predestined to enter Paradise regardless of actions.

Key Takeaway
God's decree of ease or hardship is the creation of motivations that lead to actions; thus, reliance on decree without action is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel spiritually lazy, have you ever caught yourself thinking 'it's already written' to avoid the effort? What motivation has God already placed in your heart today that you are ignoring?
?
If God creates your motivations, then what steps are you actively taking to seek motivations for obedience—like sitting with the righteous, reading His book, or reflecting on His signs—knowing that He may grant them?
?
The Prophet commanded 'Work, for each is made easy' despite the writing of fate. In what specific area of your life are you waiting for God to 'make it easy' without putting in the work yourself, and what is holding you back from starting that work now?

The Hadith of Everything by Decree
The author presents the hadith and rational proof that all things are decreed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith 'everything is by decree' and the rational principle of contingency together demonstrate that all things, including human abilities, are determined by God.

Core Idea
Everything other than God is possible and dependent — that is why everything is by decree.

The fifth argument combines a prophetic hadith with a rational principle. The hadith explicitly states that even ability and inability are decreed. But how do we know this rationally? The answer lies in the nature of everything other than God: it is possible (contingent) and therefore in need of a determiner. This passage unpacks that connection.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and note its scope
Read the Arabic hadith carefully. Notice that it includes 'even inability and ability' — showing that no human attribute is outside divine decree.
The term 'الكيس' refers to ability or intelligence, opposite of 'العجز'.
2
Understand the rational formulation
The author states: 'Everything other than God is possible, and every possible is in need.' Grasp that 'possible' means contingent (could exist or not), and 'in need' means requires a cause to exist.
3
Connect the rational principle to the hadith
The hadith's decree is the rational determination of contingents. The rational proof shows why the hadith is necessarily true: because all contingent things necessitate a determiner, which is God's decree.
4
Recognize the scope of the decree
The passage concludes that the decree includes 'actions, words, states, and morals.' Reflect on how this encompasses all human affairs.
This counters the idea that only major events are decreed.

Source Text

الحجة الخامسة : ما رواه مسلم في صحيحه بإسناده عن طاووس اليماني ، أنه قال : أدركت ناساً من أصحاب رسول الله عليه السلام ، يقولون : كل شيء بقدر الله ، وسمعت عبد الله بن عمرو ، يقول : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : كل شيء بقدر ، حتى العجز والكيس ، والاستدلال بالخبر : ظاهر. وتقريره من حيث العقل : إن كل ما سوى الله ممكن ، وكل ممكن محتاج . وذلك يدخل فيه الأفعل والأقوال والأحوال والأخلاق
The fifth proof: What Muslim narrated in his Sahih with his chain from Tawus al-Yamani that he said: I encountered some of the companions of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) saying: Everything is by God's decree. And I heard 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr saying: The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: Everything is by decree, even inability and ability. And deriving evidence from the report is apparent. And its rational formulation: Everything other than God is possible (mumkin), and every possible is in need (muḥtāj). And that includes actions, words, states, and morals.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof, consisting of a hadith narrated by Muslim from Tawus al-Yamani, quoting 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr that the Prophet said: 'Everything is by decree, even inability and ability.' The author states that the derivation of evidence from this report is apparent. Then he provides a rational formulation: everything other than God is possible (mumkin), meaning it is contingent and not necessary in itself. Every possible entity is in need (muḥtāj) of a cause or determiner to bring it into existence. This includes all actions, words, states (aḥwāl), and morals (akhlāq). Thus, all human acts are decreed by God.

الممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think divine decree only applies to major events, not to personal abilities or everyday actions.
Correction: The hadith explicitly includes 'inability and ability,' and the rational proof shows that all contingent things, including all human capacities and deeds, are in need of a determiner — thus everything is by decree.

Checkpoint

D) Actions, words, states, and morals are all created by God.

Key Takeaway
The hadith and rational proof together establish that everything other than God, including all human capacities and actions, is decreed by God.

?
If everything is by decree, what is your heart actually attached to? Your plans, your health, your relationships – are you trusting in your own ability to manage them, or in the One who decrees all? What is one thing you need to hand over to Him right now?

The Hadith of 'Each is Made Easy' and the Refutation of Fatalism
Author explains hadith and answers fatalist objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of taysir supports the Ash'ari position that acts are caused by the combination of capability and motive, not by blind fate.

Core Idea
Divine facilitation works through motives, not against them.

This lesson unpacks a key hadith often cited in debates about predestination. The author shows that the Prophet's words 'each is made easy' actually affirm human responsibility while upholding divine decree. You will see how capability and motive together produce action, and why relying on the prior decree without acting is incoherent.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its proof text
Read the hadith quote and the accompanying verse from Surah al-Layl. Notice how the Prophet links divine facilitation to human traits: giving, fearing, believing lead to ease; withholding, self-sufficiency, denial lead to hardship.
The verse is a key scriptural support for the hadith.
2
Understand the author's interpretation
The author states that the hadith explicitly supports the Ash'ari view: the conjunction of capability (qudra) and motive (daa'iy) causes the act. Reflect on why both are necessary.
3
Examine the objection and answer
The question 'Shall we not rely on the prior decree?' is answered by pointing to the causal chain: motives lead to acts, which produce effects. One cannot expect the reward or punishment without performing the act.
This refutes fatalism while preserving divine decree.
4
Connect to the broader lesson
Consider how this passage resolves the tension between divine predestination and human responsibility. The author shows that the decree itself operates through secondary causes like motives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكل ميسر . أما أهل الشقاء فييرون لعمل أهل الشقاء ، وأما أهل السعادة فيسرون لعمل أهل السعادة ، قال : ( ثم تلا هذه الآية : ( فأما من أعطى واتقي ، وصدق بالحسنى ، فسنيسره لليسرى . وأما من بخل واستغنى ، وكذب بالحسنى ، فسنيره للعسرى (١) ) والاستدلال بهذا الحديث ، كما تقدم تقريره في الحديث الثالث واعلم : أن هذا الحديث تصريح بما اخترناه من أن مجموع القدوة والداعي ، يوجب الفعل وذلك لأن صلاحية الآلة وسلامة الأعضاء ، حاصل بالنسبة إلى الطاعة والمعصية ، وإلى اليسرى والعسرى . إلا أنه إن حصلت داعية الطاعة ، فذاك هو التيسير لليسرى . وإن حصلت داعية المعصية . فذاك هو التيسير للعسرى . وأما قول السائل : أفلا نتكل على الكتاب السابق ؟ فلا جواب عنه إلا ما ذكره سيد البشر عليه السلام. وذلك لأن حصول اليسرى تارة ، والعسرى أخرى ، إنما كان بواسطة هذه الدواعي والبواعث. فأهل الشقاوة هم الذين تيسرت لهم دواعي الفساد، وأهل السعادة هم الذين تيسرت لهم دواعي الطاعات . فإن الداعية توجب الفعل ، وحصول الفعل يوجب الأثر في الدار الآخرة . وكيف يقال : إنا نترك الفعل ، ونجد أثر ذلك الفعل ؟
And each is made easy. As for the people of misery, they are made easy for the work of the people of misery, and as for the people of happiness, they are made easy for the work of the people of happiness. He said: Then he recited this verse: 'As for he who gives and fears Allah and believes in the best, We will ease him toward ease. And as for he who withholds and considers himself self-sufficient and denies the best, We will ease him toward hardship.' And the inference from this hadith is as previously established in the third hadith. And know: that this hadith explicitly states what we have chosen: that the combination of capability (qudra) and motive (daa'iy) causes the act. This is because the suitability of the instrument and the soundness of the limbs are present in relation to obedience and disobedience, and to ease and hardship. Except that if the motive for obedience occurs, that is the facilitation towards ease. And if the motive for disobedience occurs, that is the facilitation towards hardship. As for the statement of the questioner: 'Shall we not rely on the prior decree?' There is no answer to it except what the master of mankind (peace be upon him) mentioned. That is because the attainment of ease at one time and hardship at another was only through these motives and impulses. So the people of misery are those for whom the motives for corruption are made easy, and the people of happiness are those for whom the motives for obedience are made easy. For the motive causes the act, and the occurrence of the act causes the effect in the Hereafter. And how can it be said: We abandon the act and yet find the effect of that act?
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage presents and explains a hadith about divine facilitation (taysir) and defends the Ash'ari position that acts are caused by a combination of capability and motive, rejecting fatalism. The author first quotes the hadith that each person is made easy for their destined path, citing the verse from Surah al-Layl. He then states that this hadith supports the chosen position: the conjunction of qudra (capability) and daa'iy (motive) necessarily produces the act. The physical capacity is neutral, but when a motive arises, it leads to either ease or hardship. Next, he addresses an objection: why not simply rely on the prior decree and not act? The answer is that the decree itself works through motives; motives cause the act, and the act determines the outcome in the Hereafter. Therefore, one cannot expect the result without performing the action. The argument is sequential: first the hadith, then its interpretation, then the objection and answer.

Key Terms
القدرة
الداعي
التيسير
الكتاب السابق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think the hadith of taysir means that one's actions are entirely predetermined, so effort is futile.
Correction: The author shows that the hadith actually teaches that divine facilitation works through motives. One's choices and motives are part of the decree, and actions lead to results. Relying on the decree while abandoning action is illogical.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what causes the act?
A) The prior decree alone
B) The combination of capability and motive
C) Random chance
D) The act of the soul alone

Key Takeaway
Divine facilitation does not negate human responsibility; it operates through the motives that lead to actions, and actions determine one's ultimate outcome.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about a time you used the excuse 'It was written' to avoid taking responsibility for a wrong action or a missed opportunity. How does this lesson's explanation that the decree works through motives challenge you to own your choices today? What specific step will you take to align your motives with what pleases Allah?
?
The passage says that the motive causes the act, and the act causes the effect in the Hereafter. Look at your daily routine: what motives are driving your actions—fear of people, desire for comfort, or sincere love for Allah? Be honest: is your life being eased towards 'yusrā' or 'ʿusrā'? What one change in your intention could shift that direction?
?
If you truly believe that Allah facilitates ease for those who give, fear Him, and believe in the best, why do you still hesitate to give generously, fear Him consistently, or trust in His promise? What lie from your own heart or from Shaytan are you believing that stops you from embracing this facilitation? Make a concrete commitment to act on one of these three qualities today.

The Fifth Proof: Everything is by Decree, Even Ability and Inability
The author cites a hadith from Muslim as proof for universal divine decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fifth proof from hadith establishes that all human capacities and incapacities are decreed by Allah.

Core Idea
Hadith confirms decree includes all, even ability and inability.

The author now presents a proof from the Sunnah, citing a well-known hadith from Muslim. This hadith explicitly extends divine decree to encompass not just major events but also the very capacities and incapacities of human beings. The passage then adds a rational foundation for why this must be so.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its chain
Start by reading the hadith carefully, noting its chain from Tawus al-Yamani and Abdullah ibn Amr.
The chain indicates the hadith's authenticity.
2
Understand the rational exposition
After the hadith, the author provides a rational argument: everything besides Allah is possible (mumkin) and every possible is in need (muhtaj). Reflect on how this applies to all human attributes.
This rational layer supports the textual proof.
3
Reflect on the scope of decree
Consider what 'even incapacity and intelligence' means for human free will and responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : ما رواه مسلم في صحيحه بإسناده عن طاووس اليماني ، أنه قال : أدركت ناساً من أصحاب رسول الله عليه السلام ، يقولون : كل شيء بقدر الله ، وسمعت عبد الله بن عمرو ، يقول : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : كل شيء بقدر ، حتى العجز والكيس ، والاستدلال بالخبر : ظاهر. وتقريره من حيث العقل : إن كل ما سوى الله ممكن ، وكل ممكن محتاج . وذلك يدخل فيه الأفعل والأقوال والأحوال والأخلاق
The fifth proof: What Muslim transmitted in his Sahih with his chain from Tawus al-Yamani that he said: I encountered people from the companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saying: Everything is by the decree of Allah. And I heard Abdullah ibn Amr say: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Everything is by decree, even incapacity and intelligence. And the inference from the report is clear. And its rational exposition: Everything other than Allah is possible, and every possible is in need. And that includes actions, words, states, and moral qualities.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof from hadith for divine predestination. The author cites a hadith from Muslim where Abdullah ibn Amr reports the Prophet saying that everything is by decree, including 'al-ajz' (incapacity) and 'al-kais' (intelligence/ability). The author then notes that the inference from this report is apparent. He provides a rational exposition: everything other than Allah is possible (mumkin), and every possible being is in need (muhtaj) of an external cause. This neediness applies to all human actions, words, states, and moral qualities, implying they are all decreed by Allah. The proof combines textual and rational arguments: the hadith directly asserts universal decree, and the philosophical principle that all contingent things require a cause supports it.

The Hadith of Suraqa: Predestination and Action
The hadith of Suraqa and the companions' dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the apparent tension between divine decree and human action as presented in the hadith of Suraqa, and how the Prophet's response points to a deeper harmony.

Core Idea
The pen has dried, yet we are commanded to act.

In this lesson, we begin with the famous hadith where Suraqa asks whether our actions are already decreed or freely chosen. The Prophet's reply—'The pens have dried' combined with 'Work, for each is made easy'—sets up a theological puzzle. This passage invites us to hold together both divine predestination and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Suraqa frames the question: 'Is action based on what the pens have dried from, or something we initiate?'
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim.
2
Identify the two key statements of the Prophet
The Prophet first says action is based on what the pens have dried, then commands 'Work, for each is made easy.' Reflect on how these two statements relate.
The command to act shows that decree does not negate effort.
3
Understand the companions' dispute
The Sharh al-Sunnah mentions a dispute among companions about the meaning of 'each is made easy.' This shows that even the early Muslims debated how to reconcile decree and action.
Abu Dharr's view is referenced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : ما رواه مسلم في صحيحه ، بإسناده عن جابر ، قال : جاء سراقة بن مالك بن جعشم ، فقال : يا رسول الله بين لنا ديننا ، كأنا خلقنا الآن . قيم العمل اليوم ؟ فيها جفت به الأقلام ، وجرت به المقادير ؟ أو فيها نستقبل ؟ قال عليه السلام : ( بل فيها جفت به الأقلام ، وجرت به المقادير ؟ قال : فقيم العمل ؟ قال : ( اعملوا : فإن كلا ميسره. قال صاحب شرح السنة ، بعد ما روى هذا الخبر : ( وصح عن أبي هريرة ، عن رسول الله عليه السلام أنه قال : « يا أبا هريرة جف القلم بما أنت لاق . . فاختصمه على ذلك، أبو ذره قالوا : المراد من قوله : «الأمر قد فرغ منه هو الكتابة في اللوح المحفوظ ، والإخبار عن كونه شقياً أو سعيداً . قالوا : والدليل على أن المراد ما ذكر نام : أنه عليه السلام بين أن تلك الكتابة غير موجبة لشقاوة العبد ولسعادته ، وإنما يستحق ذلك بعمله الذي يحصل باختياره . وأما قوله : « كل ميسر لما خلق له ، فالمراد : أنه قادر عليه ، غير ممنوع . وذلك هو صريح مذهب الاعتزال

والجواب :
قولنا
أما حمل هذا الكلام على الحكم والكتابة فقد تقدم القول بأن هذا يوجب
وأما قوله : « إنه عليه السلام ما أحال السعادة والشقاوة على ذلك الكتاب ، بل على ذلك العمل ، فجوابه : إن الحديث دل على أنه تعالى إنما قدر له السعادة تارة ، والشقاوة أخرى ، بواسطة الأعمال المفضية إليها ، والموجبة لها . وذلك هو صريح قولنا
The sixth proof: What Muslim transmitted in his Sahih with his chain from Jabir, who said: Suraqa bin Malik bin Ju'shum came and said: O Messenger of Allah, clarify our religion for us as if we were just created. Is the action today [based on] what the pens have dried from and the decrees have run? Or is it something we initiate? He (peace be upon him) said: 'Rather, it is what the pens have dried from and the decrees have run.' He said: Then what is the action? He said: 'Work, for each is made easy.' The author of Sharh al-Sunnah said after narrating this report: 'And it is authentically reported from Abu Hurayra from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he said: "O Abu Hurayra, the pen has dried regarding what you will encounter." ... So they disputed over that, Abu Dharr. They said: The meaning of his statement "the matter has been completed" is the writing in the Preserved Tablet and the informing about whether one is wretched or blessed. They said: The evidence that the intended meaning is what we mentioned is that he (peace be upon him) explained that that writing does not necessitate the wretchedness or happiness of the servant, rather he deserves that by his action which occurs by his choice. And as for his statement: "Each is made easy for what he is created for," the meaning is that he is capable of it, not prevented. That is the explicit doctrine of the Mu'tazila. The answer: Our statement: As for interpreting this speech as referring to judgment and writing, it has already been said that this necessitates [something]. And as for his statement that he (peace be upon him) did not attribute happiness and wretchedness to that writing but to that action, the answer is that the hadith indicates that Allah only decreed for him happiness at one time and wretchedness at another through the actions that lead to them and necessitate them. That is our explicit statement.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof and addresses a Mu'tazili objection. The author first narrates the hadith where Suraqa asks the Prophet about whether actions are predestined or newly initiated. The Prophet responds that the pens have dried, yet commands to work, for each is made easy. The author of Sharh al-Sunnah is then quoted, who reports a dispute among companions (Abu Dharr and others) regarding the interpretation. The Mu'tazila interpret 'each is made easy' as meaning the person is capable and not prevented, which they see as supporting free will. The author then gives the Ash'ari answer: the hadith shows that Allah decrees happiness or wretchedness through the actions that lead to them, not directly. Thus, the writing in the Preserved Tablet does not negate the causal role of actions. The passage is structured as: hadith, Mu'tazili interpretation, and Ash'ari response.

Key Terms
جف القلم
المقادير
التيسير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the hadith 'جف القلم' implies that human effort is useless.
Correction: The Prophet immediately said 'اعملوا', showing that effort is required.

Checkpoint

A) 'Do nothing, for it is already written'
B) 'Work, for each is made easy'
C) 'It is all up to your choice'
D) 'Ask the scholars'

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Suraqa affirms both divine decree and the command to act, setting the stage for the theological reconciliation between predestination and human responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The companions themselves disputed over the meaning of 'كل ميسر'. Do you ever feel confused about how divine decree and your efforts fit together? How does this hadith challenge you to act without fully understanding the mystery?
?
Suraqa felt as if he was just created, seeking clarity. Have you ever felt the weight of predestination paralyze you? What is the one concrete action you will take this week in light of 'work, for each is made easy'?

The Ash'ari Refutation of the Mu'tazili Interpretation
Mu'tazili interpretation and Ash'ari refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari response reconciles divine decree with human action by showing that Allah decrees happiness or wretchedness through the actions that lead to them.

Core Idea
Allah decrees through actions, not apart from them.

The Mu'tazila interpreted 'each is made easy' as meaning that humans are capable and free from divine constraint, using it to support free will. The Ash'ari answer presented here shows that the hadith actually teaches that Allah's decree of happiness or wretchedness is mediated through the actions He creates. This lesson unpacks that refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazili argument
Read the passage where the Mu'tazila explain their interpretation. They say the writing in the Preserved Tablet does not cause happiness or misery; rather, the servant deserves it by his own choice.
They use 'كل ميسر لما خلق له' to mean capability.
2
Read the Ash'ari response
The author responds that the hadith shows Allah decrees happiness and misery 'by means of' (بواسطة) the actions that lead to them. This means the decree is fulfilled through the actions He creates.
The response emphasizes that actions are the means, not the ultimate cause.
3
Compare the two views
Note the difference: Mu'tazila see the hadith as supporting human autonomy; Ash'ari see it as supporting predestination through causal means. Which one aligns with the Prophet's command to work?
Both sides use the same hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : ما رواه مسلم في صحيحه ، بإسناده عن جابر ، قال : جاء سراقة بن مالك بن جعشم ، فقال : يا رسول الله بين لنا ديننا ، كأنا خلقنا الآن . قيم العمل اليوم ؟ فيها جفت به الأقلام ، وجرت به المقادير ؟ أو فيها نستقبل ؟ قال عليه السلام : ( بل فيها جفت به الأقلام ، وجرت به المقادير ؟ قال : فقيم العمل ؟ قال : ( اعملوا : فإن كلا ميسره. قال صاحب شرح السنة ، بعد ما روى هذا الخبر : ( وصح عن أبي هريرة ، عن رسول الله عليه السلام أنه قال : « يا أبا هريرة جف القلم بما أنت لاق . . فاختصمه على ذلك، أبو ذره قالوا : المراد من قوله : «الأمر قد فرغ منه هو الكتابة في اللوح المحفوظ ، والإخبار عن كونه شقياً أو سعيداً . قالوا : والدليل على أن المراد ما ذكر نام : أنه عليه السلام بين أن تلك الكتابة غير موجبة لشقاوة العبد ولسعادته ، وإنما يستحق ذلك بعمله الذي يحصل باختياره . وأما قوله : « كل ميسر لما خلق له ، فالمراد : أنه قادر عليه ، غير ممنوع . وذلك هو صريح مذهب الاعتزال

والجواب :
قولنا
أما حمل هذا الكلام على الحكم والكتابة فقد تقدم القول بأن هذا يوجب
وأما قوله : « إنه عليه السلام ما أحال السعادة والشقاوة على ذلك الكتاب ، بل على ذلك العمل ، فجوابه : إن الحديث دل على أنه تعالى إنما قدر له السعادة تارة ، والشقاوة أخرى ، بواسطة الأعمال المفضية إليها ، والموجبة لها . وذلك هو صريح قولنا
The sixth proof: What Muslim transmitted in his Sahih with his chain from Jabir, who said: Suraqa bin Malik bin Ju'shum came and said: O Messenger of Allah, clarify our religion for us as if we were just created. Is the action today [based on] what the pens have dried from and the decrees have run? Or is it something we initiate? He (peace be upon him) said: 'Rather, it is what the pens have dried from and the decrees have run.' He said: Then what is the action? He said: 'Work, for each is made easy.' The author of Sharh al-Sunnah said after narrating this report: 'And it is authentically reported from Abu Hurayra from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he said: "O Abu Hurayra, the pen has dried regarding what you will encounter." ... So they disputed over that, Abu Dharr. They said: The meaning of his statement "the matter has been completed" is the writing in the Preserved Tablet and the informing about whether one is wretched or blessed. They said: The evidence that the intended meaning is what we mentioned is that he (peace be upon him) explained that that writing does not necessitate the wretchedness or happiness of the servant, rather he deserves that by his action which occurs by his choice. And as for his statement: "Each is made easy for what he is created for," the meaning is that he is capable of it, not prevented. That is the explicit doctrine of the Mu'tazila. The answer: Our statement: As for interpreting this speech as referring to judgment and writing, it has already been said that this necessitates [something]. And as for his statement that he (peace be upon him) did not attribute happiness and wretchedness to that writing but to that action, the answer is that the hadith indicates that Allah only decreed for him happiness at one time and wretchedness at another through the actions that lead to them and necessitate them. That is our explicit statement.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof and addresses a Mu'tazili objection. The author first narrates the hadith where Suraqa asks the Prophet about whether actions are predestined or newly initiated. The Prophet responds that the pens have dried, yet commands to work, for each is made easy. The author of Sharh al-Sunnah is then quoted, who reports a dispute among companions (Abu Dharr and others) regarding the interpretation. The Mu'tazila interpret 'each is made easy' as meaning the person is capable and not prevented, which they see as supporting free will. The author then gives the Ash'ari answer: the hadith shows that Allah decrees happiness or wretchedness through the actions that lead to them, not directly. Thus, the writing in the Preserved Tablet does not negate the causal role of actions. The passage is structured as: hadith, Mu'tazili interpretation, and Ash'ari response.

Key Terms
الاختيار
اللوح المحفوظ
التيسير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari response, how does Allah decree happiness for a person?
A) Directly without any action
B) Through the actions that lead to happiness
C) By rewarding regardless of action
D) The hadith does not say

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari response reconciles divine decree and human action by showing that Allah's decree is carried out through the actions He creates, making actions the means by which predestined outcomes occur.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you genuinely live as though your actions are the means through which Allah's decree is fulfilled, or have you ever used the belief in qadar to avoid taking responsibility? Think of a specific situation where you said 'it was written' instead of acting. What would it look like to take one step toward change today, trusting that your effort is part of the decree?
?
When you sin, do you blame your circumstances or your own choice? This lesson teaches that your actions are real means to your outcome. Recall a particular sin you committed. How can you now see your own role in that act, and how does that awareness push you to repent and change your behavior starting now?
?
If you truly believe that Allah's decree is carried out through your actions, then what action will you take today—before this day ends—to seek a good outcome in your hereafter? Be specific: name one act of obedience you will perform right now as a means to realize Allah's decree of happiness.

The Seventh Proof: Hadith of the Share of Zina
Author presents a hadith and begins its theological inference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith about the prescribed share of zina is used to prove the comprehensiveness of divine foreknowledge and decree.

Core Idea
Even sins are decreed and known by Allah, showing qadar's reach.

The author presents a seventh proof drawn from a well-known hadith reported by Abu Hurayra and transmitted by al-Bukhari. This hadith reveals that Allah has decreed for every person a share of zina—not just the physical act but also the sins of the eye, tongue, and inner desires. The incomplete inference hints at the logical conclusion that what Allah knows and informs about must inevitably occur. In this lesson we will examine the hadith text and begin to unpack its theological implication.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Start by reading the Arabic hadith and its translation. Notice the three forms of zina mentioned: the eye, the tongue, and the private part, along with the soul's desires.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari, a primary source.
2
Analyze the author's inference
The author states that the inference is the same as before: because Allah knew and informed about these acts, they must happen. Consider how knowledge and information lead to inevitability.
The passage cuts off; think about how the argument would conclude.
3
Address the common misunderstanding
Some might think this hadith excuses actual zina. Reflect on the Prophet's explanation that different types of zina are sinful even if the private part is not involved.
The hadith distinguishes between forms of sin; the decree does not justify committing them.
4
Relate to the broader concept of qadar
This proof shows that divine foreknowledge and decree encompass all actions, including sins. Ask yourself how this aligns with human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : روى البخاري بإسناده عن ابن عباس أنه قال : ما رأيت شيئاً أشبه باللحمة ، مما قاله أبو هريرة ، عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، أنه قال : « إن الله كتب على ابن آدم حظه من الزنا ، أدرك ذلك لا محالة . وزنا العين النظر ، وزها اللسان النطق ، والنفس تمنى وتشتهي ، والفرج يصدق ذلك ويكذبه ) . وجه الاستدلال بالخبر : ما تقدم. أنه تعالى لما علم ذلك وأخبر عنه ،
The seventh proof: Al-Bukhari transmitted with his chain from Ibn Abbas that he said: I have not seen anything more resembling the lamam? than what Abu Hurayra said from the Prophet (peace be upon him), that he said: 'Indeed Allah has written for the son of Adam his share of zina; he will inevitably attain that. The zina of the eye is the look, the zina of the tongue is speech, the soul desires and wishes, and the private part confirms that or denies it.' The aspect of inference from the report is what preceded: that Allah, since He knew that and informed about it...
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh proof, a hadith from Bukhari narrated by Ibn Abbas. The hadith states that Allah has decreed for every person a share of zina that will inevitably occur, specifying that zina can be of the eye (looking), tongue (speech), and the private part. The author then states that the inference from this report is as previously mentioned: because Allah knew and informed about these actions, they must occur as decreed. The proof here emphasizes that even illicit actions are encompassed in divine knowledge and decree, showing the comprehensiveness of qadar. The passage appears incomplete, as it ends with 'that Allah, since He knew that and informed about it', likely continuing to conclude that the occurrence of the action is necessitated.

Key Terms

كتب

النظر
النطق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith is sometimes misinterpreted as excusing actual zina, as if to say 'since it is decreed, there is no sin'.
Correction: The Prophet's explanation shows that even the look and speech are sinful forms of zina. The decree does not remove human responsibility; rather, it affirms that Allah's knowledge covers all actions, including sins.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the share of zina affirms that Allah's decree and foreknowledge cover even the details of sin, illustrating the all-encompassing nature of qadar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Ash'ari Answer to the Tautology Objection
The author presents and refutes an interpretation of a hadith about qadar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari framework of power (qudra) and motive (dā'iyah) refutes the claim that interpreting taqdir as creation leads to a tautology.

Core Idea
Power plus motive is the condition; the action is its distinct result.

In this lesson, we examine an opponent's objection that interpreting 'taqdir' as creation makes a conditional statement tautological. The author presents an Ash'ari response that distinguishes between the condition (creation of power with motive) and the result (the action), thereby preserving meaningful causal language. This passage sharpens our understanding of how Ash'ari theology conceptualizes divine action and human agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and the opponent's interpretation
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the opponent's two possible interpretations of 'taqdir' (as knowledge or writing) and their denial that it means creation.
The hadith is from Anas ibn Malik.
2
Identify the opponent's tautology objection
Find where the opponent argues that if 'taqdir' meant creation, the conditional 'if it had been, it would have been' would make the result identical to the condition.
This is the key challenge the Ash'ari answer must address.
3
Understand the Ash'ari answer
The author responds by stating that on the Ash'ari view, the condition is the creation of power together with the motive, and the result is the action that follows. These are distinct.
This avoids tautology because condition and result are different.
4
Reflect on the metaphysical implications
Consider how this distinction preserves a meaningful role for divine causality and human action within the Ash'ari framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية عشر: روى أنس أنه قال : خدمت النبي عليه السلام سنين . فما بعثني في حاجة لم تتهيأ ، إلا قال : « لو قضى لكان ، أوه لو قدر لكان ، قالوا : المراد : أن الله لو علم أنه سيكون ، لكان . أو المراد : أنه لو كتب في اللوح المحفوظ أنه كائن ، لكان. ثم قالوا : وليس المراد من التقدير : الخلق . وإلا لصار معنى الكلام إنه لو كان لكان. فيصير الجزاء عين الشرط • والجواب : أما حمل التقدير على الكتابة ، أو العلم . فقد سبق القول فيه . وقوله : ( يلزم كون الجزاء عين الشرط ، قلنا : هذا لا يلزم على قولنا : إن مجموع القدرة مع الداعي يوجب الفعل . لأن الشرط هو خلق القدرة مع الداعي ، والجزاء ترتيب الفعل عليه
The twelfth proof: Anas narrated that he said: I served the Prophet, peace be upon him, for years. He never sent me on a need that was not accomplished, except he said: 'If it had been decreed, it would have been, oh if it had been destined, it would have been.' They said: The intended meaning is that if God had known that it would be, it would have been. Or the intended meaning is that if He had written in the Preserved Tablet that it would be, it would have been. Then they said: The intended meaning of 'taqdir' (destiny) is not creation. Otherwise the meaning of the speech would become 'if it had been, it would have been,' thus making the result identical to the condition. The answer: As for interpreting 'taqdir' as writing or knowledge, the discussion on that has preceded. And as for his statement: 'It necessitates that the result is identical to the condition,' we say: This does not follow according to our view that the combination of power (qudra) with the motive (dā'iyah) necessitates the action. Because the condition is the creation of power along with the motive, and the result is the occurrence of the action upon it.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from a hadith of Anas ibn Malik regarding the Prophet's practice of saying 'if it had been destined' when something did not occur. The author first quotes the hadith, then reports an interpretation by opponents (likely Mu'tazila) who explain the phrase 'لو قدر لكان' as referring to God's knowledge or writing in the Preserved Tablet, denying that it means creation. They argue that if 'taqdir' meant creation, the conditional sentence would be tautological ('if it had been, it would have been'). The author then gives the Ash'ari answer: this objection does not apply because, according to the Ash'ari view, the condition (sharṭ) is the creation of power (qudra) together with the motive (dā'iyah), and the result (jazā') is the action that follows from that combination. Thus, the condition and result are distinct, avoiding tautology. The key nuance is the Ash'ari theory that power and motive together necessitate the action, preserving divine causality.

Key Terms
قدر (qadar)
تقدير (taqdir)
قدرة (qudra)
داعية (dā'iyah)
شرط (sharṭ)
جزاء (jazā')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any interpretation of 'taqdir' as creation necessarily leads to a tautology in conditional statements.
Correction: The Ash'ari framework avoids tautology by distinguishing the condition (creation of power with motive) from the result (the action), so they are not identical.

Checkpoint
According to the answer in the twelfth proof, what is the condition (sharṭ) that necessitates the action?
A) God's knowledge alone
B) The writing in the Preserved Tablet
C) The creation of power along with the motive
D) The mere existence of the action

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari theory of power and motive distinguishes condition from result, refuting the accusation of tautology in interpreting taqdir as creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you said 'if only' about something that did not happen. Did you subconsciously think it was because God's decree was absent? This lesson teaches that the Prophet himself said 'if it had been destined, it would have been' — meaning everything that occurs does so only by God's creation of power and motive. Will you now confess that even your missed opportunities were decreed by God, and that regret is a form of questioning His wisdom? Commit today to saying 'qadara Allahu wa mā shā'a fa'ala' (Allah decreed and what He wills, He does) and accept His decree with contentment.
?
The opponents argued that interpreting taqdir as creation leads to tautology. In your own life, do you sometimes assume that your choices are entirely your own, separate from God's creative act? This lesson insists that every action is the result of God's creation of power and motive within you. Examine your heart: do you truly believe that even your sins are within God's decree? If not, how will you realign your belief with the Ash'ari teaching that 'there is no creator but Allah, and actions are His creation'? Take one concrete step today to acknowledge God's sovereignty in every action you perform.

The Thirteenth Proof: Belief in Qadar from the Companions
Multiple companions affirm qadar as condition for deed acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the thirteenth proof from the Companions establishes belief in qadar as a necessary condition for the acceptance of deeds, and you will see how this refutes those who limit qadar to mere knowledge and writing.

Core Idea
Belief in qadar is the key that unlocks the acceptance of all deeds.

In this lesson, we examine a powerful proof from multiple Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that ties the acceptance of all good deeds to belief in qadar. The report is narrated by Ubayy ibn Ka'b, Ibn Mas'ud, Hudhayfa, and Zayd ibn Thabit, all affirming that even enormous charity is futile without affirming destiny. The Mu'tazila's attempt to reinterpret this hadith is also addressed, showing the centrality of qadar in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage from the thirteenth proof carefully. Notice the chain of narrators and the repeated emphasis on belief in qadar.
The Arabic uses the term 'qadar' and describes the condition for acceptance.
2
Identify the key condition
Identify the condition Ubayy ibn Ka'b gives for deeds to be accepted. He says even spending like Mount Uhud is not accepted until one believes in qadar and that what befalls could not have been missed.
This is the core of the proof.
3
Trace the multiple testimonies
Notice that the same statement is confirmed by Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Hudhayfa ibn al-Yaman, and Zayd ibn Thabit (from the Prophet). This shows the unanimity of the Companions on this matter.
Multiple narrators strengthen the proof.
4
Understand the Mu'tazila response
The author notes that the Mu'tazila interpret the hadith as referring to God's knowledge and writing. Reflect on how this passage refutes that interpretation by linking acceptance to qadar itself, not just knowledge.
The answer to their interpretation is said to have preceded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة عشر : قال ابن الرملي : أتيت أبي بن كعب ، فقلت : في نفسي شيء من القدر ، فحدثني بشيء لعله أن يذهب عن قلبي . فقال : إن الله لو عذب أهل سماواته وأهل أرضه ، عذبهم غير ظالم . ولو رحمهم ، كانت رحمته إياهم خيراً لهم من أعمالهم . وولو انفقت مثل جبل أحد في سبيل الله ، ما قبل الله منك ، حتى تؤمن بالقدر ، وتعلم أن ما أصابك لم يكن ليخطئك ، وأن ما أخطأك لم يكن ليصيبك ، ولو مت على غير ذلك ، أوجبت النار . قال : ثم أتيت عبد الله بن مسعود ، فقال : مثل قوله ، ثم أتيت حذيفة بن اليمان ، فقال : مثل قوله ، ثم أتيت زيد بن ثابت فحدثني عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بمثل ذلك وأما المعتزلة . فإنهم حملوه على العلم والكتابة . وقد سبق جوابه
The thirteenth proof: Ibn al-Ramli said: I came to Ubayy ibn Ka'b and said: I have something in myself concerning qadar (destiny), so speak to me about something that might remove it from my heart. He said: 'If God were to punish the inhabitants of His heavens and the inhabitants of His earth, He would punish them without being unjust. And if He were to have mercy on them, His mercy to them would be better for them than their deeds. And if you were to spend the like of Mount Uhud in the way of God, He would not accept it from you until you believe in qadar, and know that what has befallen you could not have missed you, and what has missed you could not have befallen you. And if you die upon other than that, you would enter the Fire.' He said: Then I came to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and he said the like of his statement. Then I came to Hudhayfa ibn al-Yaman, and he said the like of his statement. Then I came to Zayd ibn Thabit, and he narrated to me from the Prophet, peace be upon him, the like of that. As for the Mu'tazila, they interpreted it as knowledge and writing, and its answer has preceded.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents the thirteenth proof, which is a report from multiple companions (Ubayy ibn Ka'b, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Hudhayfa ibn al-Yaman, and Zayd ibn Thabit from the Prophet) emphasizing the necessity of belief in qadar. The author quotes the conversation between Ibn al-Ramli and Ubayy, who states that even if one spends the equivalent of Mount Uhud in charity, it will not be accepted until one believes that whatever happens was destined and cannot be otherwise. The companion also says that if God were to punish or have mercy, it would be just. The report stresses that disbelief in qadar leads to Hell. The author then notes that the Mu'tazila interpret the hadith as referring to God's knowledge and writing, and the author says the answer to that interpretation has already been given earlier. This proof establishes qadar as a core tenet of faith without which deeds are worthless.

Key Terms
قدر (qadar)
علم (ʿilm)
كتابة (kitāba)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that belief in qadar is only about God's knowledge and writing (al-ʿilm wa al-kitāba), not about the actual decree.
Correction: The hadith explicitly ties acceptance of deeds to belief in qadar as described: that whatever befalls one could not have been missed, and whatever misses could not have befallen one, which goes beyond mere knowledge and writing.

Checkpoint
According to the thirteenth proof, what is required for one's deeds to be accepted?
A) Spending a lot in charity
B) Believing in qadar and that what befalls one could not have been missed
C) Performing many voluntary prayers
D) Following the companions exactly

Key Takeaway
The thirteenth proof from multiple companions establishes that belief in qadar is a fundamental condition for the acceptance of all deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The companion said that even spending Mount Uhud would not be accepted without belief in qadar. Is there any area in your life where you rely on your own efforts more than on Allah's decree? What would it take for you to truly internalize that every outcome is from Him?
?
Ubayy stated that if Allah punished all, He would be just, and if He had mercy, it is better than their deeds. Do you live with the awareness that you deserve nothing from Allah except by His mercy? How does that change the way you approach your good deeds and your sins?
?
The passage teaches that what has befallen you could not have missed you, and what missed you could not have befallen you. Is there a specific trial or missed opportunity in your life that you have not fully accepted as Allah's decree? What would complete surrender to that truth look like for you today?

Proof from the Istikhara Hadith
A multi-faceted proof from the istikhara hadith for divine determination of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the istikhara hadith proves that all actions and inner states are determined by Allah.

Core Idea
The istikhara hadith shows that motives and contentment come only from Allah.

The author now presents a proof from the well-known hadith of istikhara, which the Prophet taught to his companions. This prayer includes phrases that, upon reflection, reveal that even our ability to choose and our contentment with outcomes are granted by Allah. The passage first quotes the hadith, then extracts three distinct arguments from its wording, and finally responds to a potential objection from those who deny divine pre-determination.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith of istikhara
Begin by carefully reading the Arabic text of the hadith as transmitted by Tirmidhi. Notice how the supplication asks Allah for choice, power, and facilitation.
The hadith is authentic and contains key theological phrases.
2
Examine the three aspects of the proof
The author extracts three arguments: (1) facilitation implies divine creation of motive, (2) 'destine for me good' implies decree, (3) 'make me content' implies divine origin of contentment.
Each aspect builds on a different phrase from the hadith.
3
Understand the objection and response
The Mu'tazila reinterpret facilitation as external aids. The author refutes this by showing it contradicts their own view of human independence.
This exchange clarifies the Ash'ari stance.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how the hadith, when taken as a whole, supports the doctrine of qadar: everything, including motives and contentment, is from Allah.
This proof is one of several in the text.
