الحجة الرابعة عشر : التمسك بالدعاء المروي في صلاة الاستخارة ، روى أبو عيسى الترمذي في جامعه بإسناده عن جابر بن عبد الله الأنصاري . قال : كان رسول الله عليه السلام يعلمنا الاستخارة في الأمور ، كما يعلمنا السورة من القرآن . يقول : ( إذا هم أحدكم بالأمر ، فليركع ركعتين من غير الفريضة ثم ليقل : « اللهم اني استخيرك بعلمك ، واستقدرك بقدرتك ، وأسألك من فضلك العظيم . فإنك تقدر ولا أقدر ، وتعلم ولا أعلم ، وأنت علام الغيوب . اللهم إن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر خير لي في ديني ومعيشتي وعاقبة أمري ، فاقدره لي، ويسره لي، ثم بارك لي فيه . وإن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر شر لي في ديني ومعيشتي وعاقبة أمري ، فاصرفه عني واصرفني عنه ، واقدر لي الخير حيث كان ، ثم أرضني به ، قال : ويسمي حاجته . قال أبـو عيسى : هذا حديث صحيح واعلم : أن الاستدلال به من وجوه : الأول : إن الفعل الذي يطلب الاستخارة فيه . لا شك أنه قادر عليه ، نظراً إلى سلامة الأعضاء ، وصحة المزاج. ثم إنه مع ذلك طلب من الله تيسيره له ، إن كان له فيه مصلحة ، وصرفه عنه ، إن كان له فيه مفسدة . وهذا التيسير والصرف لا معنى له إلا القاء داعية الفعل في القلب ، أو القاء داعية الترك فيه. فهذا الحديث يدل على أن صدور الفعل عن العبد ، يتوقف على إلقاء تلك الداعية في قلبه ، ويدل أيضاً على أنه متى حصلت تلك الداعية الجازمة في القلب ، فإنه يحصل ذلك الفعل ، لا محالة . والوجه الثاني : قوله : ( اقدر لي الخير، حيث كان ، وهذا يدل على أن الكل بقدر الله والثالث : قوله : ( ثم أرضني به ) وهذا يدل على أن حصول الرضا في القلب تارة ، والسخط أخرى . ليس إلا من الله تعالى . · قالوا : لم لا يجوز أن يكون المراد من التيسير ، فعل الألطاف ، وتحصيل المعدات ، وإزالة العوائق ؟ وأما قوله : ( فاقدره لي ، فالمراد : فاكتب لي ذلك . والجواب : إن مذهبكم أن العبد قادر على ذلك الفعل ، وعلى ضـده ، وأن ترجيح أحدهما على الآخر ليس إلا من العبد ، وليس لله في ذلك الترجيح ، صنع ، ولا عمل البتة . وإذا كان كذلك ، كان طلب هذا التيسير عبثاً ولغواً
The fourteenth proof: Adherence to the supplication reported in the prayer of istikhara. Abu Isa al-Tirmidhi narrated in his Jami' with his chain from Jabir ibn Abdullah al-Ansari, who said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, used to teach us istikhara in matters as he taught us a sura from the Quran. He said: 'When one of you intends a matter, let him pray two rak'as of non-obligatory prayer, then say: O God, I seek Your choice by Your knowledge, and I seek Your power by Your ability, and I ask You of Your great bounty. For indeed You are able and I am not able, and You know and I do not know, and You are the Knower of the unseen. O God, if You know that this matter is good for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affair, then destine it for me, make it easy for me, then bless me in it. And if You know that this matter is evil for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affair, then turn it away from me and turn me away from it, and destine for me the good wherever it may be, then make me content with it.' He said: And he should mention his need. Abu Isa said: This hadith is authentic. And know: that the deduction from it is in aspects: The first: The action concerning which istikhara is sought – there is no doubt that one is capable of it, considering soundness of limbs and health of temperament. Yet despite that, he asks God to facilitate it for him if there is benefit in it, and to turn it away from him if there is harm in it. This facilitation and turning away mean nothing but the casting of the motive (dā'iyah) for the action into the heart, or the casting of the motive for refraining from it into the heart. So this hadith indicates that the occurrence of the action from the servant depends on the casting of that motive into his heart, and also indicates that whenever that decisive motive occurs in the heart, then that action occurs inevitably. The second aspect: His statement: 'Destine for me the good wherever it may be' – this indicates that everything is by the decree (qadar) of God. The third: His statement: 'Then make me content with it' – this indicates that the occurrence of contentment in the heart sometimes, and displeasure at other times, is only from God Most High. They said: Why is it not permissible that what is meant by 'facilitation' is the doing of favors (alṭāf), the preparation of means, and the removal of obstacles? And as for His statement: 'Then destine it for me,' the meaning is: write it for me. The answer: According to your doctrine, the servant is capable of that action and its opposite, and the preference of one over the other is only from the servant, and God has no part at all in that preference. If that is so, then asking for this facilitation would be futile and meaningless.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents the fourteenth proof, a detailed argument from the well-known hadith of the istikhara prayer. The author first quotes the hadith from Tirmidhi, then breaks down the inference into three aspects (wujuh). The first aspect: the person is capable of the action, yet he asks God to facilitate it or turn it away. This facilitation is interpreted as God casting the motive (dā'iyah) into the heart. The hadith thus shows that the action depends on the motive from God, and when the decisive motive occurs, the action necessarily follows. The second aspect: the phrase 'Destine for me the good' proves that everything is by God's decree (qadar). The third aspect: the phrase 'Make me content' shows that contentment and displeasure are from God alone. The author then presents an objection from the opponents (Mu'tazila): they suggest that 'facilitation' means God provides favors (alṭāf), prepares means, removes obstacles, and that 'destine' means write. The author replies that this interpretation is inconsistent with the Mu'tazili own doctrine that the servant independently chooses and prefers his action, because if God has no role in the preference, then asking for facilitation would be pointless. Thus the hadith supports the Ash'ari view that God creates motives and determines actions.

Key Terms
استخارة (istikhāra)
تيسير (taysīr)
داعية (dā'iyah)
قدر (qadar)
لطف (luṭf)
كتابة (kitāba)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'facilitation' in istikhara means only external assistance like removing obstacles, not an internal motive.
Correction: The author argues that facilitation must be the casting of a decisive motive into the heart, because the act of seeking facilitation would be pointless if one already has independent power to choose.

Checkpoint
According to the first aspect of the istikhara hadith, what does the act of seeking facilitation (taysīr) from God indicate?
A) That God only helps with external means
B) That the action depends on God casting a motive into the heart
C) That the servant is not capable of the action
D) That God writes the action in the Preserved Tablet

Key Takeaway
The istikhara hadith proves that both the motive to act and the contentment with outcomes are created by Allah, affirming His absolute control over human actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray istikhara, do you truly believe that Allah is the one who will create both the motive to proceed and the contentment with the outcome? How does this change how you approach decisions?
?
The hadith says 'You are able and I am not able.' Do you live as if you are truly unable without Allah's facilitation? Think of a recent decision: did you rely on your own ability or Allah's power?
?
If contentment (rida) comes only from Allah, then your dissatisfaction with Allah's decree is a spiritual problem. Reflect on a past disappointment: did you seek contentment from Allah or did you remain discontent? What would it look like to ask Allah to make you content?

The Istikharah Hadith and Divine Creation of Motives
Al-Razi argues from the istikharah hadith for divine creation of the motive for action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the istikharah hadith is used to argue that God creates the decisive motive for action in the human heart, a central Ash'ari doctrine.

Core Idea
Asking God to 'make easy' an action implies He creates the very motive to act.

The hadith of istikharah (seeking guidance) is a familiar supplication, but its theological implications are profound. Al-Razi draws out three arguments from it to show that every human action depends on God's direct creation of the motive (dā'iyah) in the heart. This passage presents the arguments, anticipates a Mu'tazilite objection, and responds decisively.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its context
First, read the Arabic of the istikharah supplication and its brief chain. Notice the key phrases: 'facilitate it for me', 'turn it away', 'decree good', 'make me satisfied'.
The hadith is authentic according to Tirmidhi.
2
Analyze the first argument about 'taysīr'
Examine how Al-Razi interprets 'facilitation' (taysīr) as casting the motive for action into the heart. Note that the person already has physical ability, so the request must be about the internal impulse.
3
Study the second and third arguments
The second argument links 'decree good' (uqdur li al-khayr) to divine decree of all things. The third argument shows that satisfaction (riḍā) in the heart comes only from God.
4
Consider the objection and the response
The opponent suggests 'taysīr' means external aids, not internal motives. Al-Razi's response undercuts the Mu'tazilite position of independent human choice by showing that such a request would be meaningless if the servant were truly autonomous.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعاقبة أمري ، فاقدره لي، ويسره لي، ثم بارك لي فيه . وإن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر شر لي في ديني ومعيشتي وعاقبة أمري ، فاصرفه عني واصرفني عنه ، واقدر لي الخير حيث كان ، ثم أرضني به ، قال : ويسمي حاجته . قال أبـو عيسى : هذا حديث صحيح واعلم : أن الاستدلال به من وجوه : الأول : إن الفعل الذي يطلب الاستخارة فيه . لا شك أنه قادر عليه، نظراً إلى سلامة الأعضاء، وصحة المزاج. ثم إنه مع ذلك طلب من الله تيسيره له، إن كان له فيه مصلحة، وصرفه عنه، إن كان له فيه مفسدة . وهذا التيسير والصرف لا معنى له إلا القاء داعية الفعل في القلب، أو القاء داعية الترك فيه. فهذا الحديث يدل على أن صدور الفعل عن العبد، يتوقف على إلقاء تلك الداعية في قلبه، ويدل أيضاً على أنه متى حصلت تلك الداعية الجازمة في القلب، فإنه يحصل ذلك الفعل، لا محالة . والوجه الثاني : قوله : ( اقدر لي الخير، حيث كان، وهذا يدل على أن الكل بقدر الله . والثالث : قوله : ( ثم أرضني به ) وهذا يدل على أن حصول الرضا في القلب تارة، والسخط أخرى . ليس إلا من الله تعالى . قالوا : لم لا يجوز أن يكون المراد من التيسير ، فعل الألطاف ، وتحصيل المعدات ، وإزالة العوائق ؟ وأما قوله : ( فاقدره لي ، فالمراد : فاكتب لي ذلك . والجواب : إن مذهبكم أن العبد قادر على ذلك الفعل ، وعلى ضـده، وأن ترجيح أحدهما على الآخر ليس إلا من العبد ، وليس لله في ذلك الترجيح ، صنع ، ولا عمل البتة . وإذا كان كذلك ، كان طلب هذا التيسير عبثاً ولغواً
And the outcome of my affair, so decree it for me, and make it easy for me, then bless me in it. And if You know that this affair is evil for me in my religion and my livelihood and the outcome of my affair, then turn it away from me and turn me away from it, and decree good for me wherever it is, then make me satisfied with it.' He said: 'And he mentions his need.' Abu Isa said: 'This hadith is authentic.' And know: that deriving evidence from it has several aspects: The first: that the action for which one seeks guidance (istikharah) is undoubtedly one he is capable of, considering the soundness of his limbs and the health of his temperament. Then despite that, he asks God to facilitate it for him if there is benefit for him in it, and to turn it away from him if there is harm for him in it. And this facilitation and turning away mean nothing other than casting the motive (dā'iyah) for the action into the heart, or casting the motive for abandoning it. So this hadith indicates that the occurrence of the action from the servant depends on the casting of that motive into his heart, and also indicates that whenever that decisive motive occurs in the heart, that action occurs without exception. The second aspect: His saying: 'Decree good for me wherever it is' — this indicates that everything is by God's decree. The third: His saying: 'Then make me satisfied with it' — this indicates that the occurrence of satisfaction in the heart sometimes, and dissatisfaction at other times, is only from God Most High. They said: 'Why is it not permissible that what is meant by facilitation (taysīr) is the act of divine graces (alṭāf), and procuring the preparations (mu'addāt), and removing obstacles (awā'iq)? And as for His saying: "Decree it for me," what is meant is: Write it for me.' The answer: Indeed your doctrine is that the servant is capable of that action and its opposite, and that the preponderance (tarjīḥ) of one over the other is only from the servant, and God has no part in that preponderance whatsoever. And if that is the case, then asking for this facilitation would be futile and in vain.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is an argument derived from the hadith of istikharah (seeking guidance) to prove that human actions depend on God's creation of the decisive motive (dā'iyah) in the heart, a key Ash'ari doctrine. The author first quotes the relevant part of the hadith, then presents three aspects of inference. First, the person seeking istikharah asks God to facilitate (yassir) the action or turn it away (ṣarrafa) if it is harmful. The author argues that 'facilitation' can only mean that God casts the motive for the action or its abandonment into the heart, because the person already has the physical ability. Second, the phrase 'decree good for me' (uqdur li al-khayr) shows that all is by decree (qadr). Third, the phrase 'then make me satisfied' (arḍinī bih) shows that satisfaction or dissatisfaction in the heart comes only from God. Then an objection is raised: perhaps 'taysīr' refers to divine graces (alṭāf), preparations, removing obstacles. The author responds by pointing out that if the Mu'tazila claim that the servant has independent power to choose, then asking for facilitation is pointless, because the servant could do it himself. Thus the hadith supports the Ash'ari view.

المفسدة (harm)
القدر (decree)
الألطاف (divine graces)
المعدات (preparations)
العوائق (obstacles)
الترجيح (preponderance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The istikharah hadith only asks for external help (like provision or circumstances), not for changes in one's internal will.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that 'facilitation' logically implies God's direct creation of the motive in the heart, because the person already has the physical ability. External help would be irrelevant if the will were independent.

Checkpoint
According to the author's first argument from the istikharah hadith, what does 'taysīr' (facilitation) mean?
A) Creating the motive in the heart
B) Providing physical means
C) Removing obstacles
D) Writing the decree

Key Takeaway
The istikharah hadith, when analyzed, demonstrates that both the motive to act and the resulting satisfaction or dissatisfaction are directly created by God, supporting the Ash'ari doctrine of divine omnipotence over human will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make istikharah, do you genuinely believe that God is deciding even your inner inclination, or do you assume the desire that arises comes solely from you? How would your du'a change if you truly internalized that the very motive to choose comes from Him?
?
The hadith teaches that satisfaction (riḍā) is directly from God. Think of a recent disappointment—did you seek contentment from Him, or did you rely on your own reasoning to accept it? What would it look like to ask God to 'make you satisfied' with an outcome you currently resist?
?
If the decisive motive for every good action you take is cast by God, then every righteous deed is a gift—every prayer, every kind word. Does this make you more grateful or more passive? And for bad actions, do you take full responsibility while still acknowledging that the motive is created? Examine your heart: where is the line between humility and fatalism in your daily choices?

The Fifteenth Proof: The Qunut Hadith on Divine Guidance and Decree
Al-Razi uses the qunut hadith to prove divine guidance and decree, and answers Mu'tazilite objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi uses the qunut hadith to prove that guidance (hidāyah) and decree (qaḍā') are from Allah, and how he refutes Mu'tazilite reinterpretations.

Core Idea
The qunut prayer is a theological argument: guidance and even 'evil' come from Allah.

Al-Razi continues his series of proofs for divine decree by citing a well-known hadith taught by the Prophet for the witr prayer. This prayer contains phrases that, upon analysis, reveal that guidance, divine friendship, and even the decree of what appears evil all originate from Allah alone. In this passage, al-Razi presents three arguments from the hadith and responds to Mu'tazilite attempts to reinterpret them.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its translation
Start by reading the full Arabic text of the qunut hadith and its literal translation. Notice the key phrases: 'guide me', 'take me into Your care', and 'protect me from the evil of what You have decreed'.
These three phrases form the basis of the three arguments.
2
Understand the first argument about guidance
Al-Razi argues that 'guide me among those You have guided' shows guidance is from God, not mere explanation (bayān), because asking for what is already possessed is futile. Consider why the Mu'tazilite view would make the prayer redundant.
3
Understand the second argument about divine friendship
The phrase 'take me into Your care among those You have taken into Your care' implies a special friendship not shared by disbelievers. Al-Razi argues this goes beyond general graces like power and evidence, pointing to the creation of necessitating motives.
This distinguishes between general and specific wilāyah.
4
Understand the third argument about evil and decree
The request 'protect me from the evil of what You have decreed' indicates that God decrees evil as well as good. This directly asserts that evil is part of God's decree.
This is the most contested point with the Mu'tazila.
5
Follow the objection and answer
The Mu'tazila object by interpreting 'evil' as calamities and arguing that the prayer implies changing God's decree is possible. Al-Razi responds that even as calamities, the Mu'tazila consider them potentially beneficial, so one cannot unconditionally ask for their removal. This neutralizes their objection.
Notice how al-Razi uses the Mu'tazila's own principles against them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة عشر: روى أبو عيسى في جامعه، بإسناده عن الحسن بن علي، أنه قال : علمني رسول الله ، كلمات أقولهن في الوتر : اللهم اهدني فيمن هديت ، وعافني فيمن عافيت ، وتولني فيمن توليت وبارك لي فيها أعطيت ، وقني شر ما قضيت. إنك تقضي ولا يقضى عليك . إنه لا يذل من واليت ، تباركت ربنا وتعاليت ، والاستدلال به من وجوه : الأول : إن قوله : ( اللهم اهدني فيمن هديت، يدل على أن الهداية من الله . ولا يمكن حمله على البيان والدلالة . لأن ذلك حاصل عند المعتزلة . وطلب الحاصل عبث . والثاني : إن قوله : ( وتولني فيمن توليت ، يدل على قولنا . لأن ولاية الله تعالى . إن كانت عبارة عن خلق القدرة والآلة ، ووضع الدلائل ، وإزالة الأعذار ، فهذا قد فعله تعالى، في حق الكافر والمؤمن . فهو تعالى ولي الكفار ، وولي المؤمنين جميعاً ، بهذا التفسير . والخبر يدل على أنه يتولى أولياء. بأمور لا توجد في حق الكفار . وما ذاك إلا ما ذكرناه من خلق الدواعي الموجبة . والثالث : قوله : « وقني شر ما قضيت»، وهذا يدل على أنه تعالى قد يقضي بالشر، كما يقضي بالخير . فإن قيل : الكلام عليه من وجوه : الأول : إنا نحمل هذا الشر على المصائب والأمراض . والثاني : إن هذا الكلام يدل على أن تغيير قضاء الله جائز . وذلك هو مذهب المعتزلة . أما على قول الجبرية . فقضاء الله عبارة عن حكمه الأزلي وذلك لا يجوز تغييره. والجواب عن الأول : إن الشر . بمعنى المصائب والآلام . قد يكون مصلحة في حق المكلف عند المعتزلة . فلا يجوز من العبد أن يطلب من الله مطلقاً أن يصرفها عنه . بل إنما يجوز ذلك السؤال ، بشرط أن يكون صرفه عنه مصلحة . فثبت : أن الشر بمعنى الألم لا يجوز للعبد أن يطلب من الله صرفه
The fifteenth proof: Abu Isa narrated in his Jami' with his chain from al-Hasan ibn Ali that he said: The Messenger of God taught me words to say during the witr prayer: 'O God, guide me among those You have guided, and grant me well-being among those You have granted well-being, and take me into Your care among those You have taken into Your care, and bless me in what You have given, and protect me from the evil of what You have decreed. Indeed You decree and none decrees against You. Indeed he is not humiliated whom You take as a friend. Blessed are You, our Lord, and exalted.' And deriving evidence from it has several aspects: The first: His saying: 'O God, guide me among those You have guided' indicates that guidance (hidāyah) is from God. And it cannot be interpreted as explanation (bayān) and indication (dalālah) because that is already obtained according to the Mu'tazila, and asking for what is already obtained is futile. The second: His saying: 'And take me into Your care among those You have taken into Your care' indicates our position. For the friendship/wilāyah of God Most High, if it is interpreted as the creation of power (qudrah) and means (ālah), and the establishment of evidences (dalā'il), and removal of excuses (a'dhār), then this He has already done for both the disbeliever and the believer. Thus He is the friend/walī of the disbelievers and the friend of all believers according to this interpretation. But the report indicates that He takes into His care (yatawallā) friends (awliyā') with matters that do not exist for the disbelievers. And that is nothing but what we have mentioned: the creation of necessitating motives (dawā'ī mūjibah). The third: His saying: 'And protect me from the evil of what You have decreed' indicates that He Most High may decree evil just as He decrees good. If it is said: Discussion upon it has several aspects: The first: We interpret this evil as calamities (maṣā'ib) and diseases (amrāḍ). The second: This statement indicates that changing God's decree (qaḍā') is permissible. And that is the doctrine of the Mu'tazila. As for the doctrine of the Jabariyya (determinists), God's decree is His eternal judgment (ḥukm azalī), and that cannot be changed. The answer to the first: Evil in the sense of calamities and pains (ālām) may be a benefit (maṣlaḥah) for the morally obligated person according to the Mu'tazila. So it is not permissible for the servant to ask God absolutely to turn them away from him. Rather, such a request is only permissible on condition that their removal is beneficial. So it is established that evil in the sense of pain is not permissible for the servant to ask God to turn it away from him.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is the fifteenth proof from the qunut hadith, used to prove divine guidance (hidāyah) and decree (qaḍā') in accordance with Ash'ari doctrine. The author quotes the hadith taught by the Prophet for the witr prayer, then extracts three arguments. First, the plea 'guide me' indicates that guidance is from God, and cannot be mere explanation (bayān) because the Mu'tazila already affirm that, so asking would be redundant. Second, 'take me into Your care' (tawallanī) indicates a special friendship not shared by disbelievers, implying something additional beyond general grace, which is the creation of necessitating motives. Third, 'protect me from the evil of what You have decreed' shows that God decrees evil (sharr) just as He decrees good. The objection then raises two issues: that 'evil' refers to calamities, and that the hadith implies changing God's decree is possible (Mu'tazilite view). The author answers that even if evil means calamities, the Mu'tazila themselves consider them potentially beneficial, so one cannot ask for their removal without condition, thereby neutralizing the objection.

Key Terms
الهداية (guidance)
الولاية (friendship)
القضاء (decree)
الشر (evil)
المصائب (calamities)
دواعي (motives)
الجبرية (Jabariyya/determinists)
المعتزلة (Mu'tazila)
الألطاف (divine graces)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The prayer 'protect me from the evil of what You have decreed' implies that God's decree can be changed by supplication.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that the Mu'tazilite interpretation leads to that conclusion, but the Ash'ari view sees the decree as eternal and unchangeable; the prayer seeks protection from the evil that was already decreed, not its alteration.

Checkpoint
How do the Mu'tazila interpret the word 'sharr' (evil) in the qunut hadith according to the objection?
A) As moral evil
B) As sinful acts
C) As calamities and diseases
D) As the decree of God

Key Takeaway
The qunut hadith provides scriptural support that guidance, divine friendship, and even the decree of evil are all from Allah alone, contradicting Mu'tazilite views.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the qunut prayer, do you genuinely believe that your guidance and wellbeing come entirely from Allah, or do you secretly attribute some of your success to your own effort? How can you train your heart to rely solely on Him?
?
Al-Razi argues that Allah decrees both good and evil. When you face a trial—like illness or loss—do you accept it as from Allah with patience, or do you grumble and question His wisdom? What would it take for you to truly embrace that even the 'evil' you experience is from Him?
?
The Mu'tazila limit 'evil' to calamities, perhaps to avoid attributing moral evil to Allah. Do you ever find yourself subtly denying that Allah is in control of the 'bad' things in your life? How can you cultivate a deep conviction that everything—every joy and every hardship—comes from His decree, and respond with complete submission?

The Witr Prayer Hadith and the First Proof: Guidance from Allah
Hadith citation and first proof against Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith's plea 'guide me' proves that guidance is solely from Allah and cannot be interpreted as merely showing the way.

Core Idea
True guidance is created by Allah, not just shown.

The author begins with a hadith taught for the witr prayer. From its first phrase, he derives a powerful argument against the Mu'tazila, who claimed guidance is merely showing the way. This lesson unpacks that first proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and first proof
Read the Arabic passage of the hadith and the first proof. Notice the wording 'guide me among those You have guided'.
2
Identify the Mu'tazili position
The author states that the Mu'tazila interpret guidance as 'showing the way'. Understand why this is problematic.
3
Analyze the refutation
The author argues that if guidance were merely showing, then it is already attained, making the prayer futile. Thus guidance must be a direct creation from Allah.
This refutes the Mu'tazili view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحسن بن علي ، أنه قال : علمني رسول الله ، كلمات أقولهن في الوتر : اللهم اهدني فيمن هديت ، وعافني فيمن عافيت ، وتولني فيمن توليت وبارك لي فيها أعطيت ، وقني شر ما قضيت. إنك تقضي ولا يقضى عليك . إنه لا يذل من واليت ، تباركت ربنا وتعاليت ، والاستدلال به من وجوه : الأول : إن قوله : ( اللهم اهدني فيمن هديت، يدل على أن الهداية من الله . ولا يمكن حمله على البيان والدلالة . لأن ذلك حاصل عند المعتزلة . وطلب الحاصل عبث . والثاني : إن قوله : ( وتولني فيمن توليت ، يدل على قولنا . لأن ولاية الله تعالى . إن كانت عبارة عن خلق القدرة والآلة ، ووضع الدلائل ، وإزالة الأعذار ، فهذا قد فعله تعالى، في حق الكافر والمؤمن . فهو تعالى ولي الكفار ، وولي المؤمنين جميعاً، بهذا التفسير . والخبر يدل على أنه يتولى أولياء. بأمور لا توجد في حق الكفار . وما ذاك إلا ما ذكرناه من خلق الدواعي الموجبة . والثالث : قوله : « وقني شر ما قضيت، وهذا يدل على أنه تعالى قد يقضي بالشر، كما يقضي بالخير . فإن قيل : الكلام عليه من وجوه : الأول : إنا نحمل هذا الشر على المصائب والأمراض والثاني : إن هذا الكلام يدل على أن تغيير قضاء الله جائز . وذلك هو مذهب المعتزلة . أما على قول الجبرية . فقضاء الله عبارة عن حكمه الأزلي وذلك لا يجوز تغييره . والجواب عن الأول : إن الشر . بمعنى المصائب والآلام . قد يكون مصلحة في حق المكلف عند المعتزلة . فلا يجوز من العبد أن يطلب من الله مطلقاً أن يصرفها عنه . بل إنما يجوز ذلك السؤال ، بشرط أن يكون صرفه عنه مصلحة . فثبت : أن الشر بمعنى الألم لا يجوز للعبد أن يطلب من الله صرفه عنه ، إلا مع شرط كونه مصلحة . وقوله : « وقنا شر ما قضيت، طلب مطلق غير مشروط ، فامتنع أن يكون المراد بهذا الدعاء ما ذكروه . والجواب عن الثاني : إن التكليف بالدعاء ، تكليف بفعل مخصوص ، كسائر التكاليف . وعندنا : أنه ليس لشيء من أفعال العباد تأثير في إيجاب ثواب، أو إيجاب عقاب . فكذا ههنا . والوجه الرابع في الاستدلال بهذا الخبر : قوله : ( فإنك تقضي ولا يقضى عليك ، وهذا صريح مذهبنا في أنه لا يقبح من الله شيء . وليس لأحد على الله حق . ولا يلزمه تعالى ، بسبب أفعال العباد شيء . وكل ذلك يبطل قول المعتزلة . والله أعلم .
Al-Hasan ibn Ali narrated that the Messenger of Allah taught me words to say in the witr prayer: 'O Allah, guide me among those You have guided, grant me well-being among those You have granted well-being, take me into Your care among those You have taken into Your care, bless me in what You have given, and protect me from the evil of what You have decreed. Indeed, You decree and nothing is decreed against You. Indeed, he whom You take as a friend is not humiliated. Blessed are You, our Lord, and exalted.' Extracting proofs from it has aspects: First: His saying 'O Allah, guide me among those You have guided' indicates that guidance is from Allah. It cannot be interpreted as showing the way (al-bayan wa al-dalala) because that is already attained among the Mu'tazila, and seeking what is attained is futile. Second: His saying 'take me into Your care among those You have taken into Your care' indicates our position because the friendship (wilaya) of Allah—if it is interpreted as creating ability and means, setting up evidence, and removing excuses—then He has done that for both the disbeliever and the believer. Thus He is the friend of disbelievers and of all believers according to this interpretation. But the hadith indicates that He takes into His care friends with matters not found in the case of disbelievers. That is nothing but what we mentioned: the creation of compelling motives (al-dawa'i al-mujiba). Third: His saying 'protect me from the evil of what You have decreed' indicates that He decrees evil just as He decrees good. If it is said: The discussion on it has aspects: First: We interpret this evil as calamities and diseases. Second: This statement indicates that changing Allah's decree is permissible, which is the position of the Mu'tazila. As for the position of the Jabriyya, Allah's decree is His eternal judgment, which cannot be changed. The answer to the first: Evil in the sense of calamities and pains may be beneficial for the responsible person according to the Mu'tazila. Thus it is not permissible for the servant to ask Allah absolutely to avert them from himself. Rather, such a request is only permitted on condition that averting it is beneficial. So it is established that evil in the sense of pain is not permissible for the servant to ask Allah to avert it from himself except with the condition that it be beneficial. And His saying 'protect us from the evil of what You have decreed' is an absolute request without condition, so it is impossible that what they mentioned is intended by this supplication. The answer to the second: The obligation of supplication is an obligation of a specific act like other obligations. And according to us, none of the acts of servants have any effect in necessitating reward or punishment. So likewise here. The fourth aspect of proof from this hadith: His saying 'Indeed, You decree and nothing is decreed against You' is explicit in our position that nothing is considered bad from Allah, no one has a right over Allah, and nothing is incumbent upon Him due to the acts of servants. All of that invalidates the position of the Mu'tazila. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage presents a kalam argument from a prophetic hadith. The author first cites the hadith taught for the witr prayer. Then he derives four proofs (wujuh) from it to refute Mu'tazili doctrines. The first proof: The plea 'guide me' shows guidance comes only from Allah, not merely showing the way, since Mu'tazila already claim that guidance is from themselves. The second proof: 'Take me into your care' implies a special friendship beyond what is common to believer and disbeliever, refuting the Mu'tazili interpretation of wilaya as mere provision of ability and evidence. The third proof: 'Protect me from the evil of what You have decreed' affirms that Allah decrees evil, not just good. An objection is then raised with two points: (1) the evil refers to calamities, not moral evil; (2) the prayer implies changing the decree, which Mu'tazila allow but Jabriyya deny. The author answers: (1) Even calamities may be beneficial, so one cannot ask for their removal unconditionally; but the hadith makes an absolute request, showing it refers to moral evil. (2) Obligation to pray does not entail human power to change the decree; it is a test like other commands. The fourth proof: 'You decree and nothing is decreed against You' establishes that no act is bad from Allah and no one has a right against Him, refuting Mu'tazili notions of divine justice (wujub). The author concludes that all these points invalidate Mu'tazili teachings.

Key Terms
هداية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That guidance is merely guidance through reason or prophets and humans choose to follow it.
Correction: The hadith shows that guidance is a direct creation by Allah, not just showing the way, as seeking what is already attained is futile.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, why cannot the word 'guidance' in the hadith be interpreted as merely showing the way?
A) Because the Mu'tazila already have that guidance.
B) Because the hadith explicitly says guidance is from Allah.
C) Because seeking what is already attained is futile.
D) Both A and C.

Key Takeaway
The first proof from the witr prayer hadith establishes that guidance is exclusively from Allah, not merely showing the way.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray 'guide me' in your witr prayer, do you truly believe that without Allah's direct creation of guidance in your heart, you would not even desire to obey Him? If so, how does that change your dependence on your own efforts to be righteous?
?
The Mu'tazila thought they already had guidance through reason and revelation, yet the Prophet still taught this dua. In your own life, where do you assume you already have enough guidance, and how does that assumption keep you from desperately asking Allah to actually create guidance in your heart?

Second Proof: Allah's Special Friendship (Wilaya)
Second proof from the hadith against Mu'tazili concept of wilaya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the phrase 'take me into Your care among those You have taken into Your care' proves that Allah grants a special friendship to believers that goes beyond general provision.

Core Idea
Allah's friendship for believers is special, not common to all.

The second proof focuses on the phrase 'take me into Your care'. The author argues that if Allah's friendship (wilaya) were merely providing ability and evidence, it would apply to all, but the hadith implies a special friendship for believers only. This lesson explains that special friendship is the creation of compelling motives to good.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof
Read the Arabic passage for the second proof. Identify the key phrase 'take me into Your care'.
2
Understand the Mu'tazili interpretation
The Mu'tazila interpret wilaya as creating ability, means, evidence, and removing excuses. This would apply equally to believers and disbelievers.
3
Contrast with the hadith
The hadith shows that there is a special friendship for some, not all. The author says this special friendship is the creation of 'compelling motives' (dawa'i mujiba) that lead people to good deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If Allah's wilaya were only external blessings like health and wealth, would you be satisfied? Examine your heart: do you long for that inner transformation that makes obedience sweet, or do you only want the external? How would your life change if you sought that internal attraction?
?
The hadith shows that there is a special group whom Allah takes into His care. What if you are not among them? What fear does that stir in you? And what hope does the promise of 'compelling motives' give you to change your ways starting today?

Third Proof: Allah Decrees Evil and the Objections
Third proof from the hadith with objections and answers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the phrase 'protect me from the evil of what You have decreed' proves that Allah decrees evil, and how the author responds to Mu'tazili objections.

Core Idea
Allah decrees both good and evil, and prayer does not change His decree.

The third proof from the hadith asserts that Allah decrees evil as well as good. The author then addresses two objections: that 'evil' means calamities, and that the prayer implies changing the decree. This lesson walks through the proof and its defense.

Guided Path
1
Read the third proof and objections
Read the Arabic passage for the third proof, including the two objections and the author's answers.
2
Understand the proof
The phrase 'protect us from the evil of what You have decreed' shows that Allah decrees evil, because one asks for protection from it.
3
Examine the first objection and answer
Objection: 'evil' here refers to calamities. Answer: Even calamities may be beneficial, so an absolute request to remove them is not allowed unless conditional; the hadith makes an absolute request, so it must refer to moral evil.
4
Examine the second objection and answer
Objection: The prayer implies changing the decree, which the Mu'tazila accept but Jabriyya reject. Answer: The obligation to pray is a test; human acts do not affect reward or punishment directly according to the author's school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحسن بن علي ، أنه قال : علمني رسول الله ، كلمات أقولهن في الوتر : اللهم اهدني فيمن هديت ، وعافني فيمن عافيت ، وتولني فيمن توليت وبارك لي فيها أعطيت ، وقني شر ما قضيت. إنك تقضي ولا يقضى عليك . إنه لا يذل من واليت ، تباركت ربنا وتعاليت ، والاستدلال به من وجوه : الأول : إن قوله : ( اللهم اهدني فيمن هديت، يدل على أن الهداية من الله . ولا يمكن حمله على البيان والدلالة . لأن ذلك حاصل عند المعتزلة . وطلب الحاصل عبث . والثاني : إن قوله : ( وتولني فيمن توليت ، يدل على قولنا . لأن ولاية الله تعالى . إن كانت عبارة عن خلق القدرة والآلة ، ووضع الدلائل ، وإزالة الأعذار ، فهذا قد فعله تعالى، في حق الكافر والمؤمن . فهو تعالى ولي الكفار ، وولي المؤمنين جميعاً، بهذا التفسير . والخبر يدل على أنه يتولى أولياء. بأمور لا توجد في حق الكفار . وما ذاك إلا ما ذكرناه من خلق الدواعي الموجبة . والثالث : قوله : « وقني شر ما قضيت، وهذا يدل على أنه تعالى قد يقضي بالشر، كما يقضي بالخير . فإن قيل : الكلام عليه من وجوه : الأول : إنا نحمل هذا الشر على المصائب والأمراض والثاني : إن هذا الكلام يدل على أن تغيير قضاء الله جائز . وذلك هو مذهب المعتزلة . أما على قول الجبرية . فقضاء الله عبارة عن حكمه الأزلي وذلك لا يجوز تغييره . والجواب عن الأول : إن الشر . بمعنى المصائب والآلام . قد يكون مصلحة في حق المكلف عند المعتزلة . فلا يجوز من العبد أن يطلب من الله مطلقاً أن يصرفها عنه . بل إنما يجوز ذلك السؤال ، بشرط أن يكون صرفه عنه مصلحة . فثبت : أن الشر بمعنى الألم لا يجوز للعبد أن يطلب من الله صرفه عنه ، إلا مع شرط كونه مصلحة . وقوله : « وقنا شر ما قضيت، طلب مطلق غير مشروط ، فامتنع أن يكون المراد بهذا الدعاء ما ذكروه . والجواب عن الثاني : إن التكليف بالدعاء ، تكليف بفعل مخصوص ، كسائر التكاليف . وعندنا : أنه ليس لشيء من أفعال العباد تأثير في إيجاب ثواب، أو إيجاب عقاب . فكذا ههنا . والوجه الرابع في الاستدلال بهذا الخبر : قوله : ( فإنك تقضي ولا يقضى عليك ، وهذا صريح مذهبنا في أنه لا يقبح من الله شيء . وليس لأحد على الله حق . ولا يلزمه تعالى ، بسبب أفعال العباد شيء . وكل ذلك يبطل قول المعتزلة . والله أعلم .
Al-Hasan ibn Ali narrated that the Messenger of Allah taught me words to say in the witr prayer: 'O Allah, guide me among those You have guided, grant me well-being among those You have granted well-being, take me into Your care among those You have taken into Your care, bless me in what You have given, and protect me from the evil of what You have decreed. Indeed, You decree and nothing is decreed against You. Indeed, he whom You take as a friend is not humiliated. Blessed are You, our Lord, and exalted.' Extracting proofs from it has aspects: First: His saying 'O Allah, guide me among those You have guided' indicates that guidance is from Allah. It cannot be interpreted as showing the way (al-bayan wa al-dalala) because that is already attained among the Mu'tazila, and seeking what is attained is futile. Second: His saying 'take me into Your care among those You have taken into Your care' indicates our position because the friendship (wilaya) of Allah—if it is interpreted as creating ability and means, setting up evidence, and removing excuses—then He has done that for both the disbeliever and the believer. Thus He is the friend of disbelievers and of all believers according to this interpretation. But the hadith indicates that He takes into His care friends with matters not found in the case of disbelievers. That is nothing but what we mentioned: the creation of compelling motives (al-dawa'i al-mujiba). Third: His saying 'protect me from the evil of what You have decreed' indicates that He decrees evil just as He decrees good. If it is said: The discussion on it has aspects: First: We interpret this evil as calamities and diseases. Second: This statement indicates that changing Allah's decree is permissible, which is the position of the Mu'tazila. As for the position of the Jabriyya, Allah's decree is His eternal judgment, which cannot be changed. The answer to the first: Evil in the sense of calamities and pains may be beneficial for the responsible person according to the Mu'tazila. Thus it is not permissible for the servant to ask Allah absolutely to avert them from himself. Rather, such a request is only permitted on condition that averting it is beneficial. So it is established that evil in the sense of pain is not permissible for the servant to ask Allah to avert it from himself except with the condition that it be beneficial. And His saying 'protect us from the evil of what You have decreed' is an absolute request without condition, so it is impossible that what they mentioned is intended by this supplication. The answer to the second: The obligation of supplication is an obligation of a specific act like other obligations. And according to us, none of the acts of servants have any effect in necessitating reward or punishment. So likewise here. The fourth aspect of proof from this hadith: His saying 'Indeed, You decree and nothing is decreed against You' is explicit in our position that nothing is considered bad from Allah, no one has a right over Allah, and nothing is incumbent upon Him due to the acts of servants. All of that invalidates the position of the Mu'tazila. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage presents a kalam argument from a prophetic hadith. The author first cites the hadith taught for the witr prayer. Then he derives four proofs (wujuh) from it to refute Mu'tazili doctrines. The first proof: The plea 'guide me' shows guidance comes only from Allah, not merely showing the way, since Mu'tazila already claim that guidance is from themselves. The second proof: 'Take me into your care' implies a special friendship beyond what is common to believer and disbeliever, refuting the Mu'tazili interpretation of wilaya as mere provision of ability and evidence. The third proof: 'Protect me from the evil of what You have decreed' affirms that Allah decrees evil, not just good. An objection is then raised with two points: (1) the evil refers to calamities, not moral evil; (2) the prayer implies changing the decree, which Mu'tazila allow but Jabriyya deny. The author answers: (1) Even calamities may be beneficial, so one cannot ask for their removal unconditionally; but the hadith makes an absolute request, showing it refers to moral evil. (2) Obligation to pray does not entail human power to change the decree; it is a test like other commands. The fourth proof: 'You decree and nothing is decreed against You' establishes that no act is bad from Allah and no one has a right against Him, refuting Mu'tazili notions of divine justice (wujub). The author concludes that all these points invalidate Mu'tazili teachings.

Key Terms
شر
قضاء
دعاء
تكليف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That evil in the hadith refers only to calamities, not moral evil, and that prayer can change God's eternal decree.
Correction: The hadith's absolute request shows it is moral evil, and prayer does not change the decree; it is an act of worship.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that the 'evil' in the hadith cannot refer to calamities?
A) Because calamities are not evil.
B) Because the request to be protected from calamities is unconditional, but Mu'tazila say one can only ask conditionally.
C) Because the hadith specifically mentions 'evil of decree'.
D) Because calamities are from Satan.

Key Takeaway
The third proof affirms that Allah decrees evil, and the prayer for protection does not change His decree but is an act of obedience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a calamity, do you pray for it to be lifted with the attitude that Allah must remove it because it's 'evil', or do you submit to His decree, trusting that it may be beneficial? How does this lesson challenge the way you speak to Allah in hardship?
?
Have you ever assumed that your du'a 'changed' what was written for you? If prayer does not alter the decree, what is its true purpose according to this passage? How does that affect your sincerity and reliance on Allah alone?
?
The author affirms that Allah decrees both good and evil, including moral evil. Does this make you less vigilant against sin, thinking it's already decreed? How does this passage call you to take responsibility for your actions while affirming Allah's absolute sovereignty? What is the balance?

Divine Decree
beginner
3 min
Fourth Proof: Allah's Absolute Sovereignty
Fourth proof from the hadith refuting Mu'tazila on divine justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the phrase 'You decree and nothing is decreed against You' establishes that nothing is bad from Allah and no one has a right against Him, refuting Mu'tazili notions of justice.

Core Idea
Allah is sovereign; nothing is imposed on Him.

The fourth and final proof from the hadith is short but powerful. The phrase 'You decree and nothing is decreed against You' is used to establish the Ash'ari position that nothing is inherently bad from Allah and that no one has a claim against Him. This directly challenges the Mu'tazili doctrine of divine justice (wujub).

Guided Path
1
Read the fourth proof
Read the Arabic passage for the fourth proof. Notice the phrase 'You decree and nothing is decreed against You'.
2
Identify the implications
The author states that this phrase implies: nothing is considered bad from Allah, no one has a right over Allah, and nothing is incumbent upon Him due to acts of servants.
3
Connect to Mu'tazili refutation
These implications directly oppose the Mu'tazili doctrine that good and evil are rational categories binding on Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحسن بن علي ، أنه قال : علمني رسول الله ، كلمات أقولهن في الوتر : اللهم اهدني فيمن هديت ، وعافني فيمن عافيت ، وتولني فيمن توليت وبارك لي فيها أعطيت ، وقني شر ما قضيت. إنك تقضي ولا يقضى عليك . إنه لا يذل من واليت ، تباركت ربنا وتعاليت ، والاستدلال به من وجوه : الأول : إن قوله : ( اللهم اهدني فيمن هديت، يدل على أن الهداية من الله . ولا يمكن حمله على البيان والدلالة . لأن ذلك حاصل عند المعتزلة . وطلب الحاصل عبث . والثاني : إن قوله : ( وتولني فيمن توليت ، يدل على قولنا . لأن ولاية الله تعالى . إن كانت عبارة عن خلق القدرة والآلة ، ووضع الدلائل ، وإزالة الأعذار ، فهذا قد فعله تعالى، في حق الكافر والمؤمن . فهو تعالى ولي الكفار ، وولي المؤمنين جميعاً، بهذا التفسير . والخبر يدل على أنه يتولى أولياء. بأمور لا توجد في حق الكفار . وما ذاك إلا ما ذكرناه من خلق الدواعي الموجبة . والثالث : قوله : « وقني شر ما قضيت، وهذا يدل على أنه تعالى قد يقضي بالشر، كما يقضي بالخير . فإن قيل : الكلام عليه من وجوه : الأول : إنا نحمل هذا الشر على المصائب والأمراض والثاني : إن هذا الكلام يدل على أن تغيير قضاء الله جائز . وذلك هو مذهب المعتزلة . أما على قول الجبرية . فقضاء الله عبارة عن حكمه الأزلي وذلك لا يجوز تغييره . والجواب عن الأول : إن الشر . بمعنى المصائب والآلام . قد يكون مصلحة في حق المكلف عند المعتزلة . فلا يجوز من العبد أن يطلب من الله مطلقاً أن يصرفها عنه . بل إنما يجوز ذلك السؤال ، بشرط أن يكون صرفه عنه مصلحة . فثبت : أن الشر بمعنى الألم لا يجوز للعبد أن يطلب من الله صرفه عنه ، إلا مع شرط كونه مصلحة . وقوله : « وقنا شر ما قضيت، طلب مطلق غير مشروط ، فامتنع أن يكون المراد بهذا الدعاء ما ذكروه . والجواب عن الثاني : إن التكليف بالدعاء ، تكليف بفعل مخصوص ، كسائر التكاليف . وعندنا : أنه ليس لشيء من أفعال العباد تأثير في إيجاب ثواب، أو إيجاب عقاب . فكذا ههنا . والوجه الرابع في الاستدلال بهذا الخبر : قوله : ( فإنك تقضي ولا يقضى عليك ، وهذا صريح مذهبنا في أنه لا يقبح من الله شيء . وليس لأحد على الله حق . ولا يلزمه تعالى ، بسبب أفعال العباد شيء . وكل ذلك يبطل قول المعتزلة . والله أعلم .

Commentary
This passage presents a kalam argument from a prophetic hadith. The author first cites the hadith taught for the witr prayer. Then he derives four proofs (wujuh) from it to refute Mu'tazili doctrines. Correction: The hadith shows that nothing is decreed against Allah; He is sovereign and not bound by human conceptions of justice.

?

Divine Decree
intermediate

Hadith of Moses and the Samaritan as Proof of Divine Decree
Hadith about Moses and the Samaritan cited as proof, followed by al-Ka'bi's objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of Moses and the Samaritan is used as a proof for divine decree, and the first objection raised by al-Ka'bi.

Core Idea
Even the Samaritan's misguidance is ultimately from Allah.

The author presents a hadith in which Moses swears that only Allah led his people astray, even though the Samaritan made the calf. This hadith is used to support the Ash'ari view that all actions, including misguidance, are created by Allah. Then al-Ka'bi, a Mu'tazili scholar, objects that the hadith contradicts the Quran and is therefore weak. This passage introduces a key proof and the first line of theological critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith narrative
Read the hadith carefully, noting the dialogue between Moses and Allah. Identify how Moses concludes that only Allah misguides.
The hadith is presented as the sixteenth proof.
2
Understand the proof for divine decree
Notice how the author uses Moses's statement 'none other than You led my people astray' to argue that all misguidance is from Allah. This supports the Ash'ari position.
3
Examine al-Ka'bi's objection
Al-Ka'bi declares the hadith weak because it contradicts the Quranic verse 'the Samaritan led them astray'. He argues that the hadith implies Allah misled them, which would be accusing Allah of lying.
This is the first of several objections al-Ka'bi raises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة عشر : ما رواه الزهري عن عبد الرحمن بن كعب بن أبيه ، قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ( إن الله تعالى لما وعد موسى ان يكلمه ، خرج في الوقت الذي وعده الله ، قال : « فبينا هو يناجي ربه ، إذ خلفه صوتاً . فقال : اللهم اسمع خلفي صوتاً . لعل قومي ضلوا قال : نعم يا موسى . قال : إلهي . فمن أضلهم ؟ فقال : أضلهم السامري . قال : إلهي . فيم أضلهم ؟ قال : صاغ لهم عجلاً جسداً ، له خوار . قال : إلهي . هذا السامري ، صاغ لهم العجل ، فمن نفخ فيه الروح ، حتى صار له خوار ؟ قال : أنا يا موسى . قال : فوعزتك يا إلهي . ما أضل قومي غيرك قال : صدقت يا حكيم الحكماء . لا ينبغي الحكيم أن يكون أحكم منك . . قال الكعبي في بعض تصانيفه : هذا الخبر ضعيف ، وبيانه من وجوه : الأول : إن هذا الخبر ، اشتمل على تكذيب الله . لأنه تعالى قال : وأضلهم السامري (۱) ) والحديث دل على أن موسى حلف بعزة الله : أنه ما اضلهم غير الله . وإذا كان المضل هو الله ، فالسامري لا يكون مضلا لهم ، مع
The sixteenth proof: What al-Zuhri narrated from Abd al-Rahman ibn Ka'b ibn Abi, who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When Allah Almighty promised to speak to Moses, he set out at the time Allah had promised him. He said: While he was conversing with his Lord, suddenly a sound came from behind him. He said: O Allah, I hear a sound behind me. Perhaps my people have gone astray. He said: Yes, O Moses. He said: My God, who led them astray? He said: The Samaritan led them astray. He said: My God, in what did he lead them astray? He said: He fashioned for them a calf, a body with a lowing sound. He said: My God, this Samaritan fashioned the calf, then who breathed the spirit into it until it had a lowing sound? He said: I did, O Moses. He said: So by Your might, my God, none other than You led my people astray. He said: You have spoken the truth, O wisest of the wise. It is not fitting that the wise be wiser than you.' Al-Ka'bi said in some of his works: This hadith is weak, and its explanation has aspects: First: This hadith includes accusing Allah of lying, because He said 'And the Samaritan led them astray' (Surah Taha 85), while the hadith indicates that Moses swore by Allah's might that none other than Allah led them astray. If the misguider is Allah, then the Samaritan is not a misguider for them, along with...
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage presents the sixteenth proof (hujja) from a hadith about Moses and the Samaritan. The hadith recounts that after Allah promised to speak to Moses, Moses heard a sound and feared his people had gone astray. Allah confirmed that the Samaritan led them astray. Moses then questioned how the Samaritan could have done so, pointing out that Allah had breathed the spirit into the calf, making it low. Moses concluded that only Allah could truly misguide, and Allah affirmed his words. This hadith is used to support the Ash'ari position that all acts—including misguidance—are created by Allah. The author then cites al-Ka'bi, a Mu'tazili scholar, who declares the hadith weak. Al-Ka'bi's first objection is that the hadith contradicts the Quranic verse (20:85) which attributes the misguidance to the Samaritan. According to al-Ka'bi, the hadith implies that Allah misled them, thereby denying the Samaritan's role, which would be accusing Allah of lying. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument continues in later pages.

Key Terms

تكذيب
حديث ضعيف
سامري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Ka'bi, why is the hadith of Moses and the Samaritan weak?
A) Because the chain of narration is broken
B) Because it contradicts the Quranic verse that says the Samaritan led them astray
C) Because it claims Moses doubted Allah
D) Because it is not found in any authentic collection

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Moses and the Samaritan is used to argue that Allah creates all acts, including misguidance, but al-Ka'bi objects that it contradicts the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When Moses realized that only Allah could lead his people astray, he swore by Allah's might. Does this truth make you more humble about your own mistakes, knowing that even your wrong choices are ultimately under Allah's control? Or does it make you complacent? How will you change your attitude toward sin and repentance today?
?
Al-Ka'bi rejected this hadith because it seemed to contradict the Quran. When you encounter a religious text that challenges your understanding, do you submit or resist? Are you willing to accept that Allah's wisdom may be beyond your comprehension? What will you do the next time you face a difficult verse or hadith?
?
The Samaritan was the tool, but Allah created the calf's lowing. If you truly believe that every act—good or evil—is created by Allah, does that lead you to rely more on Him for guidance? Or do you still act as if you are independent? Before you go to sleep tonight, examine one area where you need to increase your reliance on Allah.

The Hadith Proof: Tawfiq Necessitates the Deed
Proof from hadith that tawfiq necessitates the righteous deed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a hadith about divine tawfiq proves that God's grant of success necessitates the righteous deed, supporting the Ash'ari view on human action.

Core Idea
Tawfiq is not just help; it makes the deed inevitable.

This lesson examines the seventeenth proof from a hadith narrated by Anas. The proof uses the concept of tawfiq (divine success) to argue that when God wants good for a servant, He grants him success to perform a righteous deed, and this success necessarily leads to the act. The hadith's language shows that mentioning the cause (tawfiq) suffices for the effect (the deed), because tawfiq establishes the preponderant motive that necessitates action.

Guided Path
1
Read the Hadith and Translation
Read the Arabic text of the hadith and its literal translation. Notice the key phrase 'yuwaffiquhu li-'amal salih' (grants him success to a righteous deed).
2
Define Tawfiq
According to the passage, tawfiq is the preponderance (tarjih) of the motive for righteousness over the motive for corruption in the heart. Understand that this is an internal state given by God.
3
Analyze the Logical Inference
The hadith only mentions tawfiq, not the actual deed. Why? Because when tawfiq occurs, the deed becomes necessary (wajib). Thus mentioning the cause suffices for the effect.
4
Consider the Counterfactual
Imagine if the deed could lag behind tawfiq. Then the hadith would have to specify whether the deed actually occurred. Since it does not, the necessity is proven.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة عشر : ما روى أنس . أن النبي عليه السلام قال : ( إذا أراد الله بعبد خيراً ، استعمله ، قيل : فكيف يستعمله يا رسول الله ؟ قال : يوفقه لعمل صالح قبل الموت ) ووجه الاستدلال بهذا الخبر : هو أن هذا مذهبنا في أن قدرة العبد إن كانت صالحة للعمل الصالح وللعمل الفاسد . فذلك التوفيق ، عبارة عن ترجيح داعية الصلاح على داعية الفساد في قلبه . ثم إنه تعالى اكتفى بذكر هذا التوفيق عن وقوع ذلك العمل الصالح لأن عند حصول هذا التوفيق يكون حصول الفعل واجباً ، فاستغنى بذكر السبب عن ذكر المسبب . ولو كان تخلف الفعل عن حصول هذا التوفيق ممكناً ، لكان من الواجب أن لا يكتفي بذكر هذا التوفيق عن حصول ذلك الفعل . بل كان ينبغي أن يذكر أن ذلك الفعل . هل حصل أم لا ؟
The seventeenth proof: What Anas narrated: that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'When Allah wants good for a servant, He employs him.' It was said: 'How does He employ him, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'He grants him success (yuwaffiquhu) to a righteous deed before death.' The aspect of inference from this report is that this is our doctrine that the servant's power, if it is suitable for righteous deed and for corrupt deed, then that tawfiq (divine granting of success) is an expression of the preponderance of the motive (dā'iyya) of righteousness over the motive of corruption in his heart. Then He, exalted, sufficed with mentioning this tawfiq instead of the occurrence of that righteous deed, because when this tawfiq occurs, the occurrence of the act becomes necessary (wājib). So He sufficed with mentioning the cause instead of the effect. And if it were possible for the act to lag behind the occurrence of this tawfiq, it would have been necessary not to suffice with mentioning this tawfiq instead of the occurrence of that act. Rather, it would have been necessary to mention whether that act occurred or not.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage presents the seventeenth proof for the Ash'ari position on human action, based on a hadith. The proof uses the concept of tawfiq (divine grant of success). The hadith states that when God wants good for a servant, He 'employs him' by granting him success (yuwaffiquhu) to perform a righteous deed before death. The author explains that according to the Ash'ari school, the servant's power (qudra) is equally capable of good and evil. Tawfiq is defined as the preponderance (tarjīḥ) of the motive (dā'iyya) for righteousness over the motive for corruption in the heart. The key point: the hadith mentions only tawfiq, not the actual deed, implying that tawfiq necessarily leads to the deed. If it were possible for the deed not to occur despite tawfiq, then mentioning tawfiq alone would be insufficient; the hadith would have to specify whether the deed actually happened. Since the hadith does not, it proves that tawfiq necessitates the action. This supports the Ash'ari view that when God gives tawfiq, the act inevitably follows, because the combination of power and motive (here, the preponderant motive) necessitates the act.

Key Terms
توفيق
ترجيح داعية الصلاح
سبب
مسبب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tawfiq is merely an external aid that the servant can accept or reject.
Correction: The passage shows tawfiq is an internal preponderance (tarjih) of the motive for righteousness, which makes the act necessary. It is not an external aid that the servant can choose to ignore.

Checkpoint
According to the seventeenth proof, why does the hadith mention only tawfiq and not the actual righteous deed?
A) Because the deed is less important than tawfiq.
B) Because tawfiq necessarily entails the deed, so mentioning the cause suffices.
C) Because the deed may or may not occur, so it is left ambiguous.
D) Because the hadith is incomplete and the deed is implied.

Key Takeaway
Tawfiq is the internal preponderance of the motive for good, and its mention alone in the hadith proves that it necessarily leads to the righteous deed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you truly attribute it to Allah's tawfiq, or do you silently credit your own effort? What would change in your prayer if you genuinely believed the deed was inevitable only through His grant?
?
Consider a sin you struggle with. The lesson says tawfiq makes the righteous deed necessary. Does that mean you are excused if you lack tawfiq? Or does it demand that you seek it more earnestly? What action will you take today to seek tawfiq?
?
If tawfiq is the preponderance of the motive for good, what motives for sin still dominate your heart? What does that reveal about your need for divine intervention, and what step will you take right now to invite His preponderance?

The Hadith on Creation for Paradise or Hell
Proof from hadith that God created some for Paradise and some for Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'aris use this hadith as a proof for predestination and why the opponent's metaphorical interpretation is rejected.

Core Idea
God's creation for Paradise or Hell is not just foreknowledge—it is His actual will.

This short passage presents a powerful prophetic hadith in which God declares that He created certain people for Paradise and others for Hell, without any concern for their apparent deeds. This hadith is a key proof for the Ash'ari doctrine of qadar. However, opponents interpret it as mere knowledge or inscription. Let's examine the text and its implications for theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
First, read the Arabic text of the hadith and its literal translation. Notice the explicit words 'I created these for Paradise, and I care not, and I created these for the Fire, and I care not.' This sets the stage for the proof.
The emphasis is on God's creative act directly linked to final destiny, not on human action.
2
Understand the proof for predestination
Think about why this hadith is considered a proof for predestination. If God creates someone specifically for Paradise, then that person's ultimate destination is determined by God's will alone, not by their deeds. This supports the Ash'ari view that God's will is decisive.
The Ash'aris use this to argue that human actions are acquired (kasb) but not the ultimate cause of salvation.
3
Analyze the opponent's interpretation
The author mentions that opponents interpret the hadith as referring to God's foreknowledge or the writing in the Preserved Tablet. Reflect on why this interpretation weakens the proof—if it is only about knowledge, it does not necessarily indicate actual creation for that purpose. The author says the answer has already been given, implying the literal meaning stands.
This step connects to the broader debate between predestination and free will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة عشر : قوله عليه السلام ، حكاية عن رب العزة : خلقت هؤلاء للجنة ، ولا أبالي ، وخلقت هؤلاء للنار ، ولا أبالي . والخصوم حملوه على العلم ، أو على الكتابة في اللوح المحفوظ . وقد سبق جوابه .
The eighteenth proof: His saying, peace be upon him, narrating from the Lord of Might: 'I created these for Paradise, and I care not, and I created these for the Fire, and I care not.' And the opponents interpret it as referring to knowledge, or to the writing in the Preserved Tablet. And its answer has preceded.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This short passage presents the eighteenth proof, which is a hadith qudsi where God says He created some people for Paradise and some for Hell, and He does not care. This hadith is used by Ash'aris to support predestination — that God's will determines who goes to Paradise or Hell. The author notes that opponents (likely Mu'tazilites or others who affirm free will) interpret this hadith metaphorically: they say it refers to God's foreknowledge (that He knows who will end up where) or to the inscription in the Preserved Tablet (al-lawḥ al-maḥfūẓ) that records what will happen. The author states that the answer to this interpretation has already been given earlier in the work (not provided here), implying that the literal meaning is the correct one and that the opponents' interpretation is rejected.

Key Terms
خلقت هؤلاء للجنة
العلم
الكتابة في اللوح المحفوظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this hadith denies human responsibility entirely, making human effort meaningless.
Correction: Ash'aris argue that while God creates the person for a destiny, human actions are acquired (kasb) and are the means by which destiny is realized, preserving moral responsibility.

Checkpoint
How do the opponents interpret the hadith 'I created these for Paradise, and I care not'?
A) As a literal decree of creation for Paradise.
B) As referring to God's knowledge or writing in the Preserved Tablet.
C) As a mere figure of speech with no meaning.
D) As a command rather than a creation.

Key Takeaway
The hadith that God creates some for Paradise and some for Hell serves as a direct scriptural proof for predestination, and its literal meaning is defended against metaphorical reinterpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you ponder that God created some for Hell, how does that change how you view your own salvation? Are you relying on your deeds or on God's mercy? Write down one specific prayer you will say tonight asking God to write you among the people of Paradise.
?
The hadith says 'I care not'—God's will is independent of human merit. Does that comfort you or disturb you? What does that say about how much you truly trust His decree? Commit to one act of submission today that shows you accept His judgment even when you don't understand it.
?
If this hadith is not just about God knowing who will go to Hell but about Him creating them for it, how should that affect your attitude toward non-Muslims? Does it increase your urgency to call them to faith, or your humility knowing that guidance is from God alone? Name one person you will reach out to this week to share a word of da'wah.

The Nineteenth Proof: Protection from Sin Comes from God's Tawfiq
Proof from hadith that protection (wiqāya) is divinely bestowed, with a response to the alṭāf objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a hadith about protection (wiqāya) is used as evidence that God's tawfiq is the cause of sinlessness, and how the Ash'ari response to the objection of alṭāf reinforces the determinative nature of God's grace.

Core Idea
Protection from sin is attributed to God, not the servant, proving tawfiq is decisive.

This lesson examines the nineteenth proof from al-Maṭālib al-ʿĀliya, which cites a famous hadith to argue that protection from sin comes solely from God's tawfiq. The passage includes an objection from those who interpret the protection as merely 'graces' (alṭāf) and the author's rebuttal, though the argument is cut short. Despite the incompleteness, we can grasp the core evidence and the intended logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its implication
Read the Arabic and translation of the hadith portion. Notice that the passive verb 'wuqiya' attributes protection to an external agent.
2
Identify the argument's flow
The author argues: hadith shows protection is from other than servant → that other is Allah → so servant remains sinless only by God's tawfiq.
3
Understand the objection and the start of the answer
Opponents say it means divine graces; author answers that God already did all possible alṭāf, and luṭf must be a preponderator. Consider why this rebuttal matters.
The argument continues but is cut off; think about what a preponderator implies.
4
Reflect on the cut-off
The argument is incomplete; we can speculate that the full answer would argue that a preponderator necessarily brings about its effect, so if God gives the grace, it must determine the act.
This speculation is based on the logic of the words 'murajjiḥ' and the necessity of its effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة عشر : ما روى أبو حازم، عن أبي هريرة - رضي الله عنه ـ قال : قال رسول الله : ( من وقى الذي بين لحييه ورجليه دخل الجنة ) النص : دل على أن تلك الوقاية مضافة إلى غير العبد . وما ذاك إلا الله تعالى. وهذا يدل على أن العبد إنما يبقى مصوناً عن المعاصي بتوفيق الله . قالوا : المراد منه : الألطاف ، وجوابنا : إن كل ما قدر الله عليه من الألطاف ، فقد فعله . وأيضاً : اللطيف لا بد وأن يكون مرجحاً ، وكل مرجح ...
The nineteenth proof: What Abu Hazim narrated, from Abu Hurayra - may Allah be pleased with him - said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever is protected from what is between his jaws and between his legs will enter Paradise.' The text indicates that that protection (wiqāya) is attributed to other than the servant. And that is none other than Allah Almighty. And this indicates that the servant only remains protected from sins by the tawfiq of Allah. They said: What is meant by it is the 'alṭāf' (divine graces). Our answer: Indeed everything that Allah is capable of in terms of alṭāf, He has done. And also: al-Luṭf (the grace) must be a preponderator, and every preponderator...
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage presents the nineteenth proof, a hadith stating that whoever is protected (wuqiya) from the mouth (what is between the jaws) and the private parts (what is between the legs) will enter Paradise. The author argues that the phrase 'whoever is protected' (man wuqiya) uses a passive verb indicating that the protection comes from an external agent, not the servant himself. That agent is Allah alone. Therefore, the servant remains sinless only through God's tawfiq (divine success). The opponents object that what is meant by this protection is al-alṭāf (divine graces), which are aids that do not compel but facilitate. The author's answer (though cut off) is that God has already done everything He is capable of in terms of alṭāf, and that al-luṭf must be a preponderator (murajjiḥ) — meaning it tips the balance so that the act becomes necessary. The argument seems to be that if God's grace (luṭf) is given, it must have an effect, otherwise it would be pointless. The cut-off phrase 'and every preponderator' likely continues to argue that a preponderator must lead to its effect.

Key Terms
وقاية
ألطاف
لطيف
مرجح
توفيق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's protection is merely an external aid that the human can accept or reject.
Correction: The Ash'ari view insists it is a determinative grace that necessitates the act, as indicated by the claim that al-luṭf must be a preponderator.

Checkpoint
According to the nineteenth proof, to whom is the protection from sin attributed?
A) To the servant himself through his own will.
B) To the servant through his good deeds.
C) To God alone through His tawfiq.
D) To the angels who guard him.

Key Takeaway
The hadith shows that protection from sin is attributed to God, demonstrating that human sinlessness depends entirely on divine tawfiq.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you genuinely believe that every time you avoid a sin, it is because God specifically protected you, or do you subtly credit your own willpower? How would your prayer life change if you truly internalized that you cannot resist sin without His tawfiq?
?
When you fall into sin, do you feel it is because you failed to try hard enough, or do you realize it is because God withheld His tawfiq? How can you humbly ask Him for that protection today, in a specific area where you struggle?
?
The hadith promises Paradise to the one protected from the mouth and private parts. Are your words and desires truly surrendered to God, or do you still claim ownership over what you say and want? What would it mean to hand over the reins of your tongue and your heart to Him right now?
