The 17th Proof: Hadith of Anas on Tawfiq
Author presents a hadith proof and logical inference for tawfiq necessitating action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of Anas and the logical inference from Allah's sufficiency of mentioning tawfiq prove that tawfiq necessitates righteous action, supporting the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb.

Core Idea
Tawfiq is not mere help; it necessitates the action.

This lesson examines the seventeenth proof for the Ash'ari position on divine predestination and human acquisition (kasb). Through a hadith narrated by Anas, the Prophet explains that when Allah desires good for a servant, He 'employs' him by granting him success (tawfiq) for righteous deeds. The author then draws a logical inference: Allah mentions only tawfiq, not the action itself, because tawfiq makes the action necessary. If the action could fail to occur despite tawfiq, Allah would have had to mention the action separately. This reasoning reinforces the idea that all actions are created by Allah and that the servant's role is acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic text of the hadith from Anas and its translation. Notice the key term 'tawfiq'.
The hadith is short but dense.
2
Understand the definition of tawfiq
The author defines tawfiq as the preponderance of the motive for righteousness over the motive for corruption in the heart. This is a key concept.
Tawfiq is an act of Allah.
3
Follow the logical inference
The author argues that because Allah mentions only tawfiq and not the action itself, the action must necessarily follow from tawfiq. If it were possible for the action not to occur, mentioning tawfiq alone would be insufficient.
This is a conditional argument: if action could not follow, Allah would have mentioned it.
4
Connect to the Ash'ari doctrine
Understand how this proof supports the view that all actions are created by Allah and that human power (qudra) is effective through acquisition (kasb).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة عشر : ما روى أنس . أن النبي عليه السلام قال : ( إذا أراد الله بعبد خيراً ، استعمله ، قيل : فكيف يستعمله يا رسول الله ؟ قال : يوفقه لعمل صالح قبل الموت ) ووجه الاستدلال بهذا الخبر : هو أن هذا مذهبنا في أن قدرة العبد إن كانت صالحة للعمل الصالح وللعمل الفاسد . فذلك التوفيق ، عبارة عن ترجيح داعية الصلاح على داعية الفساد في قلبه . ثم إنه تعالى اكتفى بذكر هذا التوفيق عن وقوع ذلك العمل الصالح لأن عند حصول هذا التوفيق يكون حصول الفعل واجباً ، فاستغنى بذكر السبب عن ذكر المسبب . ولو كان تخلف الفعل عن حصول هذا التوفيق ممكناً ، لكان من الواجب أن لا يكتفي بذكر هذا التوفيق عن حصول ذلك الفعل . بل كان ينبغي أن يذكر أن ذلك الفعل . هل حصل أم لا ؟
The seventeenth proof: What Anas narrated, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'If Allah desires good for a servant, He employs him.' It was said: 'How does He employ him, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'He grants him success (yuwaffiquhu) for righteous action before death.' And the aspect of inference from this report is that this is our doctrine—that the servant's power (qudra) is capable of both righteous action and corrupt action. So that success (tawfiq) is an expression of the preponderance of the motive for righteousness over the motive for corruption in his heart. Then He, exalted, sufficed with mentioning this success instead of the occurrence of that righteous action, because when this success occurs, the occurrence of the action becomes necessary, so He sufficed with mentioning the cause instead of mentioning the effect. And if the non-occurrence of the action despite the occurrence of this success were possible, it would have been necessary not to suffice with mentioning this success instead of the occurrence of that action. Rather, He should have mentioned whether that action occurred or not.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage presents the seventeenth proof for the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb and divine predestination. It is a scriptural proof (hadith) followed by a logical inference. The proof begins by citing the hadith where the Prophet says that when Allah wants good for a servant, He 'employs' him, which is explained as granting him success (tawfiq) for righteous deeds before death. The author then explains the inference: according to the Ash'ari school, the servant's power is capable of both good and evil. The tawfiq is the divine act of tipping the balance of motives in the heart towards righteousness. Allah mentions only tawfiq, not the action itself, because tawfiq necessarily leads to the action—the action is necessitated by the preponderant motive. If it were possible for the action not to occur despite tawfiq, then mentioning tawfiq alone would be insufficient; Allah would have had to specify whether the action actually occurred or not. The argument shows that the occurrence of the action is necessitated by tawfiq, supporting the Ash'ari view that all actions are created by Allah and that the servant's role is acquisition (kasb).

Key Terms
توفيق
داعية الصلاح
داعية الفساد
قدرة
وجوب
سبب
مسبب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tawfiq is mere assistance that does not guarantee action.
Correction: The passage argues that tawfiq necessarily leads to action; otherwise, Allah would not have sufficed with mentioning it alone.

Checkpoint
According to the 17th proof, what does 'tawfiq' refer to?
A) The creation of the action by Allah
B) The servant's free choice
C) The preponderance of the motive for righteousness in the heart
D) The writing of destiny on the preserved tablet

Key Takeaway
The hadith and logical inference show that divine tawfiq necessitates righteous action, supporting the Ash'ari view that all actions are created by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If tawfiq necessitates action, what does your failure to act righteously reveal about the state of your heart and the balance of your motives? Have you earnestly begged Allah to tip that balance, or do you rely on your own strength?
?
The hadith says tawfiq is granted before death. Are you living today as if you are expecting that tawfiq, actively seeking it through supplication and reliance on Allah, or are you assuming that your good deeds are from yourself?
?
When you find yourself procrastinating or neglecting a duty to Allah, pause and ask: have I truly been granted that preponderant motive from Allah? What concrete step will you take today to seek that divine success (tawfiq) before it is too late?

The 18th Proof: Hadith Qudsi on Creation for Paradise and Fire
Author cites a hadith qudsi and notes opponent's interpretation as foreknowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith qudsi proof used in predestination debates and why opponents reinterpret it as referring to divine knowledge or the Preserved Tablet.

Core Idea
Divine creation for Paradise or Fire does not eliminate human responsibility; the hadith shows foreknowledge.

This lesson examines a short but significant proof from hadith qudsi. The author cites a well-known narration where Allah says He created some for Paradise and some for the Fire. Opponents reinterpret this as merely referring to Allah's knowledge or a written decree. The author notes that the complete refutation has already been given earlier, so our focus will be on understanding the proof and the objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the hadith qudsi and the opponent's interpretation mentioned.
The author does not repeat the earlier answer here, so we must rely on context.
2
Identify the core proof
The proof is the hadith itself: Allah directly creating people for their ultimate destiny. This implies that destiny is determined by divine creation, not solely by human choice.
3
Understand the opponent's response
Opponents claim the hadith refers to Allah's foreknowledge (علم) or the writing on the Preserved Tablet (اللوح المحفوظ), not actual causation.
This turns the proof into a statement of knowledge, not creation.
4
Reflect on the missing answer
The author says 'its answer has already preceded.' Think about what answer would reconcile divine creation with human responsibility—likely the distinction between creating based on foreknowledge and creating arbitrarily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة عشر : قوله عليه السلام حكاية عن رب العزة : خلقت هؤلاء للجنة ولا أبالي وخلقت هؤلاء للنار ولا أبالي . والخصوم حملوه على العلم أو على الكتابة في اللوح المحفوظ . وقد سبق جوابه.
The eighteenth proof: His saying, peace be upon him, narrating from the Lord of Might: 'I created these for Paradise and I do not care, and I created these for the Fire and I do not care.' And the opponents interpreted it as [referring to] knowledge or as the writing on the Preserved Tablet. And its answer has already preceded.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This is a very brief proof that simply cites the well-known hadith qudsi indicating that Allah creates people directly for Paradise or the Fire, implying that their ultimate destiny is determined by divine creation, not by their own actions. The author notes that opponents (likely the Mu'tazila or Qadariyya) interpret this hadith as referring to Allah's foreknowledge or the decree written on the Preserved Tablet, thereby denying that the hadith proves predestination of people to bliss or perdition. The author states that the answer to those interpretations was already given earlier, so he does not repeat it here. This proof is thus a reference to a previous refutation.

Key Terms
رب العزة
علم
لوح محفوظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this hadith proves that Allah arbitrarily creates people for heaven or hell regardless of their actions, thus denying free will and accountability.
Correction: The author's earlier answer (not repeated here) likely distinguishes between Allah's creative will and His legislative will, or shows that the hadith refers to the final outcome based on foreknowledge, not the creation of actions. Human responsibility remains intact.

Checkpoint
How do the opponents interpret the hadith 'I created these for Paradise...'?
A) As referring to actual creation of people for Paradise and Fire
B) As referring to Allah's knowledge or the writing on the Preserved Tablet
C) As a metaphor for the test of faith
D) As referring to the intercession of prophets

Key Takeaway
The hadith qudsi proof asserts divine creation for destiny, but opponents reinterpret it as foreknowledge, a refutation of which was already given earlier.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah created some for Paradise and some for Fire, does that make you feel a sense of urgency about your own state, or do you feel resigned? What does your emotional response reveal about your trust in Allah's justice and mercy?
?
The opponents reinterpreted the hadith as foreknowledge to avoid determinism. In your own life, do you sometimes use the concept of divine decree to excuse your sins or procrastinate on good deeds? How would your actions change if you truly believed that your choices matter despite Allah's foreknowledge?
?
The author does not repeat the refutation here but refers you back to an earlier answer. Are you willing to go back and study that answer, or are you content with a partial understanding? How does your diligence in seeking truth reflect your love for Allah?

The 19th Proof: Protection and Preponderant Motives
Author presents a hadith proof, then addresses two objections about divine graces and motives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument from the hadith on protection that a servant's sinlessness is by divine tawfiq, and the principle that an unopposed preponderant motive necessitates action.

Core Idea
A truly unopposed motive must lead to action; otherwise it's not truly preponderant.

This lesson presents the nineteenth proof from the text: a prophetic hadith that attributes protection from sin to Allah, not the servant. The author then tackles two objections from those who interpret this protection as mere divine graces, and the key principle that a preponderant motive (murajjih) necessitates its effect. Understanding this exchange clarifies the Ash'ari view on divine causality and human action.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith proof
Read the hadith and the author's inference that the protection (wiqaya) is from Allah, not the servant. This establishes the foundation that sinlessness is by divine tawfiq.
Note the phrase 'من وقى الذي بين لحييه ورجليه' refers to guarding tongue and private parts.
2
Understand the first objection and answer
The opponents claim the hadith refers to divine graces (al-altaf). The author replies that Allah has done every possible grace, and that a grace must be a preponderator, which necessitates its effect.
3
Understand the second objection and answer
Opponents argue that not every preponderant motive leads to action, citing personal experience. The author clarifies that such inclinations are not truly preponderant because they are opposed by stronger motives.
The key principle: a preponderant motive free from opposition necessarily leads to action.
4
Reflect on the principle of preponderant motive
Consider why this principle matters for the Ash'ari theory of causality. It shows that even in human actions, a fully determined cause (the preponderant motive) inevitably produces its effect.
This connects to broader discussions of qadar and human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة عشر : ما روى أبو حازم، عن أبي هريرة - رضي الله عنه ـ قال : قال رسول الله : ( من وقى الذي بين لحييه ورجليه دخل الجنة ) النص : دل على أن تلك الوقاية مضافة إلى غير العبد . وما ذاك إلا الله تعالى. وهذا يدل على أن العبد إنما يبقى مصوناً عن المعاصي بتوفيق الله . قالوا : المراد منه : الألطاف ، وجوابنا : إن كل ما قدر الله عليه من الألطاف ، فقد فعله . وأيضاً : اللطيف لا بد وأن يكون مرجحاً ، وكل مرجح فهو موجب . على ما مر تقريره مراراً . وقالوا : ليس كل ما رجح الداعي فإنه واجب الفعل فإنه قد يميل قلبنا إلى بعض الأفعال مع أنا لا نفعل والجواب : إن ذلك الميل إنما لا يوجب الفعل لأنه لما صار معارضاً بصادر آخر أقوى منه فحينئذ لم يبق ميلا . بل الميل المرجح إذا حصل وخلى عن المعارض فإنه كما يرجح فلا بد وأن يوجب الفعل كما قررناه .
The nineteenth proof: What Abu Hazim narrated from Abu Huraira - may Allah be pleased with him - who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever is protected (wuqiya) between his jaws and his legs will enter Paradise.' The text indicates that that protection (wiqaya) is attributed to other than the servant, and that is none other than Allah. And this indicates that the servant only remains protected from sins by Allah's success (tawfiq). They said: What is meant by it is the divine graces (al-altaf). Our answer: Indeed, every grace that Allah has decreed He has done. Also, a grace (latif) must be preponderating, and every preponderator necessitates. As has been established many times. And they said: Not every preponderance of motive makes the action necessary, for our heart may incline towards some actions while we do not do them. The answer: That inclination does not necessitate the action because it is opposed by another stronger inclination; then it is no longer an inclination. Rather, the preponderant inclination when it occurs and is free from opposition, it just as it preponderates, necessarily necessitates the action, as we have established.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage presents the nineteenth proof and includes two objections and answers. The proof is a hadith about being protected between the jaws (tongue) and legs (private parts) leading to Paradise. The author argues that the protection is attributed to Allah, not the servant, showing that the servant's sinlessness is by divine tawfiq. The opponents (likely Mu'tazila) interpret 'protection' as referring to divine graces (al-altaf) that make obedience easier but do not compel. The author's first response: Allah has already done every grace He could, implying that if more grace were possible, He would have done it. Also, a grace (latif) must be a preponderator (murajjih), and every preponderator necessitates its effect. This is a key Ash'ari principle: a preponderant motive necessitates the action. The second objection: Not every preponderance of motive results in action, because we often feel inclined but do not act. The answer: That inclination is not truly preponderant because it is opposed by a stronger inclination; a genuine preponderant motive free from opposition necessarily leads to action. This reinforces the deterministic causality underlying Ash'ari kalam.

Key Terms
وقاية
ألطاف
مرجح
موجب
داعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People often think that any strong inclination or desire will necessarily lead to action.
Correction: The author explains that an inclination only leads to action if it is unopposed by a stronger inclination; a truly preponderant motive necessitates the action.

Checkpoint
What is the second objection's claim about inclined motives?
A) They always lead to action
B) They rarely lead to action
C) They do not necessarily lead to action because they may be opposed
D) They are created by the servant

Key Takeaway
The hadith on protection proves that sinlessness is by Allah's grace, and only an unopposed preponderant motive necessitates action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you last avoided a major sin, did you consciously thank Allah for protecting you, or did you attribute it to your own willpower? The hadith teaches that protection is from Allah. Will you today, in your next prayer, specifically thank Allah for the sins He has prevented you from committing, even those you nearly committed?
?
Think of a sin you used to commit regularly. At the moment of committing it, was there any opposing motive in your heart, like fear of Allah or shame? If not, you were completely overpowered by the motive. How can you strengthen opposing motives (like remembering Allah's presence) so that they become truly preponderant before you slip?
?
The author argues that a preponderant motive free from opposition necessarily leads to action. Reflect on your current spiritual state: what is the strongest motive in your heart right now? Is it love of this world or love of Allah? What would it take for the love of Allah to become unopposed and truly preponderant in your daily choices?

The 20th Proof: Hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn on Decree and Striving
Author presents a hadith narrative on divine decree and accountability, then begins analysis of 'qada'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument that divine decree and human striving are compatible, as illustrated by the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn.

Core Idea
Decree does not negate striving; both are from Allah's wisdom.

The twentieth proof presents a hadith narrative that directly addresses the apparent tension between divine decree and human accountability. Through a conversation between 'Imran ibn Husayn and a companion, and later a man from Murcia with the Prophet, the passage clarifies that actions are decreed yet people are still responsible for their choices. This lesson unpacks the hadith and its theological implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith narrative
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the central question: are actions decreed or not?
The narrative involves two similar dialogues.
2
Identify the Prophet's answer
Find the phrase 'بل شيء قضى عليهم ومضى عليهم' and the Prophet's response that actions are decreed.
3
Reflect on the deeper meaning
Consider the Prophet's statement: 'كان خلقه لواحد من المنزلتين فهو مستعمل لها' meaning creation is for one of two stations and He uses them.
This implies divine purpose and utilization of actions.
4
Note the Quranic support
The author cites verse 91:7-8 about inspiration of wickedness and righteousness as confirmation.
5
Understand the incomplete analysis
The passage begins explaining 'qada' as setting of causes, but ends mid-sentence. Recognize that the full argument continues beyond this excerpt.
This highlights the need to consult the full text.

الحجة العشرون : ما روى يحيى بن معمر عن أبي الأسود الدؤلي قال : قال عمران بن الحصين : يا أبا الأسود أرأيت ما يعمل الناس اليوم ويكدحون فيه ؟ أشيء قضى عليهم ومضى عليهم ؟ أو فيما يستقبلون مما اتى به نبيهم وأخذ به عليهم الحجة . قال : بل شيء قضى عليهم ومضى عليهم ، قال : فلم نعمل إذا ؟ قال : ففزعت من ذلك فزعاً شديداً فقلت : إنه ليس شيء إلا خلق الله وملك يده لا يسأل عما يفعل وهم يسألون فقال عمران ابن الحصين : سددك الله ووفقك . أما والله ما سألت إلا لأجد . وإن رجلا من مرسية أتى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال يا رسول الله : أرأيت ما يعمل الناس ويكدحون فيه ؟ أشيء قضى عليهم ومضى عليهم ؟ أو فيما يستقبلون مما أتاهم به نبيهم وأخذت عليهم من الله الحجة قال : بل شيء قضى عليهم ومضى عليهم قال : فلم نعمل إذاً ؟ قال : كان خلقه لواحد من المنزلتين فهو مستعمل لها . وتصديق ذلك في كتاب الله : ( ونفس وما سواها فألهمها فجورها وتقواها ) واعلم : أن القضاء يحتمل أن يكون المراد منه : وضع الأسباب التي
The twentieth proof: What Yahya ibn Ma'mar narrated from Abu al-Aswad al-Du'ali, who said: 'Imran ibn Husayn said: O Abu al-Aswad, have you seen what people do and strive in? Is it something decreed upon them and passed? Or is it something they will face from what their Prophet brought and the proof established upon them? He said: Rather, it is something decreed upon them and passed. He said: Then why do we work? He said: I was extremely frightened and said: There is nothing except that Allah created it and owns it; He is not asked about what He does, but they will be asked. Then 'Imran ibn Husayn said: May Allah direct you and grant you success. By Allah, I only asked to find [the answer]. And a man from Murcia came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: O Messenger of Allah, have you seen what people do and strive in? Is it something decreed upon them and passed? Or something they will face from what their Prophet brought and the proof of Allah was taken upon them? He said: Rather, it is something decreed upon them and passed. He said: Then why do we work? He said: [They are] His creation for one of the two stations, and He is using them. And the confirmation of that in the Book of Allah: {And a soul and what proportioned it, and inspired it with its wickedness and its righteousness.} And know: That 'al-qada' (decree) may mean the establishment of the causes which...

Commentary
This passage presents the twentieth proof, which is a lengthy hadith narrative. The proof aims to show that human actions are decreed by Allah, yet people are still held accountable. The narrative involves 'Imran ibn Husayn asking Abu al-Aswad about the nature of actions, and then relaying a story of a man from Murcia who asked the Prophet about the same issue. The Prophet's answer: 'It is something decreed upon them and passed,' and when asked why work then, he replied that Allah created people for one of two stations and uses them. The author then cites the Quranic verse about the soul and its inspiration of wickedness and righteousness. Finally, the author begins an explanation of the meaning of 'qada' (decree), suggesting it may refer to the setting of causes, but this explanation is cut off due to the end of the page. The passage thus demonstrates the Ash'ari position that divine decree does not negate human responsibility, but the full argument is incomplete.

The 21st Proof: Hadith on Creation and Diversity
Author presents a hadith to prove that differences in actions and beliefs are divinely ordained.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a hadith about Adam's creation from diverse earth is used to argue that differences in human actions and beliefs are divinely ordained.

Core Idea
Our physical diversity points to a deeper, divinely ordained diversity in character and belief.

In this proof, the author cites a hadith from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari to support the doctrine that human actions are not independent but determined by God. The hadith describes how Adam was created from a handful of earth taken from all over, resulting in diversity of temperaments. The author then argues that this diversity in temperament necessarily leads to diversity in morals, actions, and beliefs. Let's examine the text and its theological implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its context
Read the Arabic passage once, including the hadith and the author's commentary. Then read the translation. Notice how the author presents the hadith as evidence.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Musa al-Ash'ari.
2
Understand the link between physical diversity and temperament
Focus on the phrase 'فجاء بنو آدم على قدر الأرض' (so the children of Adam came according to the measure of the earth). The author interprets this as diversity of temperaments (اختلاف الأمزجة).
3
See how the author deduces moral and behavioral differences
The author states 'فوجب اختلاف الأخلاق والأفعال والعقائد' (so diversity of morals, actions, and beliefs is necessitated). This is the key conclusion of the proof.
The word 'وجب' indicates necessity, not mere possibility.
4
Reflect on the specific examples
The author gives examples of yellow bile leading to anger and savagery, and phlegm leading to calmness and dullness. Consider how these humors are linked to behavior.
This is based on ancient humoral theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الحادية والعشرون : ما روى أبو موسى الأشعري قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ( إن الله خلق آدم من قبضة قبضها من جميع الأرض . فجاء بنو آدم على قدر الأرض . منهم الأحمر والأسود والأبيض والأصفر . ومن ذلك السهل والحزن والخبيث والطيب ، واعلم : أن هذا إشارة إلى ما بينا من اختلاف الأمزجة . فوجب اختلاف الأخلاق والأفعال والعقائد . فمن كانت الصفراء عليه أغلب ، كان الغضب والسبعية والقسوة عليه أغلب . ومن كان البلغم عليه أغلب ، كان السكون والهدوء والبلادة عليه أغلب
The twenty-first proof: What Abu Musa al-Ash'ari narrated, he said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Indeed God created Adam from a handful which He took from all of the earth. So the children of Adam came according to the measure of the earth. Among them are the red, the black, the white, and the yellow. And from that are the easy, the difficult, the bad, and the good. And know that this is an indication of what we have explained of the diversity of temperaments. So diversity of morals, actions, and beliefs is necessitated. So whoever has the yellow bile predominant upon him, anger, savagery, and harshness are predominant upon him. And whoever has the phlegm predominant upon him, calmness, tranquility, and dullness are predominant upon him.'
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage presents the twenty-first proof in a series of arguments for the doctrine that the servant has no independent power over action (العبد لا استقلال له بالفعل والترك). The author cites a hadith from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari in which the Prophet explains that God created Adam from a handful of soil taken from all parts of the earth, resulting in the diversity of human temperaments—red, black, white, yellow, and varying dispositions like easy, difficult, bad, good. The author interprets this as an indication of the diversity of temperaments (اختلاف الأمزجة), implying that differences in moral character, actions, and beliefs are necessitated (فوجب) by these divinely determined temperaments. He then gives a specific example: if yellow bile (الصفراء) is predominant, then anger, savagery, and harshness are predominant; if phlegm (البلغم) is predominant, then calmness, tranquility, and dullness are predominant. Thus, the hadith is used to support the idea that human actions are ultimately determined by God's creation and not by independent human choice.

Key Terms
اختلاف الأمزجة
الصفراء
البلغم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this hadith only describes physical diversity or racial variation without implications for behavior.
Correction: The author explicitly argues that the hadith indicates diversity of temperaments, which necessitates diversity in morals, actions, and beliefs, thus supporting divine determinism.

Checkpoint
According to the twenty-first proof, what is indicated by the diversity of colors and temperaments mentioned in the hadith?
A) That people have free will to choose their actions
B) That differences in morals, actions, and beliefs are divinely necessitated
C) That only physical appearances are predetermined
D) That humans are created equal in all respects

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Abu Musa shows that the diversity of human temperaments, rooted in creation, necessitates diversity in actions and beliefs, supporting divine determinism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own natural tendencies—whether quick anger, calmness, or something else—do you truly accept that they are part of God's decree from your very creation? If they are predetermined, how does that change your view of your own faults? Will you stop blaming yourself and instead focus on working within your nature to please God?
?
Think of a person whose behavior you find difficult to tolerate. Could their temperament be a direct result of the earth from which they were created? How does this lesson challenge your right to judge them? What would it look like to extend mercy to them today, knowing that their actions are rooted in divine decree?
?
If your moral actions are necessitated by your temperament, then where does sincere effort fit in? Does this lesson make you feel passive or resigned? Or does it drive you to seek God's help to transform your temperament through worship and dua? What specific step will you take this week to align your will with His decree?

The 22nd Proof: Hadith of the Dispute over Qadar
Author narrates a hadith about a dispute between Abu Bakr and Umar on qadar, resolved by the Prophet citing a precedent from angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how this hadith serves as a proof for the Ashʿari position that both good and evil are decreed by Allah.

Core Idea
The Prophet settled the qadar dispute by citing angelic precedent: both good and evil are from Allah.

This lesson presents the twenty-second proof from Al-Matalib al-ʿAliyah, a hadith that directly addresses the debate over divine decree and human action. The narration records a historical dispute between Abu Bakr and Umar, and how the Prophet resolved it by referring to an earlier judgment among the angels. This story serves as a powerful support for the Ashʿari doctrine of qadar.

Guided Path
1
Read the Hadith
Read the Arabic passage once through, then follow the translation. Notice the narrative flow: the dispute, the Prophet's inquiries, and the angelic parallel.
The hadith is narrated from Amr ibn Shuʿayb, with a chain of transmission.
2
Identify the Two Positions
Abu Bakr said: 'Good deeds are from Allah, evil deeds are from ourselves.' Umar said: 'Good and evil are both from Allah.' Contrast these views.
Abu Bakr's position resembles the Muʿtazili view, while Umar's is the Ashʿari view.
3
Observe the Prophet's Reaction
The Prophet turned away from Abu Bakr but became cheerful at Umar's statement. Why? His cheer indicates approval of Umar's view.
This shows the Prophet's endorsement of the view that both good and evil are from Allah.
4
Understand the Angelic Precedent
The Prophet reveals that Gabriel and Michael had a similar disagreement, and Israfil judged that 'good and evil are from Allah.' The Prophet confirms this as his judgment.
This elevates the ruling to divine authority, as angels are infallible.
5
Reflect on the Final Statement
The Prophet says: 'If Allah had willed that no one would disobey Him, He would not have created Iblis.' This reinforces that evil and disobedience are part of Allah's decree.
This ends the hadith on a note of divine sovereignty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية والعشرون : ما روی عمرو بن شعیب ، عن أبيه عن جده قال : كنت جالساً عند رسول الله ، إذ أقبل أبو بكر وعمر ، ومعهما قوم ) من الناس ، قد ارتفعت أصواتهم . فكف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الحديث وتسمع فلما دنوا ، جاء أبو بكر فسلم على رسول الله وجلس إلى جنبه ، ثم جاء عمر وسلم وجلس بعيداً منه . فقال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام : « ما هذا الذي ارتفعت أصواتكم فيه ؟ قال بعض القوم : يا رسول الله تكلم أبو بكر وعمر ، واختلفا فاختلفنا باختلافهما . قال : ( وما ذاك ؟ ، قالوا : في القدر (4) قال أبو بكر : يقدر الله الخير ولا يقدر الشر. وقال عمر : بل يقدرهما . فتبع بعض القوم أبا بكر ، وبعضهم عمر . فقال : رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : وكيف قلت يا أبا بكر ؟ ، قال : قلت الحسنات من الله ، والسيئات من أنفسنا . فأعرض عنه . ثم أقبل على عمر ، وقال : ( كيف قلت يا عمر ؟ ، قال : قلت : الحسنات والسيئات كلها من الله قال فانبسط رسول الله ، حتى عرف البشر في وجهه . وقال : ( والذي بعثني بالحق ، لأقضي بينكما بما قضى به إسرافيل ، بين جبريل وميكائيل ، فقال بعضهم : أو تكلم فيه جبريل وميكائيل ؟ فقال : ه والذي نفس محمد بيده إنها لأول الخلائق تكلما فيه . أما جبريل فقال : مثل مقالتك يا عمر ، وأما ميكائيل فقال مثل مقالتك يا أبا بكر . فتحاكما إلى إسرافيل ، فقضى بيها قضاءاً هو قضائي بينكما ، قالوا يا رسول الله فما كان من قضائه ؟ قال : « قضى إسرافيل بينهما بأن الخير والشر من الله ، وهذا قضائي بينكما ، ثم قال : ( يا أبا بكر لو أراد الله [ أن (۱) ] لا يعصى في أرض أحد ، لم يخلق إبليس : .
The twenty-second proof: What Amr ibn Shu'ayb narrated from his father from his grandfather, he said: I was sitting with the Messenger of God, when Abu Bakr and Umar approached, and with them a group of people, their voices had risen. So the Messenger of God, may peace be upon him, stopped talking and listened. When they drew near, Abu Bakr came and greeted the Messenger of God and sat next to him, then Umar came and greeted and sat far from him. The Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'What is this that your voices have been raised about?' Some of the people said: 'O Messenger of God, Abu Bakr and Umar spoke and disagreed, so we disagreed due to their disagreement.' He said: 'And what is that?' They said: 'About predestination (al-qadar). Abu Bakr said: God decrees good and does not decree evil. And Umar said: Rather He decrees both.' So some of the people followed Abu Bakr, and some followed Umar. Then the Messenger of God, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'How did you say, O Abu Bakr?' He said: 'I said: Good deeds are from God, and evil deeds are from ourselves.' So he turned away from him. Then he turned to Umar and said: 'How did you say, O Umar?' He said: 'I said: Good deeds and evil deeds, all of them are from God.' So the Messenger of God became cheerful until joy was seen in his face. And he said: 'By Him Who sent me with the truth, I will judge between you with what Israfil judged between Gabriel and Michael.' Some of them said: 'Did Gabriel and Michael speak about it?' He said: 'He [or By Him] in Whose hand is the soul of Muhammad, they were the first creatures to speak about it. As for Gabriel, he said like your statement, O Umar. And as for Michael, he said like your statement, O Abu Bakr. So they sought judgment from Israfil, and he judged between them with a judgment that is my judgment between you.' They said: 'O Messenger of God, what was his judgment?' He said: 'Israfil judged between them that good and evil are from God, and this is my judgment between you.' Then he said: 'O Abu Bakr, if God had willed that no one would disobey Him in any land, He would not have created Iblis.'
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage presents the twenty-second proof. The author narrates a hadith from Amr ibn Shu'ayb via his father and grandfather, describing a dispute between Abu Bakr and Umar over qadar (predestination). Abu Bakr held that God decrees good but not evil, while Umar held that God decrees both. The people split into factions. The Prophet first asks each their opinion: Abu Bakr says good deeds are from God, evil from ourselves; Umar says both good and evil are from God. The Prophet then becomes cheerful and declares that he will judge between them with the same judgment that Israfil made between Gabriel and Michael, who had previously disagreed on the same issue. Gabriel held Umar's view (both from God), Michael held Abu Bakr's view (good from God, evil from us). They took the matter to Israfil, who ruled that both good and evil are from God. The Prophet confirms this as his own judgment, and adds that if God had wanted no disobedience, He would not have created Iblis (Satan). This hadith is thus used to support the Ash'ari position that all actions, both good and evil, are created by God, and to refute the Mu'tazili view that evil comes from humans.

Key Terms
القدر
الحسنات
السيئات
إسرافيل
جبريل
ميكائيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the hadith supports the Mu'tazili position because Abu Bakr initially stated a view similar to theirs (God decrees good but not evil).
Correction: The Prophet clearly endorses Umar's view that both good and evil are from Allah, as shown by his cheerful reaction and the angelic precedent. Abu Bakr's view is corrected, not upheld.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, what was the judgment of Israfil between Gabriel and Michael concerning good and evil?
A) Good deeds are from God and evil deeds are from ourselves
B) Both good and evil are from God
C) Good is from God and evil is from Satan
D) There is no such thing as evil from God

Key Takeaway
This hadith establishes that both good and evil are from Allah, as affirmed by the Prophet and the precedent of the angels.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe that Allah decreed that act? How does that belief affect your repentance and your view of yourself? Will you still take full responsibility while acknowledging His sovereignty?
?
The Prophet turned away from Abu Bakr's statement that 'evil is from ourselves.' Is there any area in your life where you subtly deny Allah's decree over your failures, as if they happen outside His will? What would change if you fully embraced that every evil deed you have committed was written by Allah?
?
The hadith ends with the creation of Iblis despite Allah knowing he would cause disobedience. Does this unsettle you? How do you reconcile Allah's will for evil to exist with His justice and wisdom? What does this demand from your trust in His plan for your life?

Two Interpretations of the Hadith on Abu Bakr and Umar's Disagreement
Two interpretations of a hadith on Abu Bakr and Umar's disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two distinct interpretations that reconcile the apparent disagreement between Abu Bakr and Umar regarding the decree of good and evil.

Core Idea
The Companions' disagreement was over terminology, not divine reality.

This passage addresses a hadith that seems to show a dispute between Abu Bakr and Umar about divine decree. However, the author presents two interpretations that explain how their differing statements can be reconciled. The first interpretation focuses on the application of the word 'evil' to painful experiences, while the second narrows the meaning of 'decree' to the act of writing in the Preserved Tablet. Both interpretations show that the disagreement was about words, not beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the two interpretations.
Notice the structure: 'السؤال الثاني : إن صح متن هذا الخبر فله تأويلان'.
2
Understand the first interpretation
The first interpretation concerns the linguistic use of 'sharr' (evil) for painful experiences. Note how Abu Bakr and Umar differed and how the Prophet clarified.
Abu Bakr avoided calling afflictions 'evil' because they are ultimately good for the servant.
3
Understand the second interpretation
The second interpretation redefines 'qadr' as 'kitabah' (writing). Abu Bakr said only good is written; Umar said both. This shows a terminological, not theological, difference.
Key phrase: 'المراد بالقدر: الكتابة'.
4
Recognize the resolution
Both interpretations show that the Companions did not genuinely disagree about divine decree. They only differed in wording or scope.
This prevents sectarian misuse of the hadith.
5
Reflect on terminology
Consider how careful definition of terms prevents misunderstandings in theological discussions.
This lesson highlights the importance of precise language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الثاني : إن صح متن هذا الخبر ، فله تأويلان : أحدهما : إنهما اختلفوا في إطلاق اسم الشر على الآلام والأسقام والمحن فمنعه أبو بكر عن ذلك . لأنه وإن كان مؤلماً، فهو خير للعبد . لما فيه من الأعراض . وأجازه عمر . فبين رسول الله : جواز ذلك، وأنها وإن كانت مصلحة، فهي شر بمعنى كونه مؤلماً . الثاني : إن المراد بالقدر: الكتابة . فكان أبو بكر يقول : يقدر الخير دون الشر، أي أن يكتب الخير في اللوح المحفوظ ، ولا يكتب الشر . وعمر كان يقول يكتبهما.
The second question: If the text of this report is authentic, it has two interpretations: First: That they disagreed over applying the name 'evil' (sharr) to pains, ailments, and tribulations. Abu Bakr forbade that because although it is painful, it is good for the servant due to what it contains of benefits. Umar permitted it. So the Messenger of Allah clarified the permissibility of that, and that even though they are a benefit, they are evil in the sense of being painful. Second: That what is meant by 'al-qadr' is the writing (al-kitabah). So Abu Bakr used to say: He decrees good but not evil, i.e., He writes good in the Preserved Tablet and does not write evil. Umar used to say: He writes both.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage presents two interpretations of a hadith that apparently reports a disagreement between Abu Bakr and Umar. The first interpretation concerns the linguistic application of the term 'sharr' (evil) to painful experiences. Abu Bakr avoided calling them evil because they are ultimately good for the servant, while Umar saw no harm in using the term due to their painful nature. The Prophet confirmed its permissibility, distinguishing between moral evil and physical pain. The second interpretation reframes the term 'qadr' (decree) as specifically referring to writing in the Preserved Tablet. Abu Bakr held that only good is written, while Umar held that both good and evil are written. Thus, the disagreement is about the scope of what is written, not about divine decree as a whole. This shows that even apparent disagreements among the Companions can be resolved through careful interpretation of texts.

Key Terms
الشر
القدر
الكتابة
اللوح المحفوظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Abu Bakr and Umar actually disagreed about divine decree itself.
Correction: The passage shows they only disagreed about terminology and the specific meaning of 'qadr'.

Checkpoint
According to the first interpretation, why did Abu Bakr forbid calling afflictions 'evil'?
A) Because they are not painful
B) Because they are ultimately good for the servant
C) Because the Prophet forbade it
D) Because Umar disagreed

Key Takeaway
The apparent disagreement between Abu Bakr and Umar over divine decree is resolved by understanding that they differed only in terminology, not in core belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a painful trial, do you instinctively label it as 'evil'? How does the Companions' discussion about the terminology of 'sharr' challenge your immediate reaction, and what would it take for you to see it as a benefit despite the pain?
?
If you truly believed that only good is written in the Preserved Tablet (as per one interpretation), would that change how you view the hardships in your life? What is holding you back from that conviction?
?
The Prophet clarified that afflictions are 'evil in the sense of being painful' but still a benefit. When was the last time you felt pain (physical or emotional) and failed to see any benefit? What would it mean to ask Allah to show you the hidden good in that moment, rather than resenting the trial?

Refuting the Objection: Why Did Allah Create Iblis?
Refutation of an objection concerning Allah's creation of Iblis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that Allah's will against sin would preclude creating Iblis is refuted by distinguishing between divine will and human choice.

Core Idea
Creating Iblis does not contradict Allah's will; it tests human free will.

This passage addresses a common objection against divine decree: if Allah truly wills that no disobedience occur, why did He create Iblis, the source of all sin? The author argues this objection is weak and offers two interpretations that preserve both divine will and human responsibility. As you read, notice how the author navigates between theological determinism and human free will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the objection and the author's response.
Pay attention to the phrase 'هذا ضعيف' which signals the refutation.
2
Identify the two interpretations
The author offers two possible meanings of the objection. Find each one and note how they differ.
3
Understand the role of the Jabriyya
Notice how the author uses the Jabriyya position to show that the objection is weak, because for them existence and non-existence are equal.
The Jabriyya deny human choice, so the objection doesn't stand.
4
Reflect on free will and reward
Consider why the author emphasizes that the servant acts by his own choice to deserve reward. This is key to the refutation.
Divine will does not compel; it allows choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما قوله : ( لو شاء الله أن لا يعصى لم يخلق إبليس ، فنقول : هذا ضعيف . لأنه عند المجبرة : وجود إبليس وعدمه سواء . فإن ثبت هذا الكلام ، فمعناه : لو شاء الله أن لا يخلق من يعصيه، لما خلق إبليس . وهو رأس العصاة . فأشار إلى أنه تعالى كما يخلق من يعلم أنه يؤمن، كذلك يخلق من يعلم أنه يكفر وإنما يأتي المكلف بالكفر والايمان من قبل نفسه لا من قبل ربه . ويحتمل أيضاً : أنه لو شاء أن يمتنع من المعصية جبراً، أو قسراً، لما خلق إبليس، مع علمه بأنه رأس الكفر . ولكنه تعالى أراد أن يؤمن العبد باختياره ليستحق الثواب . والله اعلم .
As for his saying: 'If Allah willed that He not be disobeyed, He would not have created Iblis,' we say: This is weak. Because according to the Jabriyya, the existence of Iblis and his non-existence are equal. If this statement is established, its meaning is: If Allah willed not to create anyone who disobeys Him, He would not have created Iblis, and he is the head of the disobedient. So He indicated that He, exalted, just as He creates one whom He knows will believe, likewise He creates one whom He knows will disbelieve, and the servant only brings about disbelief and faith from himself, not from his Lord. It is also possible: That if He willed to prevent disobedience by compulsion or force, He would not have created Iblis, knowing he is the head of disbelief. But He, exalted, wanted the servant to believe by his choice to deserve reward. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage refutes an objection raised against divine decree: 'If Allah willed that He not be disobeyed, He would not have created Iblis.' The author first notes that this objection is weak because, according to the Jabriyya who deny human choice, existence and non-existence of Iblis are equal (since everything is directly from Allah). However, the author then offers a proper interpretation: the statement means that if Allah had willed not to create any disobedient being, He would not have created Iblis, who is the chief of sinners. This shows that Allah creates both those He knows will believe and those He knows will disbelieve, but the servant's act of faith or disbelief comes from himself, not from Allah. Alternatively, the author suggests another interpretation: if Allah had willed to prevent disobedience by compulsion, He would not have created Iblis. But instead, Allah wanted the servant to believe by his own choice in order to deserve reward. Thus, divine creation of Iblis does not contradict divine will; rather, it is consistent with the test of human free will.

Key Terms
المجبرة
إبليس
العصيان
الاختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Creating a being known to disobey contradicts divine will.
Correction: Divine will includes the test of free will. Creating Iblis allows for human choice and deserving reward.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main response to the objection about creating Iblis?
A) The objection is true and cannot be answered
B) The objection is weak and has two possible interpretations that preserve free will
C) Allah wanted Iblis to rebel
D) Iblis was not created by Allah

Key Takeaway
Allah's creation of Iblis does not contradict His will; it is part of a test where humans choose faith or disbelief by their own free will to deserve reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever feel like it was predestined or forced upon you? How does this lesson challenge you to own your choices and turn back to Allah with sincerity?
?
Allah created Iblis knowing he would disobey, yet He still gave you the chance to believe by your own choice. Are you truly using your free will to seek His reward, or are you coasting on the excuse that 'everything is written'?
?
This passage insists that your faith or disbelief comes from yourself. If you were to stand before Allah tomorrow, would you be able to say you chose faith with full responsibility? What is one concrete step you will take today to exercise your free will in obedience?

The 24th Proof: Hadith of Aisha on Creation of Paradise and Hell
Narration of the hadith with its apparent inference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of Aisha demonstrates Allah's foreknowledge and creation of the inhabitants of Paradise and Hell before their birth, supporting the doctrine of qadar.

Core Idea
Allah preordains the ultimate destiny of every soul before creation.

This lesson presents a powerful hadith narrated by Aisha that directly addresses the question of predestination. The Prophet (peace be upon him) declares that Allah created Paradise and Hell and even their inhabitants before they were born. This concise statement carries profound theological implications for understanding divine decree.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and translation
Read the Arabic text of the hadith carefully, then read the literal English translation. Notice how the words 'خلق' (created) and 'أصلاب' (loins) set the timeframe.
The hadith is very short but packed with meaning.
2
Reflect on the timing
Consider the phrase 'while they were in the loins of their fathers' – it means these people did not yet exist, yet Allah created them as inhabitants of Paradise or Hell. What does this imply about when destinies are determined?
3
Understand the inference
The author says 'the inference is apparent.' Identify the logical conclusion from this hadith: that Allah's decree of who will be in Paradise and Hell is set before birth, supporting the Sunni doctrine of qadar.
This inference is central to the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة والعشرون : عن عائشة قالت : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ه إن الله خلق الجنة ، وخلق لها أهلاً. وهم في أصلاب آبائهم . وخلق النار ، وخلق لها أهلا . وهم في أصلاب آبائهم ، والاستدلال به ظاهر .
The twenty-fourth proof: From Aisha, she said: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Indeed Allah created Paradise, and created for it people, while they were in the loins of their fathers. And He created Hell, and created for it people, while they were in the loins of their fathers.' And the inference from it is apparent.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents the twenty-fourth proof, a hadith from Aisha. The Prophet states that Allah created Paradise and its inhabitants, and Hell and its inhabitants, even before they were born (while still in their fathers' loins). The author notes that the inference (istidlal) from this hadith is apparent: it clearly indicates that the ultimate destiny of individuals—whether they will be among the people of Paradise or Hell—is predetermined by Allah's creation and decree, long before their actual existence. This supports the Sunni doctrine of predestination (qadar).

Key Terms
الجنة
النار
الأصلاب
القضاء والقدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That this hadith denies human free will; rather, it affirms divine foreknowledge and creation of the end result.
Correction: The hadith affirms that Allah creates the ends, but Islamic theology also holds that humans acquire their actions. This hadith does not negate human responsibility; it only shows that the outcome is known and decreed by Allah.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith from Aisha primarily demonstrate?
A) That Paradise and Hell are not yet created
B) That people earn their place by their own deeds
C) That Allah preordains the inhabitants of Paradise and Hell
D) That only Paradise's inhabitants are preordained

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Aisha clearly indicates that Allah's decree encompasses the final abode of every person, established before their birth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah has already created you for Paradise or Hell before you were born, what genuine difference does your daily struggle with sin and obedience make? Do you truly live as if your choices are real and consequential, or has this lesson exposed a hidden fatalism in your heart that excuses laziness in worship?
?
When you sin, do you blame qadar and say 'it was written'? When you obey, do you take credit? How does the fact that Allah created your destiny while you were still in your father's loins strip away both arrogance and despair? Will you commit to acting as if your choices matter precisely because Allah's decree is the foundation of His justice?
?
This hadith says Allah created the people of Hell while they were still in the loins of their fathers. Do you feel a shiver of fear that you might be among them, or do you assume you are safe? What specific change in your life today would reflect a genuine trust that Allah's decree is good, even if you don't know your final outcome?

The 25th Proof: The Prophetic Supplication on Divine Control
Citing the famous du'a to argue that all acts are from Allah's creation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's du'a 'O Allah, there is no preventer of what You give' serves as a proof that all human acts are created by Allah.

Core Idea
A prophetic supplication proves human acts are from Allah's creation.

This lesson presents the 25th proof from the author, which is a well-known supplication of the Prophet. The du'a declares that nothing can prevent what Allah gives and nothing can give what Allah prevents. The author uses this to argue that if human actions were independent, they could contradict this divine monopoly on giving and preventing.

Guided Path
1
Read the du'a and its context
Read the Arabic text of the du'a and its translation. Notice that the du'a affirms Allah's exclusive power to give and prevent.
The du'a is well-known and often recited in supplications.
2
Analyze the logical conditional
Focus on the conditional statement: 'if the servant's act were not from Allah...' The author draws a conclusion that the servant could then prevent what Allah gives, which contradicts the du'a.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Reflect on the implication
Understand that the du'a is not only about material provisions but extends to all acts, including the servant's own actions. Thus, all actions are under Allah's creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة والعشرون : الدعاء المشهور المأثور عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو قوله : ( اللهم لا مانع لما أعطيت، ولا معطى لما منعت ، ولو كان جعل العبد ليس من خلق الله تعالى، لكان العبد قد يمنع كثيراً مما(٢) أعطى الله ،
The twenty-fifth proof: The well-known supplication transmitted from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, which is his saying: 'O Allah, there is no preventer of what You give, and no giver of what You prevent. And if the act of the servant were not from the creation of Allah the Exalted, then the servant would prevent much of what Allah gives.'
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents the twenty-fifth proof, which is a famous supplication (du'a) taught by the Prophet: 'O Allah, there is no preventer of what You give, and no giver of what You prevent.' The author argues that if the actions of human beings were not created by Allah (i.e., if they were independent acts originating from themselves), then humans would be able to prevent many of the things that Allah gives, such as the ability to do good or to receive blessings. But the du'a affirms that nothing can prevent what Allah has decreed to give, and nothing can give what Allah has decreed to prevent. Therefore, the servant's actions must be under Allah's complete control and creation, supporting the doctrine that all human acts are created by Allah.

Key Terms
الدعاء
المانع
المعطي
جعل العبد
خلق الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The du'a is only about material provisions (like sustenance, wealth) and does not relate to human actions.
Correction: The author extends the du'a to all acts, arguing that if human actions were independent, they could prevent what Allah gives (e.g., the ability to perform good deeds), which contradicts the du'a's universal scope.

Checkpoint
What is the logical consequence the author draws from the du'a if the servant's actions were not from Allah?
A) The du'a would be meaningless
B) The servant could prevent much of what Allah gives
C) Allah would not be omnipotent
D) The servant would be forced to obey

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's du'a demonstrates that no one can prevent or give except Allah, implying that even human actions are under Allah's creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'O Allah, there is no preventer of what You give,' do you truly believe this applies to every outcome in your life, including those you try hard to control? What would change in your daily decisions if you lived as if every act of yours is also created by Him?
?
Can you identify a situation where you acted as if your own effort alone could 'give' or 'prevent' something, independent of Allah's decree? How does the Prophet's du'a challenge that mindset, and what would it look like to surrender that area to Allah today?
?
If you deeply accepted that even your 'making' (ja‘l) is from Allah, how would your attitude towards your successes and failures shift? What would you need to let go of to truly embrace that your actions are under His creation?

Hadith Proof of Predestination
A short proof from a hadith that God created the inhabitants of Paradise and Hell beforehand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how this hadith from 'A'isha serves as a proof for the predetermined creation of the inhabitants of Paradise and Hell.

Core Idea
God foreordains the final abode of every soul before birth.

This lesson presents a concise proof from prophetic tradition. The hadith cited by the author is remarkably direct: it states that God created the inhabitants of Paradise and Hell before they were ever born. Understanding this proof helps clarify the Islamic doctrine of qadar (divine decree).

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic hadith once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the parallel structure: 'He created Paradise and created for it inhabitants... and He created the Fire and created for it inhabitants.'
The phrase 'while they were in the loins of their fathers' emphasizes pre-existence before birth.
2
Identify the key claim
The hadith explicitly affirms that God created the inhabitants of Paradise and Hell before their existence. This implies that their final abode was determined prior to any action.
3
Reflect on the author's conclusion
The author says 'the deduction from it is apparent.' Ask yourself: Why is this hadith considered a clear proof for predestination? How does it challenge the idea that human actions alone determine one's fate?
Consider that if God creates someone already destined for Paradise, then that person's good deeds are a consequence, not the cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة والعشرون : عن عائشة قالت : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ه إن الله خلق الجنة ، وخلق لها أهلاً. وهم في أصلاب آبائهم . وخلق النار ، وخلق لها أهلا . وهم في أصلاب آبائهم ، والاستدلال به ظاهر .
The twenty-fourth proof: from 'A'isha, she said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Indeed God created Paradise and created for it inhabitants, and they were in the loins of their fathers. And He created the Fire and created for it inhabitants, and they were in the loins of their fathers.' And the deduction from it is apparent.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents a very concise proof. The author cites a hadith from 'A'isha where the Prophet states that God created the inhabitants of Paradise and Hell before they were even born, while they were in the loins of their fathers. The author simply notes that the deduction (istidlal) from this hadith is obvious: if God created people for Paradise or Hell before their existence, then their final abode is predetermined and not based solely on their own choice.

Key Terms
الجنة
النار
أصلاب
القضاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, when did God create the inhabitants of Paradise and Hell?
A) After their actions
B) Before their existence in the loins of their fathers
C) At the moment of death
D) Only for those who believe

Key Takeaway
This hadith directly asserts that God predetermined the final abode of every person before their birth, making it a clear proof for qadar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God created you for Paradise or Hell before you were born, does that change how you view your daily choices? What would you start doing today if you knew your destination was already set?
?
Are you living as if your final abode is already determined and you are merely fulfilling what was written, or as if your actions can change it? How does this hadith make you feel about your own accountability?
?
Imagine you truly believed that every person you meet was created by God for either Paradise or Hell. How would that change the way you interact with them, especially those who oppose you?

The Supplication Proof: No Preventer to What You Give
Proof from a well-known supplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a well-known supplication demonstrates that all actions, including giving and preventing, are under God's control and thus created by Him.

Core Idea
If we truly believe the supplication, then human actions must be created by God.

This lesson examines a proof based on a famous supplication taught by the Prophet (ﷺ). The supplication affirms that only God can truly give or prevent. The author argues that if human actions were independent of God's creation, then humans could contradict the supplication by giving what God prevents and preventing what God gives. This proof reinforces the doctrine that all actions are created by God.

Guided Path
1
Read the supplication
Read the hadith quote carefully: 'O God, there is no preventer to what You give, and no giver to what You prevent.' Notice the absolute nature of the statement.
2
Understand the logical implication
The author draws an implication: if humans' actions were not created by God, then humans could prevent what God gives and give what God prevents, which contradicts the hadith.
3
Connect to the doctrine of qadar
Reflect on how this proof supports the idea that all human acts are created by God, affirming God's sovereignty and control over all events.

Source Text

The twenty-fifth proof: the famous supplication reported from the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, which is his saying: 'O God, there is no preventer to what You give, and no giver to what You prevent.' And if the servant's action were not from the creation of God Almighty, then the servant would be able to prevent much of what God gives, and would be able to give much of what God prevents. And that is contrary to the hadith.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents a proof using the logic of a well-known supplication. The supplication affirms that only God can give or prevent. If the servant's actions were not created by God, then the servant could effectively give what God prevents and prevent what God gives, thereby contradicting the supplication. Therefore, the servant's actions must be created by God.

The Prayer for Help as a Proof
Analyzing the term 'help' in a Prophetic supplication to prove divine control of motives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's supplication for help demonstrates that divine assistance must be more than just empowerment, proving God's control over internal motives.

Core Idea
Help in prayer is not just empowerment; it is God's special creation of motives.

This lesson examines a Prophetic hadith used as a theological proof. The author argues that if 'help' in the supplication meant only the ability and removal of obstacles that God already gives to everyone, then asking for it would be pointless. Therefore, 'help' must refer to something else—the divine creation of motives—which proves that God controls the internal factors of action.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and deduction
Read the Arabic passage carefully: first the hadith, then the logical analysis. Notice how the author presents two possible meanings for 'help'.
The hadith is from Mu'adh ibn Jabal.
2
Analyze the first alternative
The author says if 'help' meant empowerment, enabling, and removal of excuses, then God already gives that to everyone. Ask yourself: why would that make the prayer pointless?
Empowerment is given to all, so there is no need to ask.
3
Understand the conclusion
Since the prayer is meaningful, 'help' must mean something else — the creation of motives to obey and deterrents from sin. This shows God's control over internal factors.
This proof is used in the context of qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة والعشرون : عن معاذ بن جبل أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، قال : و ألا أعلمك كلمات تقولهن ؟ اللهم أعني على ذكرك وشكرك وحسن عبادتك ، وجه الاستدلال : أن هذه الإعانة. إن كان المراد منها الإقدار والتمكين وإزاحة الأعذار ، فالكل قد جعله الله ، فلا فائدة في طلبه بالدعاء . وإن كان المراد شيئاً آخر . فهو المطلوب
The twenty-sixth proof: from Mu'adh ibn Jabal that the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Shall I not teach you words to say? O God, help me to remember You, to thank You, and to worship You well.' The aspect of deduction: that this help: if what is meant by it is empowerment, enabling, and removal of excuses, then that is something God has given to all, so there would be no benefit in asking for it through supplication. And if something else is meant, then that is what is sought.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage analyzes the word 'help' (i'ana) in the Prophetic supplication. The author argues: if 'help' meant only empowerment (iqdar), enabling (tamkin), and removal of excuses (izahat al-a'dhar), then God has already given these to everyone, making the prayer pointless. Therefore, 'help' must refer to something additional: the creation of motives towards obedience and deterrents from disobedience. This proves that God controls the internal factors that lead to action.

Correction: The author argues that external empowerment is already given; the prayer must be for internal motives and deterrents created by God.

C) It would be impossible to ask for

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Hadith of 'It is Easy for Whom God Makes it Easy' and the Logic of Necessity
A proof using the logic of necessary concomitance: if God makes it easy, then the work is easy; otherwise not.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the principle of necessary concomitance is used to interpret the hadith 'It is easy for whom God makes it easy' and why taysir must refer to divine creation of motives.

Core Idea
The absence of ease proves the absence of God's special taysir.

This lesson examines a proof from the hadith narrated by Mu'adh ibn Jabal. The Prophet’s statement 'It is easy for whom God makes it easy' is analyzed using a logical tool: arguing from the absence of the consequent to the absence of the antecedent. By applying this reasoning, the author shows that the 'making easy' mentioned cannot be the general empowerment given to all, but must be a specific divine act of creating motives and deterrents.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and the logical argument
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice how the author first presents the hadith, then explains the logical deduction (istidlal) using the relation of necessary concomitance.
2
Understand the logical form: absence of consequent implies absence of antecedent
The author argues: if God's taysir (antecedent) necessitates ease in action (consequent), then when ease is absent, taysir must be absent. This is a standard logical move called 'istidlal bi 'adam al-lazim 'ala 'adam al-malzum'.
This step is key to the proof.
3
Refine the meaning of taysir
The author then notes that if taysir meant general empowerment and removal of excuses, it would be present for everyone. But not everyone finds obedience easy. So the taysir in the hadith must mean something else: the creation of motives (dawa'i) towards obedience and deterrents (sawarif) from sin.
4
Connect to the broader topic of qadar
Consider how this argument relates to divine predestination: it shows that God’s guidance is not just general but specific, involving inner motivation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة والعشرون : عن معاذ بن جبل أنه قال للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : أخبرني بعمل يدخلني الجنة . فقال : ( إنه ليسير على من يسره الله عليه ، وجه الاستدلال : أن النص دل على أن التيسير الصادر من الله تعالى ، يلزمه اليسر في العمل ، وحيث لا يحصل اليسر في العمل، علمنا : أنه لم يحصل التيسير من الله . استدلالاً بعدم اللازم لعدم الملزوم . ثم إن التيسير بمعنى الإقدار وخلق العقل وإزاحة الأعذار : حاصل للكل، فوجب أن يكون المراد بهذا التيسير المذكور ههنا : شيء آخر . وذلك بخلق الدواعي إلى الطاعات ، وخلق الصوارف عن أضدادها . وهو المطلوب .
The twenty-seventh proof: from Mu'adh ibn Jabal that he said to the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace: 'Tell me of an action that will admit me to Paradise.' He said: 'It is easy for whom God makes it easy.' The aspect of deduction: that the text indicates that the making easy (taysir) coming from God Almighty necessitates ease in the action, and where ease in the action does not occur, we know that the making easy from God has not occurred—arguing from the absence of the consequent to the absence of the antecedent. Then, if making easy means empowerment, creation of intellect, and removal of excuses, that is something present for all, so it must be that the making easy mentioned here is something else. And that is the creation of motives towards acts of obedience and the creation of deterrents from their opposites. And that is what is sought.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This is a logical argument using the principle of necessary concomitance. The Prophet said 'It is easy for whom God makes it easy.' If 'making easy' (taysir) were simply giving power and reason, then everyone would have it and find obedience easy, which is false. Therefore, taysir must mean something additional: the creation of motives (dawa'i) towards obedience and deterrents (sawarif) from disobedience. The author uses the logical form: if the consequent (ease) is absent, then the antecedent (God's taysir) is absent. Since ease is not always present, God's taysir (in this special sense) is not always present.

Key Terms
التيسير
الملزوم
اللازم
استدلال
الدواعي
الصوارف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'making easy' refers to external circumstances or general empowerment given to all people equally.
Correction: The author argues that if taysir were only general empowerment, then everyone would find obedience easy, which is false. Therefore, taysir must be a specific divine act: creating inner motives towards obedience and deterrents from sin.

Checkpoint
The reasoning from absence of consequent to absence of antecedent is used to show:
A) That if ease is absent, then God's making easy is absent
B) That God makes everything easy for everyone
C) That empowerment is the same as making easy
D) That the hadith is about human effort

Key Takeaway
The absence of ease in obedience proves that God's specific 'making easy' (creation of motives and deterrents) is not given to all—highlighting the role of divine grace in righteous action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you struggle to perform an act of worship, do you attribute it solely to your own weakness, or do you consider that you may be lacking God's specific taysir of created motives? What would it mean for you to sincerely ask God for that grace right now?
?
The author argues that general taysir (intellect, empowerment) is given to all, yet many do not find ease in obedience. Think of a specific area in your life where you continue to disobey despite knowing what is right. What 'deterrent' from disobedience are you refusing to let God create in your heart?
?
If God's specific taysir is the creation of motives, then your desire to pray or give charity is itself a gift. When was the last time you thanked God not just for the action but for the desire to do it? How can you make that awareness a daily habit?
