Twenty-Eighth Proof: Hadith of the Hearts Between the Fingers of the Merciful
A proof from multiple hadiths that God directly controls human hearts and the scale of deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how multiple hadiths prove that God has direct control over human hearts and deeds, supporting the doctrine of divine predestination.

Core Idea
God controls every heart and every scale.

This lesson presents the twenty-eighth proof from al-Matalib al-Aliyah, drawing on well-known hadiths. The Prophet (peace be upon him) teaches that every heart is between two fingers of the Merciful, and that even the Prophet himself prayed for steadfastness. These texts establish that human will is subordinate to God's will.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadiths carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that there are three distinct hadith citations: the general statement about hearts, the mention of the scale, and the specific narration from Jabir.
2
Examine the Prophet's prayer
Focus on the phrase 'O Turner of hearts, make my heart firm upon Your religion.' Ask yourself why the Prophet would pray this if he had complete control over his own faith.
This shows that even the Prophet's faith depends on God.
3
Reflect on the implication for free will
Consider how these hadiths challenge the notion of absolute human free will. The doctrine of qadar is supported by the idea that God directly turns hearts and raises or lowers scales.
This connects to the broader theological topic of predestination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة والعشرون : الخبر المشهور عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال : • ما من قلب إلا وهو بين إصبعين من أصابع الرحمن . إن شاء أن يقيمه أقامه وإن شاء أن يزيغه ازاغه ، وكان يقول : ( يا مقلب القلوب . ثبت قلبي على دينك  والميزان بيد الرحمن يرفع ويخفض ، وعن جابر بن عبد الله قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كثيراً ما يقول : « يا مقلب القلوب ، ثبت قلبي على دينك فقيل له يا رسول الله : اتخاف علينا ، وقد آمنا بك ، وبما جئت به ؟ فقال : " إن القلوب بين إصبعين من أصابع الرحمن يقلبها هكذا ، وأشار إلى السبابة والوسطى ، يحركهما
The twenty-eighth proof: the well-known report from the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, that he said: 'There is no heart except that it is between two fingers of the Merciful. If He wills to make it upright, He makes it upright; and if He wills to make it deviate, He makes it deviate.' And he used to say: 'O Turner of hearts, make my heart firm upon Your religion.' And the scale is in the hand of the Merciful, He raises and lowers. And from Jabir ibn 'Abdullah said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, used to say often: 'O Turner of hearts, make my heart firm upon Your religion.' So it was said to him: O Messenger of God, do you fear for us, when we have believed in you and in what you have brought? He said: 'Indeed, the hearts are between two fingers of the Merciful; He turns them like this,' and he pointed with his index and middle fingers, moving them.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage presents multiple hadithic texts. The core message is that God directly controls the hearts of all people, turning them towards faith or deviation. The Prophet himself prayed for steadfastness, showing that faith is not self-generated but depends on God's ongoing will. The reference to the scale also indicates God's control over the weight of deeds. These hadiths collectively prove that God has absolute control over human hearts and actions, supporting the doctrine of predestination.

Key Terms
القلب
الأصابع
الرحمن
التثبيت
مقلب القلوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that human free will is absolute and independent of God's control.
Correction: These hadiths show that even the Prophet's heart depends on God, and that God directly turns hearts and controls the scale, refuting absolute free will.

Checkpoint
The Prophet's prayer 'O Turner of hearts, make my heart firm upon Your religion' shows that:
A) The Prophet doubted his faith
B) Even the Prophet's faith depends on God's will
C) Hearts are beyond God's control
D) Humans can turn their own hearts

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's prayer for steadfastness shows that even the best of creation relies on God for faith, affirming God's absolute control over hearts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet, who is sinless and whose faith is perfect, constantly pleaded, 'O Turner of hearts, make my heart firm upon Your religion.' When did you last truly beg God to keep your faith alive? Does the fact that you rarely or never pray this prayer reveal a dangerous self-reliance? Will you begin to say it daily from now on?
?
You have just read that every heart is between two fingers of the Merciful — He turns it as He wills. If that is true, then your next spiritual slip or your next moment of steadfastness is entirely in His hands. Are you living as if that is true? Or do you still act as if your faith depends on your own efforts? What will you change today to acknowledge His absolute control?
?
God controls even the scale of your deeds — He raises and lowers at will. Does this thought comfort you or terrify you? If it comforts you, are you truly humble before Him? If it terrifies you, do you realize that your good deeds are not your own achievement? How will this reshape your gratitude and your fear of Him?

Twenty-Sixth Proof: Divine Help in the Hadith of Mu'adh
Presents a contradictory claim and then the twenty-sixth proof from the hadith of Mu'adh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the twenty-sixth proof from the hadith of Mu'adh, and how it argues that divine help (i'ana) must include something beyond mere empowerment.

Core Idea
The Prophet's supplication proves that help is not just empowerment.

This lesson presents a key proof from the hadith of Mu'adh. The author argues that if the 'help' requested were simply empowerment and removal of excuses, the supplication would be pointless. Therefore, it must refer to something else — the creation of motives for obedience. This is a sophisticated argument about the nature of divine assistance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the logical flow from the contradictory claim to the hadith and the inference.
2
Identify the two interpretations of 'help'
In the inference, the author presents two possible meanings of 'help': (1) empowerment, enablement, and removal of excuses, or (2) something else. Understand the difference.
3
Understand why only one interpretation works
The author argues that if 'help' meant merely empowerment, then asking for it would be pointless because it is already given. Therefore, it must mean something else, which is the desired conclusion.

And He often gives much of what He has prohibited. And that is contrary to the hadith. The point of inference: This help. If what is meant by it is empowerment, enablement, and removal of excuses, then all of that has been given by Allah, so there is no benefit in asking for it through supplication. But if it means something else, then that is what is sought.

Commentary
This passage begins with a statement that contradicts a hadith (probably refuting a claim that God gives what He has forbidden). The inference (wajh al-istidlal) is that the 'help' requested cannot be merely empowerment and removal of excuses, because those are already given to all and there would be no point in asking for them. Therefore, it must be something else, which is the desired conclusion (the creation of motives for obedience).

Twenty-Seventh Proof: Facilitation in the Hadith of Mu'adh
Presents the twenty-seventh proof from the hadith about ease.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith 'It is easy for whom Allah makes it easy' is used as a proof in kalam for divine creation of motives and deterrents.

Core Idea
True facilitation is not external ease, but Allah creating the inner drive to obey.

This lesson examines the twenty-seventh proof, which draws on a well-known hadith. The Prophet's response to Mu'adh is unpacked to reveal a deeper point about divine action. By analyzing the logical inference, we see that the facilitation mentioned must refer to something beyond general empowerment—specifically, the creation of motives for obedience and deterrents against sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and the inference
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the logical structure: if ease in action is absent, then God's facilitation is absent, using the contrapositive form.
2
Distinguish two meanings of taysir
The author argues that taysir as empowerment is universal, so the hadith must mean something else. Identify the two meanings: general empowerment vs. specific creation of motives and deterrents.
3
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that the taysir in the hadith refers to Allah creating dawa'i (motives) towards obedience and sawarif (deterrents) against disobedience. This is the sought proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة والعشرون : عن معاذ بن جبل أنه قال للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : أخبرني بعمل يدخلني الجنة . فقال : ( إنه ليسير على من يسره الله عليه . وجه الاستدلال : أن النص دل على أن التيسير الصادر من الله تعالى ، يلزمه (۱) اليسر في العمل ، وحيث لا يحصل اليسر في العمل، علمنا : أنه لم يحصل التيسير من الله . استدلالاً بعدم اللازم لعدم الملزوم . ثم إن التيسير بمعنى الإقدار وخلق العقل وإزاحة الأعذار : حاصل للكل، فوجب أن يكون المراد بهذا التيسير (۲) المذكور ههنا : شيء آخر . وذلك بخلق الدواعي إلى الطاعات ، وخلق الصوارف عن أضدادها . وهو المطلوب .
The twenty-seventh proof: From Mu'adh ibn Jabal that he said to the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم: 'Tell me of a deed that will admit me to Paradise.' He said: 'It is easy for whom Allah makes it easy.' The point of inference: The text indicates that the facilitation (taysir) from Allah necessitates ease in the deed. So when ease in the deed is not obtained, we know that facilitation from Allah has not occurred, by inference from the absence of the necessary consequence to the absence of the necessitating condition. Then, if facilitation means empowerment, creation of intellect, and removal of excuses, it is present for all, so what is meant by this facilitation mentioned here must be something else: that is, the creation of motives (dawa'i) towards acts of obedience, and the creation of deterrents (sawarif) against their opposites. And that is what is sought.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage gives the twenty-seventh proof from the hadith where the Prophet says a deed is easy for whom Allah makes it easy. The author infers that if ease in action is not present, then Allah's taysir is absent. Since taysir in the sense of empowerment and removal of excuses is universal, the taysir mentioned in the hadith must be something else: specifically, the creation of motives towards obedience and deterrents against disobedience.

Correction: The author argues that since empowerment is universal, taysir must refer to the creation of internal motives and deterrents.

A) Empowerment and removal of excuses.
B) Creation of motives and deterrents.
C) Predestination of all actions.

Key Takeaway
The hadith's 'ease' refers to Allah's creation of motives for obedience and deterrents against sin, not merely external facilitation.

?

Twenty-Eighth Proof: Hearts Between Allah's Fingers
Presents hadith and rational argument linking motives to divine control.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of the heart being between Allah's two fingers is rationally supported by the argument from motives and deterrents, and why this proves divine control over human actions.

Core Idea
Allah controls every action by granting or withholding the motive.

This lesson presents a powerful proof that combines revealed and rational evidence. The Prophet's ﷺ description of hearts being between Allah's fingers is not a physical metaphor but points to a profound truth: every human action depends on a motive that comes only from Allah. We will examine both the hadith and the rational argument that backs it.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith versions
Start by reading the two hadith reports about the heart being between Allah's fingers. Notice the Prophet's supplication and the reaction of the Companions.
The hadith uses metaphorical language; don't take it literally.
2
Understand the rational argument
The author explains that actions depend on motives (dawa'i) and deterrents (sawarif). An action occurs only when its motive is present; otherwise it does not. The 'two fingers' symbolize the presence or absence of the motive.
Think of the heart as a scale: motive tips it toward action.
3
Connect to divine causation
The motive must come from Allah; otherwise an infinite regress would follow. This is the key rational reason for Allah's control over hearts.
The infinite regress argument is a standard kalam proof.
4
Confirm with Quran
Read the Quranic verse (8:24) that Allah intervenes between a man and his heart. This supports the same point.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The author asserts that combining these proofs leaves no doubt about Allah's sovereignty over hearts. Consider how this applies to your own life.
This is a profound truth in Islamic theology of qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة والعشرون : الخبر المشهور عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال : ما من قلب إلا وهو بين إصبعين من أصابع الرحمن . إن شاء أن يقيمه أقامه وإن شاء أن يزيغه ازاغه ، وكان يقول : يا مقلب القلوب . ثبت قلبي على دينك والميزان بيد الرحمن يرفع ويخفض ، وعن جابر بن عبد الله قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كثيراً ما يقول : يا مقلب القلوب ، ثبت قلبي على دينك فقيل له يا رسول الله : اتخاف علينا ، وقد آمنا بك ، وبما جئت به ؟ فقال : إن القلوب بين إصبعين من أصابع الرحمن يقلبها هكذا ، وأشار إلى السبابة والوسطى ، يحركهما واعلم : أن هذا الذي بينه صاحب الشريعة صلوات الله عليه في هذا الخبر معلوم الصحة بالبراهين اليقينية العقلية. وذلك لأن أفعال الجوارح لا تصدر إلا عند الدواعي والصوارف في القلوب . فرجحان الفعل موقوف على حصول داعية الفعل ، ورجحان الترك موقوف على عدم حصول تلك الداعية ، لأن علة العدم : عدم العلة . فالقلب كالشيء الموصوف بين حصول تلك الداعية واللاحصول لها. فإن حصلت داعية الفعل ، حصل الفعل .. وإن لم تحصل تلك الداعية ، لم يحصل ذلك الفعل . فصاحب الشريعة ، عبر عن حصول هذه الداعية وعدم حصولها بالإصبعين ، لما ثبت أن حصول تلك الداعية ليس إلا بالله تعالى . وإلا لزم التسلسل وكما ثبت هذا المعنى بهذا البرهان العقلي ، وبهذا الخبر الذي رويناه ، ثبت أيضاً بنص القرآن . وهو قوله تعالى : ( واعلموا : أن الله يحول بين المرء وقلبه ) ومن تأمل في هذه البراهين العقلية ، وضم إليها هذه الآيات ، وهذا الخبر خاصة ، ورجع إلى نفسه : لم يبقى في قلبه شك في صحة مذهبنا . ولكن ذلك إنما يسهل على من سهله الله عليه .
The twenty-eighth proof: The well-known report from the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم that he said: 'There is no heart except that it is between two fingers of the fingers of the Most Merciful. If He wills to make it stand, He makes it stand, and if He wills to make it deviate, He makes it deviate.' And he used to say: 'O Turner of hearts, make my heart firm upon Your religion.' And the balance is in the hand of the Most Merciful, He raises and lowers. And from Jabir ibn Abdullah said: The Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم often said: 'O Turner of hearts, make my heart firm upon Your religion.' It was said to him: 'O Messenger of Allah, do you fear for us, while we have believed in you and what you have brought?' He said: 'Indeed, the hearts are between two fingers of the fingers of the Most Merciful; He turns them like this,' and he pointed to his forefinger and middle finger, moving them. And know: that what the author of the Law (صلى الله عليه وسلم) has made clear in this report is known to be true by certain rational proofs. That is because the actions of the limbs do not issue except when there are motives (dawa'i) and deterrents (sawarif) in the hearts. So the preponderance of an action depends on the presence of the motive for the action, and the preponderance of avoidance depends on the absence of that motive, because the cause of non-existence is the non-existence of the cause. So the heart is like something described between the presence of that motive and its non-presence. If the motive for the action is present, the action occurs; and if that motive is not present, the action does not occur. So the author of the Law expressed the presence and absence of this motive as 'two fingers', because it is established that the presence of that motive is only from Allah Almighty; otherwise an infinite regress would follow. And just as this meaning is established by this rational proof and by this report which we have related, it is also established by the text of the Quran, namely His saying: {And know that Allah intervenes between a man and his heart} (8:24). And whoever reflects on these rational proofs and joins to them these verses and especially this report, and returns to himself, no doubt will remain in his heart about the correctness of our doctrine. But that is only easy for whom Allah makes it easy.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage presents the twenty-eighth proof, combining hadith and rational argument. It begins with two versions of the famous hadith about the heart being between Allah's fingers, indicating divine control. Then the author provides a rational analysis: physical actions depend on motives (dawa'i) and deterrents (sawarif) in the heart. An action occurs only when its motive is present; otherwise it does not. The hadith's 'two fingers' symbolize the presence or absence of this motive, which is entirely from Allah to avoid an infinite regress of motives. This is further supported by the Quranic verse (8:24). The author concludes that these rational proofs, hadith, and Quran leave no doubt for anyone who reflects sincerely.

Key Terms
إصبعين
القلب
الدواعي
الصوارف
التسلسل
البراهين العقلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'fingers' are literal, implying Allah has a physical hand that holds hearts.
Correction: The 'fingers' are a metaphor for Allah's absolute control over the presence or absence of motives in the heart, as explained by the rational argument.

Checkpoint
According to the rational argument in the twenty-eighth proof, why did the Prophet describe the heart as being between two fingers?
A) To emphasize that hearts are physically held by Allah.
B) To symbolize the presence or absence of motives, which are from Allah.
C) To indicate that humans have two choices.
D) To show that hearts are fragile.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the two fingers is a metaphor for Allah's absolute control over the motives that determine every human action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you performed a good deed today, did you pause to recognize that the very desire to do it was placed in your heart by Allah? If not, why have you been attributing your righteousness to your own self?
?
The Prophet himself constantly begged Allah to turn his heart to firmness. Do you still think your faith is secure without regularly pleading to the Turner of hearts? How many times today did you say 'Ya Muqallib al-Qulub, thabbit qalbi 'ala dinik'?
?
Think of a recent sin you committed. Was it not because the motive for that sin was present and the deterrent absent? And who controls that? How can you ever feel arrogant about your obedience, knowing that Allah withholds the motive to sin?

The Hadith of Power as a Proof
Presents the twenty-ninth proof from the hadith about power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' serves as a proof for divine power and the necessity of divine strengthening for actions, and how it relates to the balance between action and inaction.

Core Idea
Action occurs not from power alone, but from divine strengthening of motives.

This lesson examines the twenty-ninth proof in Al-Matalib al-Aliyah, based on a profound hadith often recited by Muslims. The author unpacks the logical inference: power is inherently neutral, so something extra must tip the balance toward action—that extra is the divine power mentioned in the phrase 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah.' By understanding this, you will grasp a key argument in Sunni theology about God's role in human actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its context
Notice the words 'from beneath the Throne' and 'treasure of Paradise' to sense its importance. The hadith directly connects the phrase to divine power.
2
Understand the logical structure
The author argues that power (qudra) is equally balanced between action and inaction. As long as this equilibrium remains, action is impossible. Action requires a strengthening of the side of action.
3
See how the hadith proves divine involvement
This strengthening is what is referred to by 'لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله'. Thus, the hadith shows that human actions depend on divine aid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة والعشرون : عن أبي هريرة قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ألا أعلمك كلمة من تحت العرش [ كنز ] من كنوز الجنة : لا قوة إلا بالله . يقول الله : أسلم عبدي واستسلم . وجه الاستدلال به : إن القدرة بالنسبة إلى الفعل أو إلى الترك، على السوية. وما دام تبقى القدرة على هذا الاستواء ، امتنع صدور الفعل . فإذا رجع جانب الفعل على جانب الترك بتحصيل الدواعي وإزالة الصوارف، فحينئذ يحصل الفعل . وهذه التقوية . المشار إليها بقوله : ( لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله ) ولما كان الإيمان لا يتم ولا يكتمل إلا به ، لا جرم زعم أنه من تحت العرش ، ومن كنز الجنة
The twenty-ninth proof: From Abu Huraira said: The Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'Shall I not teach you a word from beneath the Throne, a treasure from the treasures of Paradise: There is no power except with Allah. Allah says: My slave submitted and surrendered.' The point of inference by it: That power (qudra) is equally balanced between action and inaction. As long as power remains in this equilibrium, the occurrence of the action is impossible. So when the side of action overpowers the side of inaction through the acquisition of motives and the removal of deterrents, then the action occurs. And this strengthening is what is referred to by his saying: 'There is no strength nor power except with Allah.' And since faith is not complete and perfect except through it, he—no wonder—claimed that it is from beneath the Throne and from the treasures of Paradise.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage presents the twenty-ninth proof using the hadith 'لا قوة إلا بالله'. The author explains that power (qudra) is neutral between action and inaction. Action only occurs when the side of action outweighs the side of inaction through acquiring motives and removing deterrents. This strengthening is the 'power' from Allah mentioned in the hadith. Since faith depends on this divine strengthening, the Prophet called it a treasure from Paradise.

Key Terms
قدرة
استواء
داعية
صوارف
لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think 'power' in the hadith refers to physical ability or human strength.
Correction: In this context, 'power' refers to the divine strengthening of motives that tips the balance toward action, not merely human physical ability.

Checkpoint

B) The acquisition of motives and removal of deterrents.
C) The mere existence of power.
D) External circumstances.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' proves that actions occur only through divine strengthening of motives, not from human power alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fail to do a good deed, do you admit that it is because Allah did not grant you the motive and remove the deterrents, or do you blame your own weakness? How will you change your dua tonight to ask for that strengthening?
?
If every good action you perform is only possible because Allah tipped the balance in your favor, how will you thank Him not just for the ability to act, but for the very desire to do good?
?
Are there areas in your life where you rely on your own power, forgetting that even the inclination to act is a gift from Allah? What would it look like to surrender that area to Him right now?

The Rational Mechanism of Actions: Motivation and Deterrence
Rational analysis of action dependence on motivations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why actions of the limbs depend on motivations and deterrents in the heart, and how this forms the basis for the Ash'ari doctrine of predestination.

Core Idea
Actions follow motivations; the heart is the pivot between doing and not doing.

Before we can appreciate the hadith of the two fingers, we must first grasp the rational structure of human action. The author explains that every action of the limbs is preceded by an internal motivation or deterrent. Understanding this mechanism is essential for seeing why divine control over hearts is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on action and motivation
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice how the author connects limb actions to internal states (motivations and deterrents).
2
Understand 'preponderance' of action
The author says that whether an act occurs or not depends on the presence or absence of its motivation. This is the key link to divine predestination.
3
Reflect on the heart as a described entity
The heart is described as being between existence and non-existence of motivation. This sets up the later metaphor of the two fingers.
This is a rational, not metaphorical, description.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أن هذا الذي بينه صاحب الشريعة صلوات الله عليه في هذا الخبر معلوم الصحة بالبراهين اليقينية العقلية. وذلك لأن أفعال الجوارح لا تصدر إلا عند الدواعي والصوارف في القلوب . فرجحان الفعل موقوف على حصول داعية الفعل ، ورجحان الترك موقوف على عدم حصول تلك الداعية ، لأن علة العدم : عدم العلة . فالقلب كالشيء الموصوف بين حصول تلك الداعية واللاحصول لها. فإن حصلت داعية الفعل ، حصل الفعل .. وإن لم تحصل تلك الداعية ، لم يحصل ذلك الفعل . فصاحب الشريعة ، عبر عن حصول هذه الداعية وعدم حصولها بالإصبعين ، لما ثبت أن حصول تلك الداعية ليس إلا بالله تعالى . وإلا لزم التسلسل وكما ثبت هذا المعنى بهذا البرهان العقلي ، وبهذا الخبر الذي رويناه ، ثبت أيضاً بنص القرآن . وهو قوله تعالى : ( واعلموا : أن الله يحول بين المرء وقلبه ) ومن تأمل في هذه البراهين العقلية ، وضم إليها هذه الآيات ، وهذا الخبر خاصة ، ورجع إلى نفسه : لم يبقى في قلبه شك في صحة مذهبنا . ولكن ذلك إنما يسهل على من سهله الله عليه .
And know: that which the possessor of the Sharia, blessings of Allah be upon him, clarified in this report is known to be correct by certain rational proofs. That is because actions of the limbs only occur when there are motivations and deterrents in the hearts. So the preponderance of the act depends on the existence of the motivation for the act, and the preponderance of omission depends on the non-existence of that motivation, because the cause of non-existence is the non-existence of the cause. The heart is like a described thing between the existence of that motivation and its non-existence. If the motivation for the act exists, the act occurs. And if that motivation does not exist, that act does not occur. So the possessor of the Sharia expressed the existence of this motivation and its non-existence by 'the two fingers,' because it is established that the existence of that motivation is only from Allah Almighty. Otherwise, infinite regress would be necessary. And just as this meaning is established by this rational proof and by this report we narrated, it is also established by the text of the Quran, namely His statement: 'And know that Allah comes between a man and his heart' (8:24). And whoever contemplates these rational proofs, adding to them these verses and this particular report, and returns to himself, no doubt will remain in his heart about the correctness of our school. But that is only facilitated for whom Allah makes it easy.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof integrated with a hadith. The author begins by stating that the Prophet's report (the hadith of the heart between two fingers) is verified by rational proofs. He then explains the mechanism: actions of the limbs depend on motivations (dawa'i) and deterrents (sawarif) in the heart. Preponderance (tarjih) of action or omission hinges on the presence or absence of the motivation. The heart is described as being between these two states. The Prophet metaphorically referred to this with 'two fingers,' indicating that the motivation comes only from Allah; otherwise, an infinite regress would result. This meaning is also confirmed by Quran 8:24. Finally, the author asserts that careful contemplation of these proofs removes any doubt about the Ash'ari doctrine of predestination, but such understanding is only granted by Allah.

القلب

Key Takeaway
Actions are not spontaneous; they are caused by internal motivations, which are the focus of divine control.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

How does this awareness affect your accountability before Allah?

Divine Control Over Hearts: The Two Fingers and Quranic Confirmation
Metaphor of two fingers and Quranic proof for divine control.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the metaphor of the 'two fingers' as indicating divine control over human motivations and why this prevents infinite regress, supported by Quran 8:24.

Core Idea
Only Allah controls motivations; otherwise we face infinite regress.

Having established the role of motivation in action, the author now explains why this leads to divine predestination. The Prophet's metaphor of the two fingers is not anthropomorphic but a rational necessity: if motivations came from anything other than Allah, we would have an endless chain of causes. The Quranic verse confirms this profound truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the two fingers
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the transition from rational analysis to the hadith metaphor.
2
Understand the infinite regress argument
The author says that if motivations were not from Allah, infinite regress would follow. Reflect on why this is a decisive proof.
Infinite regress is impossible in a finite chain of causes.
3
Connect to the Quranic verse
The author cites verse 8:24 as scriptural proof. Meditate on its meaning: Allah comes between a person and his heart.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author asserts that combining rational proofs, hadith, and Quran removes doubt. Consider why this synthesis is powerful.
The final sentence reminds that understanding is a gift from Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أن هذا الذي بينه صاحب الشريعة صلوات الله عليه في هذا الخبر معلوم الصحة بالبراهين اليقينية العقلية. وذلك لأن أفعال الجوارح لا تصدر إلا عند الدواعي والصوارف في القلوب . فرجحان الفعل موقوف على حصول داعية الفعل ، ورجحان الترك موقوف على عدم حصول تلك الداعية ، لأن علة العدم : عدم العلة . فالقلب كالشيء الموصوف بين حصول تلك الداعية واللاحصول لها. فإن حصلت داعية الفعل ، حصل الفعل .. وإن لم تحصل تلك الداعية ، لم يحصل ذلك الفعل . فصاحب الشريعة ، عبر عن حصول هذه الداعية وعدم حصولها بالإصبعين ، لما ثبت أن حصول تلك الداعية ليس إلا بالله تعالى . وإلا لزم التسلسل وكما ثبت هذا المعنى بهذا البرهان العقلي ، وبهذا الخبر الذي رويناه ، ثبت أيضاً بنص القرآن . وهو قوله تعالى : ( واعلموا : أن الله يحول بين المرء وقلبه ) ومن تأمل في هذه البراهين العقلية ، وضم إليها هذه الآيات ، وهذا الخبر خاصة ، ورجع إلى نفسه : لم يبقى في قلبه شك في صحة مذهبنا . ولكن ذلك إنما يسهل على من سهله الله عليه .
And know: that which the possessor of the Sharia, blessings of Allah be upon him, clarified in this report is known to be correct by certain rational proofs. That is because actions of the limbs only occur when there are motivations and deterrents in the hearts. So the preponderance of the act depends on the existence of the motivation for the act, and the preponderance of omission depends on the non-existence of that motivation, because the cause of non-existence is the non-existence of the cause. The heart is like a described thing between the existence of that motivation and its non-existence. If the motivation for the act exists, the act occurs. And if that motivation does not exist, that act does not occur. So the possessor of the Sharia expressed the existence of this motivation and its non-existence by 'the two fingers,' because it is established that the existence of that motivation is only from Allah Almighty. Otherwise, infinite regress would be necessary. And just as this meaning is established by this rational proof and by this report we narrated, it is also established by the text of the Quran, namely His statement: 'And know that Allah comes between a man and his heart' (8:24). And whoever contemplates these rational proofs, adding to them these verses and this particular report, and returns to himself, no doubt will remain in his heart about the correctness of our school. But that is only facilitated for whom Allah makes it easy.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof integrated with a hadith. The author begins by stating that the Prophet's report (the hadith of the heart between two fingers) is verified by rational proofs. He then explains the mechanism: actions of the limbs depend on motivations (dawa'i) and deterrents (sawarif) in the heart. Preponderance (tarjih) of action or omission hinges on the presence or absence of the motivation. The heart is described as being between these two states. The Prophet metaphorically referred to this with 'two fingers,' indicating that the motivation comes only from Allah; otherwise, an infinite regress would result. This meaning is also confirmed by Quran 8:24. Finally, the author asserts that careful contemplation of these proofs removes any doubt about the Ash'ari doctrine of predestination, but such understanding is only granted by Allah.

Key Terms
الإصبعين
التسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'two fingers' are literal parts of Allah.
Correction: The passage clarifies it is a metaphor for divine control, not an anthropomorphic description.

Checkpoint
What would be necessary if motivations came from other than Allah, according to the passage?
A) Infinite regress
B) Determinism
C) Free will
D) Chance

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's metaphor of two fingers shows that only Allah determines the motivations in our hearts, confirmed by reason and revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel a desire to obey or disobey, do you recognize that Allah could have prevented that motivation? How does this shape your reliance on Him in every moment?
?
If your heart's inclinations are ultimately from Allah, how does that affect your dua for guidance? Do you feel the weight of your need for Him in every decision?
?
Reflecting on the infinite regress argument, can you identify a moment where you attributed your own good intention to yourself rather than to Allah? What would it mean to truly acknowledge His control?

The Hadith of 'La Hawla Wala Quwwata Illa Billah' as a Proof of Divine Causation
Proof from hadith that power is equal until Allah tips the balance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith 'La hawla wala quwwata illa billah' serves as a proof that all effective power comes from Allah, and that human ability is neutral until Allah tips the balance.

Core Idea
Human power is neutral; Allah’s strengthening makes action happen.

Among the Ash'ari proofs for predestination is this hadith-based argument. The Prophet taught that all power belongs to Allah. The author unpacks the logic: ability is initially equal regarding action and omission. Action only occurs when Allah tips the scale by providing motivations and removing deterrents. This lesson examines the argument's structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its inference
Start by reading the Arabic hadith and its literal translation. Notice that the Prophet calls this phrase a treasure from Paradise.
The phrase 'لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله' is central.
2
Understand the concept of equal power
The author states that power (qudra) is initially equal regarding action or omission. Grasp why this neutrality means action cannot occur without external influence.
This is the key premise of the argument.
3
Trace the tipping of the balance
Follow how the side of action overcomes omission through acquiring motivations (dawa'i) and removing deterrents (sawarif). This strengthening is what the hadith refers to.
This is the 'حول' and 'قوة' from Allah.
4
Reflect on why this is a treasure of paradise
Consider why the Prophet deemed this phrase a treasure from Paradise—faith cannot be completed without recognizing that all power is from Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة والعشرون : عن أبي هريرة قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ألا أعلمك كلمة من تحت العرش كنز من كنوز الجنة : لا قوة إلا بالله . يقول الله : أسلم عبدي واستسلم ، وجه الاستدلال به : إن القدرة بالنسبة إلى الفعل أو إلى الترك، على السوية. وما دام تبقى القدرة على هذا الاستواء ، امتنع صدور الفعل . فإذا رجع جانب الفعل على جانب الترك بتحصيل الدواعي وإزالة الصوارف، فحينئذ يحصل الفعل . وهذه التقوية . المشار إليها بقوله : لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله ولما كان الإيمان لا يتم ولا يكتمل إلا به ، لا جرم زعم أنه من تحت العرش ، ومن كنز الجنة
The twenty-ninth proof: From Abu Huraira, he said: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Shall I not teach you a word from beneath the Throne, a treasure from the treasures of Paradise: There is no power except by Allah.' He said: 'My servant submitted and surrendered.' The aspect of inference from it: Indeed, power (qudra) with respect to action or omission is equal. As long as power remains in this equilibrium, the occurrence of the action is impossible. Then when the side of action overcomes the side of omission by acquiring motivations and removing deterrents, then the action occurs. And this is the strengthening referred to by his saying: 'There is no power nor strength except by Allah.' Since faith is not completed nor perfected except through it, without doubt he deemed it to be from beneath the Throne and from the treasure of Paradise.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) from hadith. The author cites a hadith where the Prophet offers to teach a word from under the Throne: 'لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله'. The argument proceeds: ability (qudra) is initially neutral between performing an action or leaving it. As long as this neutrality remains, the action cannot occur. When the side of action becomes stronger—through the acquisition of motivations (dawa'i) and removal of deterrents (sawarif)—then the action occurs. This strengthening is exactly what 'لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله' signifies, implying that all effective power comes from Allah. Because faith is incomplete without this recognition, the Prophet called it a treasure from Paradise.

Key Terms
لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله
القدرة
السوية
الدواعي
الصوارف
التقوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This hadith denies human effort and implies humans have no role in actions.
Correction: The hadith affirms that human ability is real but neutral; the decisive factor is Allah's enabling through motivations and removal of deterrents. Human effort is still involved in acquiring motivations and removing deterrents, but the ultimate effective power is from Allah.

Checkpoint
What does the word 'لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله' indicate according to the author?
A) That humans have no power at all
B) That power is neutral until Allah tips the balance
C) That action is always possible
D) That faith is complete without it

Key Takeaway
The decisive cause of action is not human power alone but Allah's strengthening through motivations and removal of deterrents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, when you succeed in doing good, do you truly feel that it was not by your own power but by Allah's strengthening? Or is there a lingering pride in your own effort? How would acknowledging this hadith shift your attitude after every action?
?
Think of a specific area where you struggle to obey Allah. What motivations (dawa'i) and deterrents (sawarif) has Allah placed in your life to tip the balance toward obedience? Are you actively seeking those motivations and removing those deterrents, or are you relying on your own power?
?
The Prophet called 'la hawla wala quwwata illa billah' a treasure from Paradise. If you truly believed that every action depends on Allah's strengthening, would you recite this phrase more often and with deeper conviction? Will you commit to saying it before every action today, and notice the difference it makes in your reliance on Allah?

The Hadith of the Pen: Proof of Divine Decree
Proof from hadith of the Pen writing all deeds, with general conclusion on hadith method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of the Pen serves as a proof for divine decree and why rejecting it would imply impossible consequences for Allah's knowledge and truth.

Core Idea
The Pen's writing encompasses all deeds; denying it would make knowledge ignorance.

In this lesson, we examine the thirtieth argument from al-Matalib al-Aliyah, which draws on a famous hadith about the Pen. The author shows that this hadith establishes divine decree and that any opposition leads to absurdities. By studying this argument, you will see how hadith evidence is used in kalam theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith text
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the chain of narration and the key elements: the creation of the Pen and the command to write.
2
Understand the inference
The author argues that the writing includes all actions of servants. Reflect on why this is a necessary implication of the hadith.
3
Recognize the consequence of opposition
Consider what would happen if one denies that all actions are written. The author says it would turn knowledge into ignorance and truth into falsehood. Why is that impossible?
4
Note the methodological conclusion
The author mentions that many hadiths support this, and whoever understands the method of inference from these can apply it to others.
This highlights the consistency of hadith evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثلاثون : عن أبي طهمان عن ابن عباس قال : أول ما خلق الله تعالى : القلم . فقال : اكتب . فقال : وما أكتب ؟ فقال : اكتب ما هو كائن إلى يوم القيامة. وجه الاستدلال به : إنه دخل في هذا المكتوب جميع أفعال العباد ، وخلافه يوجب انقلاب العلم جهلاً ، والصدق كذباً . وكل ذلك محال واعلم : أن الأحاديث الواردة في هذا الباب كثيرة ، ومن وقف على كيفية الاستدلال بهذه الأخبار التي رويناها ، أمكنه التمسك بسائر الأخبار الواردة في هذا الباب . والله أعلم .
The thirtieth proof: From Abu Tuhman, from Ibn Abbas, he said: 'The first thing Allah Almighty created was the Pen. He said: Write. He said: And what shall I write? He said: Write what will be until the Day of Resurrection.' The aspect of inference from it: Indeed, all actions of the servants are included in this writing, and opposing it would necessitate the turning of knowledge into ignorance, and truth into falsehood. And all of that is impossible. And know: the hadiths narrated on this topic are many, and whoever understands the method of inference from these reports that we have narrated is able to hold to the rest of the hadiths narrated on this topic. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents the thirtieth proof (al-hujja al-thalathun) from the hadith of Ibn Abbas about the creation of the Pen. The hadith states that the Pen was the first creation, commanded to write all that will happen until the Day of Judgment. The author argues that this writing encompasses all actions of servants. To deny that would imply that Allah's knowledge could become ignorance or His truth falsehood, both impossible. The passage then concludes with a general remark: there are many such hadiths, and whoever grasps the method of inference from those narrated here can apply it to others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Pen's writing negates human responsibility and free will.
Correction: The Pen's writing affirms Allah's foreknowledge and decree, but does not negate human responsibility; it establishes that all actions are known and decreed by Allah.

Key Takeaway
The Pen's writing encompasses all deeds, and rejecting that leads to absurdities.

The author warns that denying this writing would turn truth into falsehood. Are there moments when you act as if your own limited perspective is more reliable than Allah's decree? When will you finally accept that His writing is always true, even when it contradicts your wishes?

Thirtieth Proof: The Hadith of the Pen
The thirtieth proof from the hadith of the Pen and beginning of Chapter Four.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the thirtieth proof for divine decree based on the hadith of the Pen and the logical implication of denying the all-encompassing nature of what was written.

Core Idea
The hadith of the Pen proves that denying the writing of all actions contradicts Allah's knowledge and truthfulness.

This lesson presents a transmitted proof (khabar) for the reality of divine decree. The famous hadith of the Pen is narrated, and then the author extracts a logical argument: if the Pen wrote everything that will happen until Judgment Day, then all human actions are included. Denying this would imply that Allah's knowledge could become ignorance and His truth falsehood—both impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith narration
Start by reading the hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'The first thing Allah created was the Pen...' and notice the command to write all that will be.
This hadith is the foundation of the proof.
2
Understand the istidlal
The author explains that the 'istidlal' (evidence extraction) lies in the fact that everything written includes all actions of the servants. Grasp this key premise.
3
Consider the counterfactual
If someone denies that all actions are included, that would necessitate turning Allah's knowledge into ignorance and His truth into falsehood. Recognize why that is impossible (muhal).
This shows the argument's logical necessity.
4
Note the author's concluding remark
The author mentions that there are many such hadiths and that whoever understands this method can apply it to other reports.
5
Transition to Chapter Four
The passage ends with the heading for Chapter Four, which will present reports from the Salaf. This sets the stage for further evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثلاثون : عن أبي طهمان عن ابن عباس قال : « أول ما خلق الله تعالى القلم » . فقال : « اكتب » . فقال : وما أكتب ؟ فقال : « اكتب ما هو كائن إلى يوم القيامة » . وجه الاستدلال به : إنه دخل في هذا المكتوب جميع أفعال العباد ، وخلافه يوجب انقلاب العلم جهلاً ، والصدق كذباً . وكل ذلك محال . واعلم : أن الأحاديث الواردة في هذا الباب كثيرة ، ومن وقف على كيفية الاستدلال بهذه الأخبار التي رويناها ، أمكنه التمسك بسائر الأخبار الواردة في هذا الباب . والله أعلم . الباب الرابع في الآثار البارحة عن علماء السلف في هذا الباب
The Thirtieth Proof: From Abu Tahman from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'The first thing Allah Most High created was the Pen.' He said: 'Write.' He said: 'And what shall I write?' He said: 'Write what will be until the Day of Resurrection.' The aspect of using this as evidence: That all actions of the servants are included in this writing, and the opposite would necessitate turning knowledge into ignorance, and truth into falsehood. And all of that is impossible. And know: that the hadiths narrated on this chapter are many, and whoever comes to know the manner of using these reports that we have narrated as evidence, he can adhere to the rest of the reports narrated on this chapter. And Allah knows best. Chapter Four: On the Outstanding Reports from the Scholars of the Salaf in this Chapter.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents the thirtieth proof for the reality of divine decree, based on a transmitted hadith (khabar). The author first narrates the hadith from Ibn Abbas: Allah created the Pen and commanded it to write all that will occur until the Day of Resurrection. The proof (istidlal) is then explained: all actions of human servants (af’al al-‘ibad) are included in what the Pen wrote. If someone were to deny that all deeds are written, it would imply that Allah’s knowledge (al-‘ilm) becomes ignorance (jahl) and His truthful speech (al-sidq) becomes falsehood (kadhib)—both are impossible for Allah. The author then adds a general note: there are many such hadiths on this topic, and whoever grasps this method of reasoning can apply it to other similar reports. The passage concludes with the heading for the next chapter, which will present reports from the Salaf (early pious scholars) on the same subject. The argument is a classic kalam proof from transmitted tradition (naql) that supports the doctrine of predestination (qadar) by appealing to the necessary implication of denying it.

Correction: The author explicitly states that all actions of the servants are included in what the Pen wrote.

C) That humans have no free will.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the Pen provides a transmitted proof that all human actions are written in divine decree, and denying this would contradict Allah's perfect attributes.

The Jabriyya's Deterministic Argument from Preponderance
The author presents the Jabriyya's argument for determinism using the principle of preponderance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Jabriyya's argument for determinism based on the need for a preponderator and why they conclude human actions are compelled by God.

Core Idea
Every contingent act requires an external preponderator, so God determines all human actions.

The Jabriyya (determinists) use a seemingly simple axiom—that every contingent being needs a preponderator—to argue that human actions are compelled by God. This lesson unpacks their reasoning, showing how they build from an axiomatic premise to a conclusion of universal determinism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with a remark about the issue's strange nature.
2
Identify the key premise
Find the axiomatic premise: 'the contingent necessarily requires a preponderator.' Ask yourself why the Jabriyya consider this self-evident.
This premise is the foundation of their entire argument.
3
Trace the logical steps
Follow the reasoning: from the axiom to the agent's inability to prefer, to the need for an external preponderator, to the rejection of the preponderator coming from the agent (to avoid regress), and finally to the conclusion that it is from God.
The chain is tight: each step follows from the previous.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is compulsion (jabr). Think about what this implies for human responsibility. Consider if there is any escape from this logic.
The author is presenting the argument, not necessarily endorsing it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم : أن حال هذه المسألة : حال عجيبة . وذلك لأن الخلق أبداً كانوا مختلفين فيها ، بسبب متدافعة . أن الوجوه التي يمكن الرجوع إليها في هذه المسألة متعارضة وتقرير ذلك : أن نقول : الجبرية : عولوا في تقرير قولهم على أن الممكن لا بد له من مرجح . وهذه المقدمة مقدمة بديهية . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، فالقادر على الضدين يمتنع أن يرجح أحد الطرفين على الآخر ، لا المرجح . وذلك المرجح ليس منه ، وإلا لزم التسلسل ، بل هو من الله . وحينئذ يلزم الجبر
Know: that the state of this issue is a strange state. That is because creation have always differed concerning it, due to conflicting [reasons]. That the aspects which can be referred to in this issue are contradictory. And the explanation of that is: we say: The Jabriyya relied in establishing their statement upon the fact that the contingent necessarily requires a preponderator. And this premise is an axiomatic premise. And if the matter is so, then the one capable of opposites is prevented from preferring one of the two sides over the other, [without] the preponderator. And that preponderator is not from him, otherwise a regress would follow, but it is from God. And then compulsion necessarily follows.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents the argument of the Jabriyya (determinists) in support of their doctrine that human actions are compelled by God. The author begins by noting the peculiar nature of this issue, as people have always differed over it due to conflicting considerations. He then states that the various approaches to the issue are contradictory. The argument is then given: The Jabriyya rely on the principle that every contingent being (mumkin) requires a preponderator (murajjih) to tip the scales towards existence. This principle is considered self-evident (badihiyya). From this, they reason that an agent capable of performing opposites (qadir 'ala al-diddayn) cannot prefer one action over the other without a preponderator. That preponderator cannot come from the agent himself, as that would lead to an infinite regress (tasalsul). Therefore, the preponderator must come from God. Consequently, human action is compelled (jabr) by God's preponderating will. The argument hinges on the necessity of an external preponderator for any contingent action to occur, eliminating human free choice.

Key Terms
الجبرية
المرجح
الممكن
التسلسل
الجبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Jabriyya deny causality altogether.
Correction: They affirm the principle of causality (the contingent needs a preponderator) but attribute the ultimate preponderator to God.

Checkpoint
According to the Jabriyya argument presented, why can an agent capable of opposites not prefer one action over another without a preponderator?
A) Because the agent lacks free will.
B) Because the agent is not capable of acting.
C) Because contingent acts require an external preponderator to occur.
D) Because the agent is himself created.

Key Takeaway
The Jabriyya's argument for determinism relies on the self-evident principle that every contingent requires a preponderator, which they then apply to human action to conclude that God is the preponderator and hence humans are compelled.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Jabriyya argue that without God's preponderating will, you could never choose any action. Do you truly believe that every single decision you make—even the smallest—is directly caused by God? How does that sit with your sense of moral responsibility? Are you willing to let go of the idea that you have any real choice, or does something inside you rebel against that? Examine your innermost conviction: are you actually a Jabri in practice, or do you secretly believe in free will despite this argument?
?
If the Jabriyya's logic is sound, then your faith or disbelief is also compelled by God. Does that comfort you or disturb you? Are you willing to accept that your spiritual state is entirely out of your hands, or does that thought motivate you to strive harder? What does your reaction reveal about your underlying belief in human agency?
?
The passage calls the issue 'strange' because of conflicting reasons. Have you ever felt the tension between God's control and your own choices? Instead of intellectualizing it, how do you actually live with that tension? What would change in your daily life if you fully embraced one side or the other?

The Self-Evident Premises Conflict
Author presents the foundational premises of Jabriyya and Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two self-evident premises—the need for a preponderator and the goodness of praise/blame—appear to conflict in the debate on predestination and free will.

Core Idea
Two self-evident truths cannot genuinely contradict, yet here they seem to.

This lesson dives into the foundational paradox at the heart of the qadar debate. Both the Jabriyya and Qadariyya ground their arguments in premises they consider self-evident. Yet these premises lead to opposite conclusions. How can this be? Let us follow the author's exposition of each side's mainstay.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the author's framing of the issue as 'strange' before presenting the premises.
2
Identify the two self-evident premises
Find the premise of the Jabriyya (the possible requires a preponderator) and the premise of the Qadariyya (praise and blame require free will). Both are claimed to be self-evident.
3
Understand the logical conclusion of each
The Jabriyya conclude determinism; the Qadariyya conclude free will. Note how each side uses its premise to argue its position.
4
Reflect on the apparent contradiction
Ask yourself: If both premises are self-evident, how can they lead to conflicting conclusions? This is the 'strange state' the author highlights.
This motivates the need for deeper investigation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم : أن حال هذه المسألة : حال عجيبة . وذلك لأن الخلق أبداً كانوا مختلفين فيها ، بسبب متدافعة . أن الوجوه التي يمكن الرجوع إليها في هذه المسألة متعارضة . وتقرير ذلك : أن نقول : الجبرية : عولوا في تقرير قولهم على أن الممكن لا بد له من مرجح . وهذه المقدمة مقدمة بديهية . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، فالقادر على الضدين يمتنع أن يرجح أحد الطرفين على الآخر ، لا المرجح . وذلك المرجح ليس منه ، وإلا لزم التسلسل ، بل هو من الله . وحينئذ يلزم الجبر . وأما القدرية : فقد عولوا في تقرير قولهم : على أن حسن المدح والذم معلوم بالبديهة . ونعلم بالبديهة : أنه لو لم يكن العبد قادراً على الفعل لما حسن المدح والذم . وما كان أصلا للبديهي : أولى أن يكون بديهياً . فالحاصل : أن عمدة الجبرية هي أن الممكن لا بد له من مرجح . وعمدة القدرية : هي حسن المدح والذم . وهما مقدمتان معلومتان بالبديهة . فقد وقع التعارض بين هاتين المقدمتين في هذا المقام . وأما الدلائل العقلية : فاعتماد الجبرية على أن هذه التفاصيل ، غير معلومة لنا فلا تكون مخلوقة لنا . واعتماد القدرية على أن هذه الأفعال ، واقعة على وفق مقصودنا ودواعينا . فهي منا . فقد وقع التعارض بين دليل العلم ودليل القصد . وأما الإلزامات العائدة إلى باب الكمال والنقصان . فاعتماد الجبرية على حرف واحد ، وهو أن القدرة على الإيجاد صفة كمال ، فلا يليق بالعبد الذي هو منبع النقصان . واعتماد القدرية على حرف واحد ، وهو أن أفعال العباد سفه وعبث ، وإيجادها نقصان . وذلك لا يليق بالإله المتعالي عن النقصان . وأما الدلائل السمعية . فالقرآن مملوء مما يوهم الجبر تارة ، ومما يوهم القدر أخرى . وأما الأنام . فكذلك جميع الملل والنحل ، بعضهم مجبرة ، وبعضهم قدرية . ولا ترى أمة من الأمم خالية عن هاتين الطائفتين . وأما الأوضاع والحكايات . فهي أيضاً متعارضة في هذا الباب ، حتى قيل : إن واضع النرد وضعه على مذهب الجبر ، وواضع الشطرنج وضعه على مذهب القدر . فبان عندك أن التعارض غالب في هذه المسألة إلا
Know: that the state of this issue is a strange state. That is because people have always been differing in it, due to conflicting [reasons]. The aspects that can be referred to in this issue are contradictory. The explanation of that is that we say: The Jabriyya relied in establishing their statement on the premise that the possible necessarily requires a preponderator. This premise is a self-evident premise. If this is the case, then the one who is capable of two opposites is prevented from giving preponderance to one of the two sides without the preponderator. That preponderator is not from him, otherwise there would be infinite regress, but rather it is from God. Then determinism is necessitated. As for the Qadariyya, they relied in establishing their statement on the fact that the goodness of praise and blame is known by self-evidence. And we know by self-evidence that if the servant were not capable of the act, then praise and blame would not be good. And what is the foundation for the self-evident is more worthy of being self-evident. The upshot: the mainstay of the Jabriyya is that the possible necessarily requires a preponderator, and the mainstay of the Qadariyya is the goodness of praise and blame. Both are self-evident premises. Conflict has occurred between these two premises in this context. As for the rational proofs: the reliance of the Jabriyya is that these details are not known to us, so they are not created by us. And the reliance of the Qadariyya is that these actions occur in accordance with our aim and motives, so they are from us. Conflict has occurred between the proof of knowledge and the proof of intention. As for the objections pertaining to the subject of perfection and deficiency: the reliance of the Jabriyya is on one point, which is that the power to bring into existence is a quality of perfection, so it is not befitting for the servant who is a source of deficiency. And the reliance of the Qadariyya is on one point, which is that the actions of servants are foolishness and frivolity, and their creation is a deficiency, and that is not befitting for the God who is exalted above deficiency. As for the scriptural proofs: the Quran is filled with what suggests determinism at times, and what suggests free will at other times. As for the nations: likewise all religions and sects, some of them are Jabri, some are Qadari. And you do not see any nation free of these two groups. As for the invented games and stories: they too are contradictory in this topic, until it was said: the inventor of backgammon placed it on the doctrine of determinism, and the inventor of chess placed it on the doctrine of free will. So it became clear to you that contradiction is predominant in this issue, except...
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is an introductory exposition of the perplexing nature of the theological issue of predestination (jabr) and free will (qadar). The author begins by stating that the state of this issue is 'strange' because people have always differed over it due to conflicting factors. He then lists the various contradictory aspects.

The first contradiction is between the foundational premises of the Jabriyya (determinists) and the Qadariyya (free-will advocates). The Jabriyya rely on the self-evident principle that every possible thing requires a preponderator (murajjih) to bring it into existence. Since a human agent capable of two opposites cannot cause one to occur without an external preponderator, that preponderator must be God, leading to determinism. The Qadariyya rely on the equally self-evident principle that praise and blame are only meaningful if the agent has genuine choice and ability. If human actions were determined, praise and blame would be unjust. Thus two self-evident premises apparently conflict.

The second contradiction is in rational proofs: the Jabriyya argue that the detailed particularities of actions are unknown to us, so they cannot be created by us; the Qadariyya argue that actions follow our intentions and motives, so they originate from us. Thus the proof from knowledge (daliil al-'ilm) and the proof from intention (daliil al-qasd) conflict.

The third is from considerations of perfection and deficiency: the Jabriyya hold that creative power is a perfection, so it befits God alone, not the deficient servant; the Qadariyya hold that if the servant's actions are created by God, then God would create frivolity and evil, which is a deficiency unbecoming of God.

The fourth is scriptural evidence: the Quran contains verses that suggest determinism and others that suggest free will.

The fifth is the testimony of nations: every religious community has both Jabri and Qadari factions.

The sixth is cultural artifacts: games like backgammon are said to be designed on the deterministic view, while chess on the free-will view.

All these contradictory lines of evidence show that contradiction pervades this issue. The passage ends abruptly with 'except...' indicating a possible exception or resolution to come.

Key Terms
الجبرية
القدرية
المرجح
بديهية
حسن المدح والذم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main self-evident premise that the Jabriyya rely on according to this passage?
A) That the goodness of praise and blame is self-evident.
B) That every possible thing requires a preponderator.
C) That human actions are known to us through intention.
D) That God's perfection prevents Him from creating evil.

Key Takeaway
Two self-evident premises—the need for a preponderator and the goodness of praise/blame—apparently conflict at the heart of the jabr/qadar debate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a difficult situation, do you more often think 'It was God's decree, so I have no choice' or 'I am responsible for how I respond'? Which of these reflects your deeper belief?
?
The lesson presents two self-evident truths that seem to conflict. Is there an area in your life where you sense a similar tension between God's control and your own choices? How do you usually resolve it?
?
If you honestly examine your heart, do you use the idea of divine decree to excuse your sins or to comfort yourself in trials? What would it mean to hold both the need for a preponderator and the goodness of praise and blame together in your daily choices?

Rational Proofs and Perfection Arguments
Author enumerates rational proofs and perfection/deficiency arguments in the jabr/qadar debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how rational arguments (knowledge vs intention) and considerations of perfection/deficiency contribute to the contradictory nature of the jabr/qadar issue.

Core Idea
Reason itself is divided: what we know and what we intend pull in opposite directions.

The author continues his survey of contradictions, now turning to rational arguments and theological attributes. The Jabriyya argue from our ignorance of action details; the Qadariyya argue from our conscious intentions. Similarly, the two schools disagree on whether creative power is a perfection or creating evil is a deficiency. This lesson unpacks these further layers of conflict.

Guided Path
1
Read the rational proofs section
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the proof of knowledge (daliil al-'ilm) and the proof of intention (daliil al-qasd). Notice how each side uses a different aspect of human experience.
2
Understand the perfection/deficiency argument
Read the second part where the author presents the Jabriyya claim that creative power is a perfection (so only for God) and the Qadariyya claim that creating frivolity is a deficiency (so not from God).
3
Identify the common structure
Each side is said to rely on a single 'point' (harf). Notice the parallel structure: both sides appeal to a single, seemingly compelling consideration.
4
Reflect on the cumulative contradiction
Consider that both rational proofs and perfection arguments appear equally strong yet lead to opposite conclusions. The author is building a case for the pervasive contradiction.

Scripture, Nations, and Cultural Testimony
Author lists scriptural, historical, and cultural evidence of contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scriptural, historical, and cultural evidence also reflects the deep division on the issue of predestination and free will.

Core Idea
The divide over free will is not just philosophical—it appears in all human expressions.

The author broadens his scope beyond rational arguments to include revelation, history, and even games. The Quran seems to support both sides, every religious community has both factions, and even backgammon and chess are said to embody the two views. This lesson examines these external testimonies and notes the abrupt ending of the passage.

This premise is a self-evident premise. If this is the case, then the one who is capable of two opposites is prevented from giving preponderance to one of the two sides without the preponderator. That preponderator is not from him, otherwise there would be infinite regress, but rather it is from God. Then determinism is necessitated. As for the Qadariyya, they relied in establishing their statement on the fact that the goodness of praise and blame is known by self-evidence. And we know by self-evidence that if the servant were not capable of the act, then praise and blame would not be good. And what is the foundation for the self-evident is more worthy of being self-evident. The upshot: the mainstay of the Jabriyya is that the possible necessarily requires a preponderator, and the mainstay of the Qadariyya is the goodness of praise and blame. Both are self-evident premises. Conflict has occurred between these two premises in this context. As for the rational proofs: the reliance of the Jabriyya is that these details are not known to us, so they are not created by us. And the reliance of the Qadariyya is that these actions occur in accordance with our aim and motives, so they are from us. Conflict has occurred between the proof of knowledge and the proof of intention. As for the objections pertaining to the subject of perfection and deficiency: the reliance of the Jabriyya is on one point, which is that the power to bring into existence is a quality of perfection, so it is not befitting for the servant who is a source of deficiency. And the reliance of the Qadariyya is on one point, which is that the actions of servants are foolishness and frivolity, and their creation is a deficiency, and that is not befitting for the God who is exalted above deficiency. As for the scriptural proofs: the Quran is filled with what suggests determinism at times, and what suggests free will at other times. As for the nations: likewise all religions and sects, some of them are Jabri, some are Qadari. And you do not see any nation free of these two groups. As for the invented games and stories: they too are contradictory in this topic, until it was said: the inventor of backgammon placed it on the doctrine of determinism, and the inventor of chess placed it on the doctrine of free will. So it became clear to you that contradiction is predominant in this issue, except...
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is an introductory exposition of the perplexing nature of the theological issue of predestination (jabr) and free will (qadar). The author begins by stating that the state of this issue is 'strange' because people have always differed over it due to conflicting factors. He then lists the various contradictory aspects.

The first contradiction is between the foundational premises of the Jabriyya (determinists) and the Qadariyya (free-will advocates). The Jabriyya rely on the self-evident principle that every possible thing requires a preponderator (murajjih) to bring it into existence. Since a human agent capable of two opposites cannot cause one to occur without an external preponderator, that preponderator must be God, leading to determinism. The Qadariyya rely on the equally self-evident principle that praise and blame are only meaningful if the agent has genuine choice and ability. If human actions were determined, praise and blame would be unjust. Thus two self-evident premises apparently conflict.

The second contradiction is in rational proofs: the Jabriyya argue that the detailed particularities of actions are unknown to us, so they cannot be created by us; the Qadariyya argue that actions follow our intentions and motives, so they originate from us. Thus the proof from knowledge (daliil al-'ilm) and the proof from intention (daliil al-qasd) conflict.

The third is from considerations of perfection and deficiency: the Jabriyya hold that creative power is a perfection, so it befits God alone, not the deficient servant; the Qadariyya hold that if the servant's actions are created by God, then God would create frivolity and evil, which is a deficiency unbecoming of God.

The fourth is scriptural evidence: the Quran contains verses that suggest determinism and others that suggest free will.

The fifth is the testimony of nations: every religious community has both Jabri and Qadari factions.

The sixth is cultural artifacts: games like backgammon are said to be designed on the deterministic view, while chess on the free-will view.

All these contradictory lines of evidence show that contradiction pervades this issue. The passage ends abruptly with 'except...' indicating a possible exception or resolution to come.

Key Terms
الجبرية
القدرية
المرجح
بديهية
حسن المدح والذم
دليل العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, what is said about the inventor of backgammon?
A) He placed it on the doctrine of free will.
B) He placed it on the doctrine of determinism.
C) He was a Qadari.
D) He was a Jabri.

Key Takeaway
Scripture, history, and even games testify to the pervasive contradiction in the jabr/qadar debate, leaving the issue unresolved.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own daily life, do you tend to justify failures by saying 'it was written' (jabr) or overburden yourself with 'I should have done better' (qadar)? Which tendency distances you from sincere trust in Allah, and which from taking responsibility? What is the cost of that imbalance in your relationship with Him?
?
The author notes that contradiction shows up even in games like chess and backgammon. If your actions—your habits, speech, and reactions—were examined, would they lean more toward a passive acceptance of fate or an anxious striving for control? How does that hidden assumption affect the way you pray, repent, or plan for the future?
?
The passage cuts off with 'except...'—an unfinished hint at a resolution. What might that exception be for you? Are you willing to seek that resolution through deeper study and sincere worship, or are you comfortable remaining in the contradiction? What would change if you truly believed that Allah's decree and human choice are not ultimately conflicting?
